Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Bibliographical Canon: Key Texts Referenced in al-Lubab
Listing and defining key Hanafi fiqh works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi fiqh texts and classify them by type (matn, sharh, hashiyah), author's era, and role in the school's hierarchy.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school's authority is built on a hierarchy of texts, from matn to hashiyah, each serving a distinct role in transmission and fatwa.

Hanafi fiqh is not a single text but a rich tradition of commentaries and super-commentaries. This lesson introduces the key works listed in al-Lubab, helping you navigate the school's textual heritage. You will learn to distinguish foundational matns like Mukhtasar al-Quduri from authoritative fatwa references like Radd al-Muhtar, and recognize the significance of each work in the chain of transmission.

Guided Path
1
Identify the type of work
For each entry, determine whether it is a matn (basic text), sharh (commentary), hashiyah (gloss), or specialized work (e.g., fara'id, hadith). This tells you its place in the teaching tradition.
Matns are concise; sharhs expand; hashiyahs critique and update.
2
Assess the author's era and authority
Note the death date (AH) and scholarly reputation. Earlier scholars closer to the founders carry higher textual authority, but later works like Radd al-Muhtar consolidate and are relied upon for fatwa.
e.g., Ibn 'Abidin (d. 1252 AH) is a late authority; his work is a primary fatwa source.
3
Recognize the text's role in practice
Work through the list and classify each book by its practical function: basic manual (Mukhtasar al-Quduri), intermediary commentary (Zad al-Fuqaha'), fatwa reference (Radd al-Muhtar), or specialized field (al-Sirajiyyah for inheritance).
This helps you know which text to consult for a given need.

Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographical section from al-Lubab, listing key works referenced in the commentary. It serves as a reference guide for students to identify the most important Hanafi fiqh texts and their authors. The list includes major commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri (such as Zad al-Fuqaha', al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and al-Mujtaba), works on inheritance law (al-Sirajiyyah), hadith collections (Sunan al-Tirmidhi, Sunan al-Nasa'i), and Hanafi legal manuals (al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir). The author provides publication status (printed or manuscript) and occasional cross-references. Notably, Ibn 'Abidin's Radd al-Muhtar is a foundational fatwa reference, and al-Sirajiyyah is a standard text on fara'id (inheritance). The mention of Kashf al-Zunun indicates reliance on lexicographical sources for dating. This list reflects the depth of the Hanafi tradition and the interconnectedness of its core texts.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely used as a basic manual for Hanafi law.
رد المحتار على الدر المختار (Radd al-Muhtar 'ala al-Durr al-Mukhtar): A comprehensive commentary (hashiyah) by Ibn 'Abidin on al-Durr al-Mukhtar of al-Haskafi, relying on al-Tanwir and other works. It is a primary reference for fatwa in the late Hanafi school.
السراجية في الفرائض (al-Sirajiyyah fi al-Fara'id): A celebrated Hanafi text on inheritance law by al-Sajawandi, widely studied and taught. Often the first text in Hanafi fara'id.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which book is a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Isbijabi?
A) Radd al-Muhtar
B) Zad al-Fuqaha'
C) al-Siraj al-Wahhaj
D) al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah

Key Takeaway
Knowing the hierarchy of Hanafi texts—from matn to hashiyah—is essential for proper fatwa practice and avoiding reliance on superseded rulings.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating Hanafi Commentary Bibliographies: The Role of Sharh and Mukhtasar
Bibliographic list of Hanafi fiqh commentaries.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a Hanafi commentary bibliographic entry (base text, commentator, death date, status) and differentiate between a matn and its sharh.

Core Idea
Hanafi fiqh is built on matn-sharh chains; knowing these works is essential for tracing authority.

This passage from Al-Lubab lists dozens of commentaries on major Hanafi works. It is not a fiqh ruling but a map of the scholarly tradition. Understanding this list will help you locate authoritative references and avoid confusing a commentary with its base text. Here, we will learn to read such entries quickly.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base text
Each entry typically mentions the original work being commented on, e.g. 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri' or 'al-Jami' al-Saghir'. Look for phrases like 'شرح مختصر القدوري' or 'شرح الجامع'.
The base text is the matn.
2
Identify the commentator
After 'شرح' or 'على', the name of the commentator is given. Note his full name and death date (هـ).
Death date helps locate the work historically.
3
Determine the status
Look for (خ) for manuscript or (ط) for printed. This tells you whether the work is easily accessible.
(خ) = مخطوط, (ط) = مطبوع.
4
Note any additional details
Some entries include multiple commentaries, e.g., 'وله أكثر من شرح', or glosses (حاشية). Note these for further research.
Glosses often respond to the sharh.

Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography section from Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, listing and briefly describing numerous commentaries on key Hanafi fiqh texts. The author provides the title of each commentary, its author, death date, and often whether it exists in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). This serves as a valuable reference for students and researchers to identify authoritative works in the Hanafi tradition. The entries cover commentaries on foundational works such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, Al-Jami' al-Saghir, Al-Hidayah, Kanz al-Daqa'iq, and Multaqa al-Abhar, among others. The passage emphasizes the richness of the Hanafi scholarly tradition and the extensive glossarial literature that developed around its core texts.

Key Terms
شرح (sharh): A commentary or exposition on a base text (matn).
مختصر (mukhtasar): An abridgment or concise legal manual.
خ (kha'): Abbreviation for مخطوط (manuscript), indicating the work exists only in handwritten form.
ط (ta'): Abbreviation for مطبوع (printed), indicating the work has been published.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who authored the commentary known as 'Imdad al-Fattah'?
A) Al-Shurunbulali
B) Ibn Nujaym
C) Al-Haskafi
D) Ibn Abidin

Key Takeaway
Hanafi fiqh is transmitted through a layered tradition of matn and sharh; knowing these commentaries is essential for proper legal attribution.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
A Guide to Hanafi Texts and Commentaries in Al-Lubab
Author lists key Hanafi texts and commentaries

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi fiqh texts and their commentaries as listed in Al-Lubab, and explain the significance of author, death date, and manuscript/print status.

Core Idea
Knowing the authoritative Hanafi texts and their commentaries is essential for navigating the school's tradition.

This chapter from Al-Lubab provides a valuable map of the Hanafi fiqh textual landscape. It lists not only primary works but also the commentaries that have shaped the school's transmission. Understanding this bibliography helps you situate any ruling within its textual lineage.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry type
Determine whether each entry is a base text (matn), a commentary (sharh), a gloss (hashiyah), or a supercommentary. Note how they relate to each other.
Base texts are often concise summaries; commentaries expand on them.
2
Note the author and death date
For each work, note the author's full name and death year. This helps establish the historical layer and reliability of the text.
Death dates are given in Hijri; earlier authors are generally more authoritative.
3
Check the source type
Look for (خ) indicating manuscript and (ط) indicating print. This informs accessibility and textual stability.
Printed works (ط) are more widespread and standardised.
4
Understand the textual relationship
Trace the chain: base text → commentary → gloss. For example, al-Hadiqah al-Nadiyyah is a commentary on al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah.
This hierarchy is crucial for understanding the provenance of rulings.
5
Recognize canonical texts
Identify which works are foundational in the Hanafi curriculum, such as Mukhtasar al-Quduri, al-Hidayah, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq.
These texts are the backbone of Hanafi fiqh study.

Commentary
This chapter from Al-Lubab serves as a bibliography of key Hanafi fiqh texts and their commentaries referenced throughout the work. The author lists works by title, author, death date, and the type of source (manuscript 'خ' or printed 'ط'). Notable entries include: Sharh al-Tariqah al-Muhammadiyyah with its commentary al-Hadiqah al-Nadiyyah by al-Nabulsi, Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Sabbaghi, and commentaries on al-Majma', al-Kanz, al-Multaqa, and al-Manẓumah. The list also includes well-known hadith collections (Sahih al-Bukhari and Muslim) and linguistic works (al-Sihah). This section helps students identify authoritative texts and their scholarly lineage.

Key Terms
شرح (sharḥ): A commentary explaining a base text (matn).
مختصر (mukhtaṣar): A concise summary of a larger work, often used as a textbook.
حاشية (ḥāshiyah): A gloss or marginal commentary on a sharh or matn.
منظومة (manẓūmah): A versified text, often summarizing fiqh rules in poetic form for memorization.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Hanafi Bibliography in Al-Lubab
Bibliographic list of works cited in Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author and work from a bibliographic entry in a classical Hanafi fiqh text.

Core Idea
A bibliographic entry records the relative authority and genre of a work.

This passage from Al-Lubab lists sources the author cites. Learning to read these references helps you locate primary Hanafi authorities and understand the hierarchy of texts used in the commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry number and title
Each entry begins with a number and the title of the work (e.g., '٧٩- شرح المنظومة'). The title may include 'شرح' (commentary), 'حاشية' (gloss), or the base text name.
The numbering is sequential from a previous chapter; some entries may have typographical errors (e.g., '٣' for '٨٣').
2
Note the author's name and death date
The author is named after the title, often with his full name and death year in Hilal (e.g., 'للزوزني السديدي محمد بن محمود'). The death date helps place the work chronologically.
Death dates are in AH; cross-reference with biographical works if needed.
3
Check for additional notes on status or genre
Entries may include 'ط' (printed) or 'خ' (manuscript), and sometimes a brief description of the work's content (e.g., 'في اللغة' for a language work). This indicates availability and scope.
'ط' means the work has been published; 'خ' means it survives only in manuscript.
4
Recognize the genre: commentary, gloss, independent work
Distinguish between a base text (e.g., 'منظومة النسفي'), a commentary (e.g., 'شرح المنظومة'), a gloss (e.g., 'الشرنبلالية'), or a primary source (e.g., 'صحيح البخاري'). This affects the level of authority in citation.
Glosses (ḥawāshī) are secondary; they refine or critique the commentary.

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography (front matter) from the book Al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, listing works referenced in the commentary. The author provides brief identifications: book title, author, death date, and sometimes notes on publication status ('printed' or 'manuscript'). The list is numbered from 79 to 94, and includes a variety of genres: commentaries on legal works (e.g., Sharh al-Manẓūmah, Sharḥ al-Hidāyah), language works (al-Ṣiḥāḥ, al-‘Ubāb al-Zākhir), hadith collections (Ṣaḥīḥ al-Bukhārī, Ṣaḥīḥ Muslim), and glosses (al-Shurunbulāliyyah). The numbering appears to be consecutive from an earlier chapter, and a minor error (entry 83 written as 3) is noted. This material is intended for reference, helping students identify sources cited in the main text.

Key Terms
منظومة النسفي (Manẓūmat al-Nasafī): A poetic text on Hanafi fiqh by Muḥammad ibn Aḥmad al-Nasafī (d. 537 AH).
الشرنبلالية (al-Shurunbulāliyyah): A gloss (ḥāshiyah) by Ḥasan al-Shurunbulālī (d. 1069 AH) on the commentary Durar al-Ḥukkām fī Sharḥ Ghurar al-Aḥkām.
العناية شرح الهداية (al-‘Ināyah Sharḥ al-Hidāyah): A commentary on al-Hidāyah by Akmal al-Dīn al-Bābarītī (d. 786 AH), a key Hanafi fiqh work.

Navigating the Sources: Hanafi Works in Al-Lubab
Bibliography of Hanafi works cited in Al-Lubab

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to classify a referenced Hanafi work as a matn, sharh, or fatawa collection and state its relative authority in the madhhab.

Core Idea
The references in Al-Lubab reveal the layered structure of Hanafi scholarship: matn, sharh, fatawa.

When studying a Hanafi fiqh commentary like Al-Lubab, the list of cited works is not a mere appendix — it is a map of the madhhab's intellectual genealogy. This lesson unpacks that map, teaching you to recognize the types of sources and their place in the Hanafi canon.

Guided Path
1
Identify categories
Scan the list and identify the two main categories of works: sharh (commentaries) and fatawa (responsa). Look for words like 'شرح' and 'فتاوى'.
Also note works like dictionaries (القاموس المحيط) and reference works (هدية العارفين).
2
Note chronological spread
Observe the death dates of the authors, ranging from the 6th to 10th centuries AH. This shows the development of Hanafi literature over time.
3
Distinguish manuscript vs. print
Many entries are marked with (خ) for manuscript and (ط) for print. Consider what this implies about the work's accessibility and authority in the tradition.
Manuscripts may be rare or unedited; print indicates wider dissemination.
4
Identify reference citations
Notice how many entries cite Hadiyyat al-'Arifin. This biographical encyclopedia is a key tool for verifying authorship and titles in Hanafi studies.

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter bibliography from Al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, listing the works cited in the commentary. The author, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Ghunaymi al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH?), provides brief identifications of each book, its author, death date, and whether it exists in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). The list includes major Hanafi texts like Ghayat al-Bayan wa Nadirat al-Aqran, Fatawa Qadi Khan, and Fath al-Qadir. Many entries reference Hadiyyat al-'Arifin for identity confirmation. This section is not a legal ruling but a scholarly apparatus for the reader to understand the sources used in the main text.

Key Terms
فتاوى (fatāwā): Legal responsa; collections of rulings by a Hanafi jurist addressing specific questions.
شرح (sharḥ): Commentary; a work that explains and expands upon a base text (matn).
هدية العارفين (Hadiyyat al-ʿĀrifīn): A biographical encyclopedia of authors and their works by Isma'il Pasha al-Baghdadi.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Qadi Khan, 592 AH
D) Al-Kaki, 749 AH

Key Takeaway
The bibliography of Al-Lubab is a window into the Hanafi literary tradition, illustrating the relationship between matn, sharh, and fatawa.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Bibliography of al-Lubab
Bibliographic index of Hanafi works

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify key Hanafi reference works and interpret bibliographic abbreviations (khā/ṭā) used in classical indexes.

Core Idea
The Hanafi madhhab is built on a chain of authoritative texts—knowing these sources is foundational.

This lesson explores the bibliography from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. While it may appear as a simple list, it reveals the rich network of sources that underpin Hanafi fiqh. Learning to read these entries equips you to trace the lineage of rulings and assess the reliability of texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the entry format
Each entry has a number, title, author, death date, and status (manuscript or printed). Note the use of parentheses for death dates and abbreviations.
Example: '100- فتاوى العتابي ... ت ٥٨٦هـ، (خ)' – death date 586, manuscript.
2
Classify the type of work
Determine if the work is a fatwa collection (فتاوى), a commentary (شرح), a fiqh encyclopedia (مبسوط), or a lexical work (قاموس). This tells you its genre.
e.g., 'فتاوى' = fatwas, 'شرح' = commentary, 'مبسوط' = comprehensive fiqh.
3
Analyze the author's significance
Look at the author's full name and death date. Compare with other authors to see the chronological development: earlier authors (e.g., al-Hakim al-Shahid d.334) vs. later (e.g., al-Maydani d.1222).
Death dates help situate the work in the evolution of Hanafi fiqh.
4
Interpret abbreviations and symbols
Recognize that (خ) means manuscript and (ط) means printed. Also note ‘لعلها’ (probably) indicates uncertainty, which warns you to verify the identification.
These symbols are standard in Islamic bibliographies.
5
Reflect on the purpose of the list
Understand that al-Maydani includes these references to show the sources he used. This serves as a scholarly apparatus, allowing readers to consult original texts.
The list is not a curriculum but a finding aid.

Commentary
This is a front matter section from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri. The author, al-Maydani, provides a bibliographic index of works cited or relevant to the commentary. The list includes fatwa collections, commentaries on al-Hidayah, and other Hanafi fiqh sources. Each entry gives the author's full name, death date, and whether the work is in manuscript (خ) or printed (ط). Many entries are major Hanafi references such as al-Mabsut by al-Sarakhsi, Fath al-Qadir, and Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The list illustrates the depth of sources used in the Hanafi tradition. The occasional 'لعلها' or 'لعله' indicates uncertainty about identification.

Key Terms
خ (khā): Abbreviation for manuscript (مخطوط).
ط (ṭā): Abbreviation for printed (مطبوع).
ت (t): Abbreviation for death date (تاريخ الوفاة).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating the Bibliography of al-Lubab: Key Hanafi Sources
List of referenced books with author and publication status

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi fiqh works cited in al-Lubab, classify them by type (matn, sharh, fatwa, usul), and distinguish printed versus manuscript sources.

Core Idea
A scholar's library is his arsenal: knowing which books are printed and which are manuscripts saves years of research.

This lesson introduces the bibliography from al-Lubab, a foundational Hanafi commentary. The list includes essential works of fiqh, usul, and fatwa, each marked as printed (ط) or manuscript (خ). Understanding this list gives you a roadmap to the sources that shaped Hanafi jurisprudence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work type
For each entry, determine whether it is a matn (text), sharh (commentary), fatwa collection, usul work, or other. Note that some titles indicate their genre, e.g., 'Sharh' or 'Mukhtasar'.
For example, 'الكفاية شرح الهداية' is a commentary; 'كنز الدقائق' is a matn.
2
Locate the author and his era
Each entry gives the author's full name and death date. Note the century to situate the work within the development of the Hanafi school.
Death dates range from 3rd to 10th century Hijri, showing a rich scholarly tradition.
3
Check the publication status
The abbreviations ط (printed) and خ (manuscript) indicate availability. Prioritize printed works for research, but be aware that some essential texts remain in manuscript.
Many works are printed, but key references like 'المحيط' and 'المختارات' are still manuscripts.
4
Note cross-references and variants
Some entries clarify relationships (e.g., 'المجتبى - شرح الزاهدي على مختصر القدوري') or mention multiple works with the same title. Understand which specific work is intended.
For 'المحيط', three different works are listed; careful attribution is needed.
5
Build a mental map of sources
Group related works: early matns (e.g., 'الكافي', 'مختصر القدوري'), later commentaries ('الهداية', 'اللُباب'), and fatwa collections ('المختار', 'مجمع الفتاوى'). This helps you navigate from early to later authority.
Al-Lubab itself is a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.

١١٨ - المجمع، لعله غالباً مجمع البحرين، لمظفر الدين بن الساعاتي أحمد بن علي، ت ٧٤٩هـ، (ط).
۱۱۹ - مجمع الفتاوى، لأحمد بن محمد بن أبي بكر، ت ٥٢٢ هـ، (خ)، كشف الظنون ١٦٠٣/٢، الأعلام ٢١٥/١.
١٢٠ - المحيط، لمحمد بن محمد بن محمد رضي الدين برهان الإسلام السرخسي، ت ٥٧١ هـ، (خ)، وهناك أكثر من محيط. وأيضاً هناك المحيط، لبرهان الدين محمود بن تاج الدين أحمد ابن الصدر الشهيد برهان الأئمة عبد العزيز بن عمر بن مازن البخاري، ت ٦١٦هـ، وهو ابن أخي الصدر الشهيد حسام الدين، (ط). وهناك محيط السرخسي، لشمس الأئمة محمد بن أحمد، ت ٤٨٣هـ، (خ).
١٢١ - المختار في الفتوى للموصلي عبد الله بن محمود، ت ٦٨٣هـ، ولمؤلفه شرح عليه سماه: الاختيار، (ط).
۱۲۲ - المختارات للفتوى لعلاء الدين علي بن أحمد الجمالي، ت ٩٣٢هـ، (خ).
۱۲۳- مختارات النوازل (مختارات مجموع النوازل)، لعلي بن أبي بكر بن عبد الجليل المرغيناني صاحب الهداية، ت ٥٩٣هـ، (خ).
١٢٤ - مختصر الحاكم (الكافي)، للحاكم الشهيد محمد بن أحمد، ت ٣٣٤هـ، (خ).
١٢٥ - المراسيل، لأبي داود السجستاني سليمان بن الأشعث، ت ٢٧٥هـ، (ط).
١٢٦ - المستصفى شرح منظومة النسفي في الخلاف للنسفي أبي حفص عمر بن محمد، ت ٥٣٧هـ، للنسفي أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد، ت ٧١٠هـ، (خ).

Source pages p. 275

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section: a bibliography of the principal works cited in the commentary al-Lubab. The author provides for each book its title, author with full name and death date (in Hijri), and marks whether it is available in printed form (ط) or only in manuscript (خ). This list is essential for the student to identify the sources of the rulings and arguments presented in the main text. The entries cover a wide range of Hanafi fiqh and usul works, including commentaries, fatwa collections, and manuals. Note the variation in some dates and authorship (e.g., multiple works titled al-Muhit). The entry for al-Mujtaba appears without a number, inserted between lines. This bibliography reflects the depth of the Hanafi tradition and the scholarly network from which al-Lubab draws.

Key Terms
ط (ta'): Abbreviation for مطبوع (printed), indicating the book is available in print.
خ (kha'): Abbreviation for مخطوط (manuscript), indicating the book exists only in manuscript form.
ت (t): Abbreviation for سنة الوفاة (year of death), followed by the Hijri year.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
This bibliography is a vital tool for navigating the Hanafi scholarly tradition: it shows which works are foundational, which are available in print, and how they relate to each other.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Navigating Hanafi Bibliographies
Bibliographic list of Hanafi fiqh works with authors and death dates.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key elements in a Hanafi bibliographic entry (author, death date, print/manuscript status) and explain the purpose of such lists in a commentary.

Core Idea
A bibliography in a Hanafi commentary identifies the sources used, their authors, and their reliability.

This lesson introduces you to the bibliographic chapter of Al-Lubab, which lists the works cited in the commentary. Understanding this list helps you trace the sources of Hanafi rulings and evaluate their authority. You will learn to read entries with author names, death dates, and notations for print or manuscript status.

Guided Path
1
Identify the work title and author
Each entry typically begins with the work title (e.g., 'المشكلات شرح مختصر القدوري') followed by the author's name. Note the author's full name and any honorifics.
Author names may include lineage and nisbah.
2
Note the death date and its significance
Death dates (e.g., ت٥٥٢هـ) are given to situate the author chronologically. This helps assess the work's historical context and authority in the Hanafi tradition.
Earlier authors generally carry more weight in the school.
3
Distinguish manuscript (خ) from printed (ط)
Entries may include (خ) for manuscript (khatti) or (ط) for printed (taba'a). This indicates availability and reliability of the source.
A manuscript (خ) may be less accessible; a printed (ط) work is more widespread.
4
Observe uncertainties (?) and what they indicate
Question marks after titles (e.g., 'المقاييس ؟') show scholarly caution: the author is unsure of the exact reference. This reflects the critical nature of early bibliography.
Such uncertainties remind us that not all attributions are definitive.

الفصل الرابع: تعريف موجز بالكتب المذكورة في اللباب

١٢٧ - المشكلات شرح مختصر القدوري، لأبي بكر علاء الدين بن أحمد السمرقندي، ت٥٥٢هـ، (خ). وقيل : لأبي الليث نصر بن محمد بن إبراهيم السمرقندي، ت ٣٧٥هـ، ينظر كشف الظنون ١٦٣٤/٢ .
١٢٨ - المصباح المنير في غريب الشرح الكبير ، للفيومي أحمد بن محمد، ت ۷۷۰هـ ، (ط).
١٢٩ - المصفى مختصر المستصفى للنسفي - المستصفى.
١٣٠ - المطالب المستطابة في الحيض والنفاس والاستحاضة لعبد الغني الغنيمي الميداني، ت ۱۲۹۸هـ، (خ).
١٣١ - معراج الدراية إلى شرح الهداية، للكاكي قوام الدين محمد بن محمد بن أحمد البخاري، ت ٧٤٩هـ، (خ).
١٣٢ - المغرب في ترتيب المعرب ، للمطرزي ناصر الدين بن عبد السيد أبي الفتح، ت ٦١٠هـ، (ط).
١٣٣ - (المغني)، لعله أراد المغني في أصول الفقه للخبازي عمر بن محمد، ت ٦٧١هـ، (ط).
١٣٤ - المقاييس ؟ لعله مقاييس اللغة لابن فارس أحمد بن فارس بن زكريا الرازي المالكي، ت ٣٩٥هـ، (ط)، لكن النص المنقول في اللباب لم أجده في مقاييس اللغة لابن فارس.
١٣٥ - مقدمة أبي الليث (مقدمة الصلاة)، أو (مقدمة في الفقه)، لأبي الليث نصر بن محمد السمرقندي، ت ٣٧٥هـ، (ط).
١٣٦ - الملتقط في الفتاوى، لأبي القاسم بن يوسف السمرقندي، ت ٥٥٦هـ ، (ط).
١٣٧ - الملتقى، لعله أراد : (ملتقى الأبحر)، للحلبي إبراهيم بن محمد ، ت ٩٥٦ هـ ، (ط). وهناك: «ملتقى البحار من منتقى الأخبار»، للزوزني السديدي محمد بن محمود، شرح منظومة النسفي. وهناك : «ملتقى البحرين، المصنفك ت ٨٧٥هـ، كشف الظنون .١٨١٦/٢
١٣٨ - المنافع، في شرح النافع للنسفي أبي البركات عبد الله بن أحمد، ت ۷۱٠هـ، (خ)، و«النافع في فروع الحنفية»، أو (الفقـه النافع)، لأبي القاسم بن يوسف الحسيني السمرقندي، ت٦٥٦هـ، (خ)، تاج التراجم ص .۳۳۹ ، ۱۷۵.
١٣٩ - منح (الغفار شرح تنوير الأبصار)، كلاهما للتمرتاشي محمد بن عبد الله ، ت ١٠٠٤هـ، (خ).
١٤٠ - المنصورية ؟
١٤١ - (المنية) منية المصلي وغنية المبتدي، للكاشغري سديد الدین محمد بن محمد، ت ٧٠٥هـ، (ط).
١٤٢ - منية المفتي في فروع الحنفية، ليوسف بن أبي سعيد بـن أحمد السجستاني، المتوفى سنة ٦٦٦هـ ، وقيل ٦٣٨هـ، ينظر حاشية لمخطوطة من تاج التراجم . ٣١٩ من المطبوع، وينظر هدية العارفين ٥٥٤/٢ ، وسماه الجستاني، كشف الظنون ۱۸۸۷/۲.
١٤٣ - المواهب (مواهب الرحمن في مذهب النعمان)، لإبراهيم

Source pages p. 277

Commentary
This passage is the fourth chapter of the book, which provides brief definitions of the works cited in Al-Lubab. It is a bibliographic list identifying key Hanafi texts and their authors. The author notes death dates (tārikh wafāt) and indicates whether the work is available in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). Some entries include clarifications or alternative ascriptions, such as for Al-Mushkilat (attributed to both al-Samarqandi and Abu al-Layth). The list covers a wide range of fiqh and usul works, including commentaries on Al-Quduri, Al-Hidayah, and Al-Nasafi, as well as specialized treatises on menstruation (Al-Matalib al-Mustataba) and prayer (Munyat al-Musalli). The author also notes uncertainties, e.g., 'Al-Maqayis?' and 'Al-Mansuriyya?', showing scholarly caution. This front matter helps readers identify the sources used in the commentary and their reliability within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
اللباب (al-Lubāb): The title of the commentary (Sharh al-Quduri) by al-Maydani, which explains the Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Qudūrī): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied as a primer.
خ (khā'): Abbreviation for 'khaṭṭī' meaning manuscript.
ط (tā'): Abbreviation for 'taba'a' meaning printed.

Key Takeaway
The bibliographic list in Al-Lubab is a guide to the sources of the commentary, essential for understanding the Hanafi textual tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Hanafi Textual Canon: Works Cited in al-Lubab
Bibliography of Hanafi works with author death dates

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major Hanafi works categorized by author era and textual authority (zahir al-riwayah vs. later commentaries).

Core Idea
The Hanafi school relies on a hierarchy of primary texts, commentaries, and fatwa collections.

This chapter from al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri lists the key Hanafi works referenced by the author, al-Maydani. Understanding this bibliography is essential for navigating the Hanafi textual tradition: it shows how foundational works like al-Nawadir and al-Hidayah relate to later commentaries and abridgments. By studying this list, you will learn to distinguish between primary and secondary sources, and appreciate the chain of authority in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Scan the list and categorize by era
The entries span from the 2nd to 11th centuries AH. Group them into early (d. before 400 AH), middle (400-700 AH), and later (after 700 AH). This reveals the historical development of the Hanafi school.
For example, al-Nawadir (d. 189 AH) is early; al-Hidayah (d. 593 AH) is middle; Nur al-Idah (d. 1069 AH) is later.
2
Identify works of the Zahir al-Riwayah
Look for works by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (e.g., al-Nawadir) and others that form the core six books. These have the highest authority in the school.
al-Nawadir is not part of the six core books (which are al-Mabsut, al-Jami' al-Saghir, etc.), but it is a key collection of rare narrations.
3
Distinguish between matn, sharh, and mukhtasar
Note which works are original texts (matn), commentaries (sharh), or abridgments (mukhtasar). For instance, al-Hidayah is a sharh on Bidayah al-Mubtadi; al-Nuqayah is a mukhtasar of al-Wiqayah.
This hierarchy helps you trace how rulings were transmitted and refined.
4
Note the status: manuscript (خ) vs. print (ط)
The author indicates whether each work was available in manuscript (مخطوط) or print (مطبوع). This reflects the accessibility and diffusion of the text at the time of writing al-Lubab.
For example, al-Nawadir is marked (خ) meaning it existed in manuscript; al-Hidayah is (ط) meaning it was printed.
5
Recognize the significance of al-Hidayah
Al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani appears prominently (entry 153). It is one of the most authoritative Hanafi commentaries and a central text for fatwa. Notice also that it has its own commentaries (e.g., al-Nihayah by al-Sighnaqi).
Many later works in the list are either commentaries on or abridgments of al-Hidayah.

الفصل الرابع : تعريف موجز بالكتب المذكورة في اللباب
ابن موسى الطرابلسي، ت ٩٢٢هـ، (خ).
١٤٤ - النافع، أو الفقه النافع)، لأبي القاسم بن يوسف الحسيني السمرقندي، ت ٦٥٦هـ، (ط).
١٤٥ - التتف (في الفتاوى)، للسغدي علي بن الحسين، ٤٦١ هـ، (ط).
١٤٦ - نصاب الفقهاء في الفتاوى لأبي المعالي برهان الدين محمود بن أحمد بن عبد العزيز صاحب: «تتمة الفتاوى»، و«المحيط»، ت ٦١٦هـ. (خ) ، ينظر كشف الظنون ٣٤٤٣٤٣/١، تاج التراجم ص۲۸۸.
١٤٧ - نظم الخلافيات للنسفي نجم الدين عمر ، ت٥٣٧هـ (ط).
١٤٨ - النقاية مختصر الوقاية لصدر الشريعة عبيد الله بن مسعود، ت ٧٤٥هـ ، (ط).
١٤٩ - النهاية شرح الهداية، للسغناقي الحسين بن علي، ت ۷۱۰هـ، (خ).
١٥٠ - النهر الفائق شرح كنز الدقائق لابن نجيم عمر بن إبراهيم، ت ١٠٠٥هـ، (ط).
١٥١ - النوادر، لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، ت ١٨٩هـ، (خ)، له عدة روايات منها لابن سماعة ، ت ٢٣٣هـ، ومنها لهشام بن عبيد الله الرازي، ت ٢٢١هـ، ومنها لابن رُستُم إبراهيم، ت ٢١١هـ.
١٥٢ - نور الإيضاح للشرنبلالي حسن بن عمار، ت ١٠٦٩هـ، (ط).
١٥٣ - الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي للمرغيناني علي بن أبي بكر، ت ٥٩٣هـ، (ط).
١٥٤ - الواقعات، للصدر الشهيد حسام الدين عمر بن عبد العزيز ابن مازه، ت ٥٣٦هـ، (خ).
١٥٥ - الواقعات، للناطفي أحمد بن محمد، ت ٤٤٦هـ، (خ).
١٥٦ - الوقاية ( مختصر الهداية، لتاج الشريعة المحبوبي محمود ابن عبيد الله ، ت في السابع الهجري، ينظر الفوائد البهية ص ١٠٩ ، وما حرره في اسمه واسم جده.
١٥٧ - الوَلْوَالجية (الفتاوى الولوالجية، ظهير الدين عبد الرشيد ابن أبي حنيفة نعمان بن عبد الرزاق بن عبد الله الولوالجي القاضي، و(لَوَالِج) : من أعمال بدخشان في بخارى، ت ٥٤٠ هـ، (ط). هدية العارفين ٥٦٨/٥. لكن في تاج التراجم ص ۱۲۹ هكذا : « إسحاق الولوالجي، لـه الفتاوى المشهورة. اهـ، وفي كشف الظنون ۱۲۳۰/۲: «فتاویٰ الولوالجي لظهير الدين أبي المكارم إسحاق بن أبي بكر الحنفي، ت : ۷۱۰ هـ ». اهـ
١٥٨ - الينابيع في معرفة الأصول والتفاريع، شرح مختصر القدوري، لرشيد الدين محمود (محمد) بن رمضان الشبلي الرومي، فرغ من منه سنة ٦١٦هـ، (خ). هدية العارفين ١٦٤/٢.
Chapter Four: A Brief Introduction to the Books Mentioned in al-Lubab

156 - al-Wiqayah (an abridgment of al-Hidayah), by Taj al-Shari‘ah al-Mahbubi Mahmud ibn ‘Ubayd Allah, d. in the seventh century AH, see al-Fawa’id al-Bahiyyah p. 109, and what was edited regarding his name and his grandfather’s name.
157 - al-Walwaljiyyah (al-Fatawa al-Walwaljiyyah), by Zahir al-Din ‘Abd al-Rashid ibn Abi Hanifah Nu‘man ibn ‘Abd al-Razzaq ibn ‘Abd Allah al-Walwalji al-Qadi, and Walwalj: a district of Badakhshan in Bukhara, d. 540 AH, (print). Hadiyyat al-‘Arifin 5/568. But in Taj al-Tarajim p. 129 it is: 'Ishaq al-Walwalji, he has the famous fatwas. End.' Source pages p. 279

Commentary
This passage is a bibliography from the book 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri' by al-Maydani. The author lists many important Hanafi works that he references in his commentary. The entries are numbered from 144 to 158, and each includes the book title, author, death date, and often whether it exists in manuscript (خ) or print (ط). Some entries have additional notes about different narrations or sources. This list serves as a guide for readers to the sources used in al-Lubab. Among the key works are 'al-Nawadir' by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, which is a foundational collection of rare transmissions, 'al-Hidayah' by al-Marghinani, a major Hanafi commentary, and 'Nur al-Idah' by al-Shurunbulali, a later primer. The list also includes works by later scholars like Ibn Nujaym and al-Shurunbulali, showing the range of sources from the founding period to the later Ottoman era. The author notes discrepancies in some sources, such as the multiple attributions for 'al-Walwaljiyyah'. This chapter is a valuable resource for understanding the Hanafi textual tradition and the authorities behind the rulings in al-Lubab.

Key Terms
النوادر (al-Nawadir): A work by Muhammad al-Shaybani containing rare or non-standard narrations within the Hanafi school.
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A comprehensive commentary on 'Bidayah al-Mubtadi' by al-Marghinani, one of the most authoritative Hanafi texts.
نور الإيضاح (Nur al-Idah): A later Hanafi primer on fiqh by al-Shurunbulali, widely used in Ottoman-era education.
النهاية شرح الهداية (al-Nihayah Sharh al-Hidayah): A commentary on al-Hidayah by al-Sighnaqi, used for further elaboration.
النهر الفائق (al-Nahr al-Fa'iq): A commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq by Ibn Nujaym, an important Ottoman-era Hanafi text.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
The bibliography in al-Lubab maps the Hanafi textual tradition from early foundational works to later commentaries, crucial for understanding the authority of each source.

Introduction to Imam al-Quduri and His Mukhtasar
Introducing the second chapter on Imam al-Quduri and his work

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify Imam al-Quduri and explain the structure of the second chapter of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Knowing the author and the text is essential for understanding the Hanafi fiqh tradition.

This lesson introduces the second chapter of al-Lubab, which is dedicated to the study of Imam al-Quduri and his famous Mukhtasar. Although this is not a ruling passage, it contextualizes the commentary you are about to study. Recognizing the authority of the author and the status of the text is a prerequisite for engaging with the fiqh rulings that follow.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the chapter
The second chapter is an introductory study of the author and the text. It is not part of the original Mukhtasar but added by the commentator to provide background.
This is a common feature in sharh works: they often begin with a biography and textual analysis.
2
List the three sections
The chapter is divided into three parts: (1) Biography of Imam al-Quduri, (2) Study of the Mukhtasar, (3) Commentaries and scholarly works based on the Mukhtasar.
Each section builds on the previous, from the person to the book to its reception.
3
Understand the significance of each section
The biography establishes the authority of the author; the study of the Mukhtasar explains its methodology and position in the Hanafi school; the commentaries show how later scholars engaged with the text.

الباب الثاني
دراسة عن
الإمام القدوري ومختصره
الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري.
الفقه
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري.
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري والأعمال العلمية التي قامت عليه .
The Second Chapter: Study on Imam al-Quduri and His Mukhtasar. Section One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. Fiqh. Section Two: Study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Section Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the scholarly works based upon it.
Source pages p. 281

Commentary
This is the opening of the second chapter of al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri. The chapter is divided into three sections: first, a biography of Imam al-Quduri, the author of the original matn; second, a study of the Mukhtasar itself, its methodology and features; third, an overview of the commentaries and scholarly works that have been written on the Mukhtasar. This serves as an introduction to contextualize the text and its author within the Hanafi tradition.

Key Terms
الإمام القدوري (al-Imām al-Qudūrī): Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH/1037 CE), a renowned Hanafi jurist, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, one of the most foundational texts in the Hanafi madhhab.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): The abridged manual of Hanafi fiqh authored by Imam al-Quduri, widely used as a beginner's text and subject to many commentaries.
شروح مختصر القدوري (shurūḥ Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): The commentaries written on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the most famous being al-Lubab by al-Maydani. These works explain and expand upon the rulings in the matn.

Imam al-Quduri: His Teachers and Students
Biographical introduction listing teachers and students.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key teachers and students of Imam al-Quduri and explain his significance as a bridge between early and later Hanafi scholarship.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's teachers and students connect the Hanafi school from al-Jassas to the chief judges of Baghdad.

This passage introduces Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the foundational Hanafi primer Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Knowing his scholarly lineage helps us appreciate the transmission of Hanafi fiqh and the reliability of the texts we study. We will explore who taught him and who learned from him, including both Hanafi and Shafi'i scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Quduri's teachers
List the three teachers mentioned and their specialties (hadith, fiqh). Note that al-Jurjani was a student of al-Jassas and buried beside Abu Hanifa.
Teacher 3 appears only in a footnote; focus on al-Mu'adhdhib and al-Jurjani.
2
Identify al-Quduri's students
List the four named students. Note their later achievements: commentator, chief judge, historian.
Al-Khatib al-Baghdadi was a Shafi'i – showing cross-madhhab learning.
3
Map the scholarly chain
Trace the line: Abu Bakr al-Jassas → al-Jurjani → al-Quduri → al-Aqta' (commentator) and al-Damaghani (chief judge).
This chain shows continuity in Hanafi scholarship.
4
Assess al-Quduri's legacy
Understand that his Mukhtasar became a core text, and his students spread his teachings.

وروى عنه (۱).
(۲) ٢ـ أبو بكر محمد بن علي بن سويد المؤدب، الإمام المحدث، المتوفى سنة ٣٨١ هـ ، وقد أخذ عنه القدوري الحديث، وروى ، وجزء القدوري في الحديث كله مروي عنه .
(۳) ٣ـ أبو عبد الله محمد بن يحيى بن مهدي الجرجاني الحنفي، نزيل بغداد، من كبار أئمة وفقهاء الحنفية، وهو من تلاميذ الإمام أبي بكر الرازي الجصاص ، وهو الذي تفقه عليه القدوري، وقد توفي سنة ٣٩٨هـ رحمه الله تعالى، ودفن إلى جانب قبر الإمام أبي حنيفة.

(٤) (5) لا شك أنه تتلمذ على يد القدوري كثيرون، لكن لم تُدون كتب التراجم إلا أشهرهم وعدداً يسيراً منهم، فكان ممن أخذ عنه، وكان فيما بعد إماماً من الأئمة:

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. He narrated from (1)... 2. Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Suwayd al-Mu'adhdhib, the imam and hadith scholar, died 381 AH, and al-Quduri took hadith from him, and he narrated, and al-Quduri's hadith collection is entirely narrated from him. 3. Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Mahdi al-Jurjani al-Hanafi, resident of Baghdad, one of the great imams and jurists of the Hanafis, and he was a student of Imam Abu Bakr al-Razi al-Jassas, and it was he from whom al-Quduri learned fiqh. He died 398 AH, may God have mercy on him, and was buried next to the grave of Imam Abu Hanifa. His students: There is no doubt that many studied under al-Quduri, but the biographical books only record the most famous and a few of them. Among those who took from him and later became imams: 1. al-Khatib al-Baghdadi Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Baghdadi, the Shafi'i jurist, hadith scholar, historian, author of many works, including Tarikh Baghdad, one of the leading Shafi'is, died 463 AH. 2. Abu Nasr Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi, known as al-Aqta', the excellent Hanafi jurist, commentator on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, died 474 AH. 3. Abu al-Qasim Abd al-Wahid ibn Ali ibn Burhan al-'Ukbari, author of works, a Hanafi jurist who studied under al-Quduri and was a leading figure in Arabic language and genealogy, died 456 AH. 4. Abu Abdullah Muhammad ibn Ali ibn Muhammad ibn al-Husayn ibn Abd al-Malik al-Damaghani al-Kabir, Chief Judge, the Hanafi jurist, one of the great Hanafi notables, and the leadership of the Hanafis of his time ended with him.
Source pages p. 288

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri, the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh. The text lists three of his teachers: first, Abu Bakr Muhammad ibn Ali al-Mu'adhdhib (d. 381 AH), from whom al-Quduri narrated hadith; second, Abu Abdullah al-Jurjani al-Hanafi (d. 398 AH), a prominent Hanafi jurist who studied under Abu Bakr al-Jassas and from whom al-Quduri learned fiqh, buried next to Imam Abu Hanifa; third, a teacher mentioned in the footnote (not fully cited). The passage then lists four famous students: al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (d. 463 AH), a Shafi'i scholar and historian; Abu Nasr al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), a Hanafi jurist who wrote a commentary on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar; Abu al-Qasim al-'Ukbari (d. 456 AH), a Hanafi jurist and linguist; and al-Damaghani (d. 456 AH), a chief judge and head of the Hanafi school in his time. The biographical notes highlight al-Quduri's central position in the Hanafi tradition, with connections to both hadith and fiqh scholarship.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Qudūrī): Imam Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the Hanafi jurist and author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a core text of the Hanafi school.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): The concise legal manual by al-Quduri covering Hanafi fiqh, arranged according to standard fiqh chapters, from taharah to diyat.
الخطيب البغدادي (al-Khaṭīb al-Baghdādī): Abu Bakr Ahmad ibn Ali ibn Thabit al-Khatib al-Baghdadi (d. 463 AH), a famous Shafi'i hadith scholar and historian, author of Tarikh Baghdad.

Introduction and Front Matter

Imam al-Quduri and His Book al-Tajrid: A Model of Comparative Fiqh
Biographical introduction about al-Quduri and his work al-Tajrid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the purpose and methodology of al-Tajrid and explain its significance in the Hanafi tradition of comparative fiqh.

Core Idea
Al-Tajrid by Imam al-Quduri is a monumental work of comparative fiqh that respectfully presents both Hanafi and Shafi'i views with evidence, then prefers the Hanafi position.

This lesson explores the biography of Imam al-Quduri, a towering Hanafi scholar, and his magnum opus al-Tajrid. Unlike his famous Mukhtasar, al-Tajrid is an independent work on points of divergence (khilafiyyat) between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Understanding its purpose and methodology deepens your appreciation for the Hanafi tradition of rigorous yet respectful scholarly debate.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Author
Recognize Imam al-Quduri (Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Baghdadi) as a major Hanafi authority, born 362 AH, died 428 AH. He is best known for his Mukhtasar, but his expertise extended to comparative fiqh.
Al-Quduri's full name and background establish his credibility.
2
Distinguish al-Tajrid from Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Understand that al-Tajrid is not a commentary on his own matn but a separate work dedicated to issues where the Hanafis and Shafi'is disagree. The passage explicitly states this as a work on 'al-khilafiyyat'.
This distinction is crucial to avoid conflating the two works.
3
Outline the Methodology of al-Tajrid
Trace the author's consistent sequence: (1) State the Hanafi opinion, (2) state the Shafi'i opinion, (3) present Hanafi evidence, (4) present Shafi'i evidence and their critiques of the Hanafi evidence, (5) discuss each point, and finally (6) prefer (tarjih) the Hanafi view.
This systematic method trains the student in evidence-based analysis.
4
Appreciate the Scholarly Tone
Note the description: 'calm style in dialogue and debate' and 'abundant good manners'. The author avoided harshness, setting a model for respectful ikhtilaf.
Adab is integral to fiqh discourse.
5
Evaluate the Significance for a Student of Fiqh
The passage claims the book develops a 'strong fiqh faculty' and prepares the student for tarjih. It also instills respect for all madhhabs by showing that each has evidence.
Al-Tajrid is thus both a scholarly reference and a pedagogical tool.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري
أصحابنا وبين الشافعية شرع في إملائه سنة ٤٠٥هـ) (١) . اهـ وقال الإمام ابن تغري بردي (ت ٨٧٤هـ) في الثناء على التجريد ما نصه :
وأملى التجريد في الخلافيات، وأبان فيـه عـن حفظـه لمـا عنـد الدارقطني من أحاديث الأحكام وعللها». اهـ
وقال عنه صاحب كشف الظنون (۲) : «التجريد للإمام القدوري في مجلد كبير، أفرد فيه ما خالف فيه الشافعي مـن المسائل، بإيجاز الألفاظ، وأورد الترجيح، ليشترك المبتدئ والمتوسط في فهمه». اهـ
وقال العلامة الشيخ محمد زاهد الكوثري (ت ١٣٧١هـ): «ويدل تجريده على سعته الفقه» (۳). سعته في
وقد جاء في مقدمة المؤلف ما نصه :
ابتدأ الشيخ أبو الحسين أحمد بن محمد بن جعفر البغدادي القدوري رضي الله عنه بالإملاء يوم الأحد، الثالث والعشرين من ذي القعدة، سنة خمس وأربعمائة، وقال:
اللهم اعصمنا من الزلل، ووفقنا في القول والعمل، واجعلنا لك طائعين، وبما يُرضيك متمسكين، وفيما عندك راغبين.
(۱) الجواهر المضية ٢٤٨/١.
.٢( ٣٤٦/١)
(۳) التحرير الوجيز ص۱۰۸ ، في إجازته لتلميذه الأستاذ أحمد خيري.
الفصل الأول : ترجمة الإمام القدوري
۲۹۷
قد أفردنا في هذا الكتاب ما خالف فيه الشافعي، بإيجاز الألفاظ، واستيفاء معانيه، وأوردنا الترجيح ليشترك المبتدئ والمتوسط في فهمه، والانتفاع به، والله ولي التوفيق». اهـ
وكان من منهج القدوري في كتابه التجريد، أنه بدأ كتابه بكتاب الطهارة، وهكذا إلى تمام أبواب الفقه على الترتيب المعهود، ولا يذكر في التجريد إلا المسائل الخلافية بين الحنفية والشافعية، فيبدأ بذكر رأي الحنفية في المسألة، ثم يُتبع ذلك برأي الشافعية، ثم يعرض أدلة الحنفية، وبعدها يذكر أدلة الشافعية، ومناقشاتهم لأدلة الحنفية، ثم يناقشها واحداً واحداً، ثم يتوصل بعد ذلك إلى ترجيح رأي الحنفية.

Imam Ibn Taghribirdi (d. 874 AH) said in praise of al-Tajrid: 'And he dictated al-Tajrid on points of divergence, and therein he revealed his memory of what al-Daraqutni had of hadiths of rulings and their defects.' End quote.
And the author of Kashf al-Zunun said about him: 'Al-Tajrid by Imam al-Quduri is a large volume, in which he isolated the matters in which al-Shafi'i differed from the Hanafis, with concise wording, and he presented the preference (tarjih), so that both the beginner and intermediate student may understand it.' End quote.
And the erudite scholar Shaykh Muhammad Zahid al-Kawthari (d. 1371 AH) said: 'His Tajrid indicates his breadth of fiqh.'
And in the author's introduction, he said:
'Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Baghdadi al-Quduri, may Allah be pleased with him, began dictation on Sunday, the twenty-third of Dhu al-Qa'dah, in the year 405 AH, and said: O Allah, protect us from slips, and grant us success in speech and action, and make us obedient to You, adhering to what pleases You, and desiring what is with You.'

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri
297
'We have collected in this book the matters in which al-Shafi'i differed from us, with concise wording and comprehensive meanings, and we have presented the preference (tarjih) so that both beginner and intermediate student may understand it and benefit from it. Allah is the grantor of success.' End quote.
The methodology of al-Quduri in his book al-Tajrid was that he began with the Book of Purification, and so on through all chapters of fiqh in the usual order, and in al-Tajrid he only mentions controversial issues between Hanafis and Shafi'is. He begins by mentioning the Hanafi opinion on the issue, then follows it with the Shafi'i opinion, then presents the Hanafi evidence, then mentions the Shafi'i evidence and their discussions of the Hanafi evidence, then discusses them one by one, and then arrives at preferring the Hanafi opinion.
The expression of the book is good and easy, and the author used a calm style in dialogue and debate between the two sides, with abundant good manners in wording and discussions. He began dictating it in the year 405 AH, and at that time his age was 43 years, which is the age of perfection and maturity.
This book is considered one of the greatest and grandest books of comparative fiqh, rich in evidence and discussions that give the student a strong fiqh faculty, training him and qualifying him for the rank of tarjih, and consideration of opinions and their evidence. It also confirms to the student that each madhhab and opinion has its evidence, and each has its perspective and basis, which instills in the student of knowledge good manners, respect, and fairness towards all madhhabs.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction about Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the author of the famous Hanafi matn 'Mukhtasar al-Quduri'. The text focuses on his magnum opus, 'al-Tajrid', which is a work of comparative fiqh (al-fiqh al-muqaran) specifically detailing the differences between the Hanafi school and the Shafi'i school. Imam al-Quduri began dictating al-Tajrid in the year 405 AH at the age of 43. The book's methodology is described: for each issue, he presents the Hanafi opinion, then the Shafi'i opinion, then the Hanafi evidence, followed by the Shafi'i evidence and their criticisms of the Hanafi evidence, and finally he discusses and refutes each point, ultimately preferring (tarjih) the Hanafi position. The text highlights that the book is characterized by concise wording and a calm, respectful tone in debating. It is considered a major reference in the field. The passage also includes praises from later scholars such as Ibn Taghribirdi, the author of Kashf al-Zunun (Hajji Khalifa), and Muhammad Zahid al-Kawthari, all lauding al-Quduri's mastery and the value of al-Tajrid. This biography is intended to establish the credibility and significance of the author and his work for the reader of al-Lubab (a commentary on al-Quduri).

Key Terms
التجريد (al-Tajrid): The title of Imam al-Quduri's work on comparative fiqh focusing on Hanafi-Shafi'i differences, with evidence and tarjih.
الترجيح (al-tarjih): The act of preferring one scholarly opinion over another based on strength of evidence. In al-Tajrid, it refers to preferring the Hanafi view after discussion.
الخلافيات (al-khilafiyyat): Matters of dispute or divergence between schools of law; the subject matter of al-Tajrid dealing with Hanafi-Shafi'i differences.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's al-Tajrid is a model of comparative fiqh that teaches both evidence-based tarjih and respectful scholarly dialogue.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Methodology of Comparative Fiqh: Imam al-Quduri's al-Tajrid
Introduces Imam al-Quduri and his comparative fiqh work al-Tajrid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the methodology of Imam al-Quduri's comparative fiqh work al-Tajrid and explain its significance in fostering respectful scholarly debate.

Core Idea
Al-Tajrid trains students to weigh evidence with respect—each madhhab has its proofs.

Imam al-Quduri's al-Tajrid is not just another fiqh manual; it is a masterclass in comparative jurisprudence. The passage before us outlines the precise methodology he employed to present, critique, and weigh evidence from the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. Understanding this approach is essential for any student who wishes to engage in scholarship that is both rigorous and respectful.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Tajrid's Purpose
The passage states that al-Quduri devoted his book to 'what al-Shafi'i differed from us' — that is, exclusively the points of disagreement between Hanafis and Shafi'is. Recognize that this is a specialized work, not a comprehensive fiqh text.
2
Outline the Structure
For each disputed issue, al-Quduri follows a consistent sequence: Hanafi opinion, Shafi'i opinion, Hanafi evidence, Shafi'i evidence, Shafi'i objections to Hanafi evidence, Hanafi response, and finally tarjih (preference) for the Hanafi view. This ensures a balanced yet decisive presentation.
3
Note the Style and Adab
The passage highlights the 'calm style in dialogue and debate' with 'abundant good manners'. This is not just a theoretical point; it instills in the reader the proper adab of ikhtilaf — respectful disagreement.
The goal is not to demean the other school but to arrive at truth through evidence.
4
Appreciate the Outcome
The author explicitly states that this method develops a 'strong fiqh aptitude' and qualifies the student for tarjih. It also fosters respect and fairness, recognizing that every madhhab has its evidence.

Chapter One: Biography of Imam al-Quduri. 297. He said: 'We have devoted in this book to what al-Shafi'i differed from us, with concise expressions and comprehensive meanings, and we presented the tarjih so that both beginner and intermediate can understand and benefit. And Allah is the Granter of success.' End quote. The methodology of al-Quduri in his book al-Tajrid was that he began with the Book of Taharah, and so on through the chapters of fiqh in the usual order. He mentions only the disputed issues between Hanafis and Shafi'is. He begins by stating the Hanafi opinion, then follows it with the Shafi'i opinion, then presents the Hanafi evidence, then mentions the Shafi'i evidence and their objections to the Hanafi evidence, then discusses them one by one, and then arrives at the tarjih of the Hanafi opinion. The expression of the book is good and easy; the author used a calm style in dialogue and debate between the two parties, with abundant good manners in words and discussions. He began dictating it in 405 AH, when he was 43 years old, the age of perfection and maturity. This book is considered among the greatest books of comparative fiqh; it is rich in evidence and discussions that give the student a strong fiqh aptitude, training him and qualifying him for the level of tarjih and examining opinions and their evidence. This book, with its presentation of evidence from each side, affirms to the student that every madhhab and opinion has its evidence, each has its viewpoint and basis, which instills in the student good manners, respect, and fairness towards all the respected fiqh madhhabs. 298. ... and that the four fiqh madhhabs are like one cohesive family connected by the bond of Islam and knowledge, leading to mutual love and affection among the followers of these respected fiqh madhhabs. The book was printed critically edited by a team of about twenty [scholars], and published in 12 volumes. The supervisors were Prof. Dr. Muhammad Ahmad Siraj and Prof. Dr. Ali Jum'ah Muhammad. The edition was published by Dar al-Salam for Printing and Publishing in Cairo, in 1425 AH. The editors relied on several manuscript copies, and there are other copies mentioned in the comprehensive index that the editors did not mention. Overall, the edition is largely acceptable, but it is not free from corrections and errors that occurred in the text. 2- Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi: Mukhtasar al-Karkhi is authored by Imam Abu al-Hasan Ubayd Allah ibn al-Husayn al-Karkhi, to whom the leadership of the Hanafis in his time ended, who died in Baghdad in 340 AH. It appears from the texts quoted from him that al-Karkhi did not omit mentioning evidence, like the rest of the mukhtasars, and that he quotes the hadith used as evidence with its connected chain.
Source pages p. 297

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Imam al-Quduri and his important comparative fiqh work 'al-Tajrid'. The author of al-Lubab (al-Maidani) describes the methodology of al-Tajrid: it focuses exclusively on points of disagreement between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools. For each issue, al-Quduri first presents the Hanafi opinion, then the Shafi'i opinion, then the Hanafi evidence, followed by the Shafi'i evidence and their objections, after which he refutes those objections and finally gives preference (tarjih) to the Hanafi view. The style is described as calm and polite, fostering mutual respect between the schools. The book was begun in 405 AH when al-Quduri was 43. It is considered a masterpiece of comparative fiqh, training students in the skills of weighing evidence. The passage also provides information on the modern critical edition published in 12 volumes under the supervision of Prof. Dr. Muhammad Ahmad Siraj and Prof. Dr. Ali Jum'ah. Additionally, it briefly mentions another work: Sharh Mukhtasar al-Karkhi, authored by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Karkhi, a leading Hanafi scholar of his time, noting that his Mukhtasar included chains of transmission for hadiths.

Key Terms
التجريد (al-Tajrid): The title of Imam al-Quduri's comparative fiqh work, focusing on Hanafi-Shafi'i differences.
المختصر الكرخي (Mukhtasar al-Karkhi): A concise fiqh text by Imam al-Karkhi, a leading Hanafi scholar, which included evidence and hadith chains.
الترجيح (tarjih): The process of preferring one opinion over another based on stronger evidence; the final step in al-Tajrid's treatment of each issue.

The Status and Praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical praise and introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify the key elements of its scholarly reception as described in the passage.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri became the universally relied-upon foundational text of the Hanafi madhhab.

Imam al-Quduri's concise manual was not merely a personal effort; it was a work that received divine acceptance and became indispensable for scholars and students alike. This passage from a commentary introduction highlights the unanimous reliance on the Mukhtasar and the high praise it garnered across the Islamic world.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his motivation
The passage begins by noting that Imam al-Quduri compiled his concise work for his son Muhammad. This personal motivation is a common practice among scholars, but the work's impact extended far beyond.
2
Recognize the descriptors of acceptance
Look for phrases like 'Allah ordained great acceptance' and 'Allah benefited countless people through it'. These indicate that the text's success was seen as divinely ordained.
3
Analyze the scholarly consensus
The phrase 'their word agreed upon relying on it completely' shows that the Mukhtasar became a standard reference in the Hanafi madhhab.
4
Examine the metaphor used by Imam al-Razi
Imam al-Razi compares the necessity of the book to water for a thirsty person. This emphasizes that the text was considered essential for both settled and nomadic peoples.
The metaphor 'al-zilal al-sa’if al-sadi' refers to cool water in summer, highlighting indispensability.
5
Connect to the madhhab's authority structure
Understanding that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational matn helps you appreciate its role in the Hanafi curriculum and why it received so many commentaries.

Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
307
First Section
The Status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Praise of Scholars upon it
Imam al-Quduri compiled his concisework in fiqh for his son Muhammad (1). Then Allah ordained for this concise work great acceptance, and Allah benefited through it countless people. It attained a high, distinguished status among the scholars of the madhhab, and their word agreed upon relying on it completely, and that it is among the esteemed, advanced texts. And they praised it from many angles with great praise.
And among these praises that I have collected from the introductions of commentaries on al-Quduri: what Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn al-Mukhtar al-Razi, died 500 AH, said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri, named 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri':
'It — i.e., Mukhtasar al-Quduri — is a book whose fame spread widely in the horizons, and friends exchanged it, and the settled and the nomadic needed it, just as the thirsty person needs cool water in the summer (2).'
Source pages p. 306

Commentary
This passage is a biographical introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi fiqh text. It begins by noting that Imam al-Quduri authored this concise work for his son Muhammad, a common practice among scholars to benefit their families and the ummah. The text then highlights the divine acceptance and widespread benefit of the work, emphasizing that it became a central reference in the Hanafi madhhab. Scholars unanimously relied upon it and considered it among the most authoritative primary texts. The author then cites a specific praise from Imam Ahmad al-Razi (d. 500 AH), who wrote a commentary titled 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri'. Al-Razi describes the book as renowned across regions, transmitted among peers, and indispensable for both urban and rural communities, comparing its necessity to water for a thirsty person. This passage serves to establish the authority and importance of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri as a core text in Hanafi jurisprudence.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual in Hanafi fiqh compiled by Imam Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Foundational Hanafi Text
Compilation of praises for Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify the praise given by three major Hanafi scholars.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the foundational Hanafi matn, praised for conciseness, correctness, and universal acceptance.

This lesson explores the high status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri within the Hanafi school. You will read quotations from three influential Hanafi scholars—Imam al-Razi, Imam al-Marghinani, and Imam al-Samarqandi—each praising the Mukhtasar's conciseness, clarity, and widespread use. Understanding this context will help you appreciate why this text is a cornerstone of Hanafi learning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their works
List the three scholars cited and the titles of their commentaries or books where they praised al-Quduri.
Al-Razi wrote 'Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri', al-Marghinani wrote 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', al-Samarqandi wrote 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'.
2
Extract the key points of praise
For each scholar, note what specific qualities they highlighted (e.g., conciseness, correctness, blessing).
Al-Razi emphasized its need like water; al-Marghinani called it the most beautiful book; al-Samarqandi noted widespread desire.
3
Analyze the timeline
Observe the dates: al-Razi d.500 AH, al-Samarqandi d.537 AH (about 100 years after al-Quduri d.428 AH), al-Marghinani d.593 AH. This shows sustained acceptance over a century.
This chronological spread indicates the enduring legacy of the Mukhtasar.
4
Connect to the Hanafi curriculum
Understand that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a primary matn that later works like al-Hidayah build upon, making it essential for students of the school.

المبحث الأول
مكانة مختصر القدوري وثناء العلماء عليه
جَمَعَ الإمام القدوري مختصره في الفقه لابنه محمد(۱)، ثم كتـب الله لهذا المختصر القبول الكبير، ونفع الله به خلقاً لا يُحصون، ونــال مكانة عالية مرموقةً عند علماء المذهب، وأجمعت كلمتهم علـى اعتماده كل الاعتماد، وأنه من المتون المعتبرة المقدمة، وأثنوا عليه من نواح عديدة ثناءً عظيماً.
ومن هذه الثناءات التي جمعتها من مقدمات شروح القدوري: ما قاله الإمام أحمد بن محمد بن المظفر بن المختار الرازي، المتوفى سنة ٥٠٠هـ، في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري، المسمى: حل مشكلات القدوري :
«وهو ـ أي مختصر القدوري - كتاب طنَّـت بـه الآفاق، وتناقله الرفاق، واحتاج إليه الحاضر والبادي، كما يحتاج إلى الزلال الصائف الصادي(٢).
وأكب على دراسته المحتدي (۱) والمبتدي، وألب(٢) على قراءته المقتدى والمقتدي، لما فيه من حُسْن الإيجاز، ولطف الإعجاز، وجودة المعاني، ومتانة المباني، وكثرة المسائل المحتاج إليها، والألفاظ الصحيحة المتفق عليها ، وكونه مباركاً على طالبيه ميموناً على قارئيه وضابطيه ، والناسُ أعقل من أن يمدحوا مـا لـم يـروا عنده آثار إحسان...». اهـ
وقال الإمام المرغيناني ، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٣هـ، في مقدمة كتابه «بداية المبتدي»(۳)، الذي شرحه في «الهداية»: وحيث وقع الاتفاق بتطواف العراق (الطرق) ، وجدتُ المختصر المنسوب إلى القدوري أجمل كتاب، في أحسن إيجاز وإعجاب». اهـ
وقد كتب الله لهذا المختصر القبول فوق ما تقر به العيون، حتى قال الإمام السمرقندي ، المتوفى سنة ٥٣٧هـ، في مقدمـة كتابـه «تحفة الفقهاء»، أي بعد مائة سنة تقريباً من وفاة القدوري: «لقد عمت رغبة الفقهاء إلى هذا الكتاب». اهـ، ونَفَعَ الله بـه خلقاً لا يُحصون (٤) . اهـ
Section One: The Status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Scholars' Praise for It
Imam al-Quduri compiled his Mukhtasar in fiqh for his son Muhammad. Then Allah wrote for this Mukhtasar great acceptance, and Allah benefited countless people through it, and it attained a high and distinguished status among the scholars of the madhhab. Their consensus was on relying upon it completely, and that it is among the respected and preferred texts. They praised it extensively from many angles.
Among these praises that I have collected from the introductions of commentaries on al-Quduri is what Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn al-Muzaffar ibn al-Mukhtar al-Razi, died 500 AH, said in the introduction to his commentary on al-Quduri, titled 'The Solution of the Problems of al-Quduri':
''It – meaning Mukhtasar al-Quduri – is a book that resounded through the horizons, that companions transmitted, needed by the settled and the desert dweller, just as the thirsty in summer is in need of cool, pure water.
The advanced and the beginner devoted themselves to studying it, and the followed and the follower committed to reading it, because of its fine conciseness, the subtlety of its inimitability, the quality of its meanings, the strength of its structures, the abundance of needed issues, the correct and agreed-upon expressions, and that it is blessed for its students and auspicious for its readers and memorizers. People are too intelligent to praise something without seeing signs of beneficence at it....'' End quote.
And Imam al-Marghinani, died 593 AH, said in the introduction to his book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', which he explained in 'al-Hidayah': ''Whenever agreement occurred in the itineraries of Iraq, I found the Mukhtasar attributed to al-Quduri the most beautiful book, in the best conciseness and appeal.'' End quote.
And Allah wrote for this Mukhtasar acceptance beyond what eyes can bear, such that Imam al-Samarqandi, died 537 AH, said in the introduction to his book 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', that is about one hundred years after the death of al-Quduri: ''Indeed the desire of the fuqaha for this book has become widespread.'' End quote. And Allah benefited through it countless people. End quote.
Source pages p. 307

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter compilation documenting the high status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri within the Hanafi school. The author cites three major Hanafi scholars: Imam al-Razi (d. 500 AH), Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), and Imam al-Samarqandi (d. 537 AH). Each praises the Mukhtasar for its conciseness, correctness, and widespread acceptance. Al-Razi emphasizes that the book was needed by all, like water in summer, and that both beginners and advanced scholars studied it eagerly. Al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, calls it the most beautiful book in the best conciseness and appeal, based on his travels in Iraq. Al-Samarqandi notes that within a century of al-Quduri's death, fuqaha had a widespread desire for the book. The passage demonstrates the universal acceptance of this text as a foundational matn in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational Hanafi text.
الإمام القدوري (al-Imam al-Quduri): Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ahmad ibn Ja'far al-Quduri, a leading Hanafi jurist of Baghdad.
حل مشكلات القدوري (Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri): A commentary by Imam al-Razi (d. 500 AH) explaining problematic passages in Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A matn by Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, later explained in al-Hidayah.
تحفة الفقهاء (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha): A fiqh work by Imam al-Samarqandi (d. 537 AH) that shows the influence of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who wrote the commentary 'حل مشكلات القدوري' (Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri)?
A) Imam al-Marghinani
B) Imam al-Samarqandi
C) Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Razi
D) Imam al-Quduri himself

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a universally acclaimed Hanafi text, praised for its conciseness, correctness, and widespread acceptance by scholars across generations.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Later Scholars
Biographical praise of a key Hanafi text

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key Hanafi scholars who praised Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain why it is considered a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the most praised concise fiqh manual; it serves both beginners and advanced scholars.

This passage collects the testimonies of four major Hanafi imams who extolled the virtues of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Their praise highlights the text's conciseness, comprehensiveness, and universal acceptance. Understanding this context helps us appreciate why this mukhtasar became a cornerstone of Hanafi education for centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars
List the four Hanafi imams quoted: al-Marghinani, al-Samarqandi, al-Razi, and al-Zahidi. Note their death dates and key works.
Each lived within two centuries of al-Quduri.
2
Extract the key praise
For each scholar, find the specific phrase that describes Mukhtasar al-Quduri. For example, al-Marghinani calls it 'the finest book in conciseness and admiration.'
These phrases reveal what the madhhab valued in a text.
3
Analyze the audience
The passage states that both al-muhtadi (advanced) and al-mubtadi (beginner) engage with this book. Reflect on why a single text can serve both levels.
This dual utility is a sign of pedagogical excellence.
4
Synthesize the significance
Combine the praises to form a unified description of the Mukhtasar's place in the Hanafi tradition: blessed, widely circulated, indispensable, and rich in content.
The text's acceptance is seen as divinely ordained.

(٢) أي لَزِم وأقام. ينظر مختار الصحاح (لبب).

وقال الإمام حسام الدين الرازي علي بن أحمد، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٨هـ، في مقدمة كتابه : «تكملة القدوري»:
أما بعد : فإن أعلى مراتب اللاحق إذا عَجَزَ عن إدراك شأن السابق، أن يَشقَ غباره، أو يَرْمُقَ بالعين آثاره، والشيخ الإمام أبــو الحسين البغدادي القدوري رحمة الله عليه ألف مختصراً برز في تصنيفه، وجود في ترتيبه وترصيفه وأغنى بـه مـع وجازة لفظه وجزالة المعنى مع كثرة المسائل، والإيماء إلى الدلائل، حيث لا غنية للمبتدي عن دراسته وقراءته، ولا مندوحة للمنتهي عن مراجعته ومطالعته ، فمَن طَمِعَ أن يأتي بمثله : كان أطمـع مـن أشعب(۱)، وأعجز من ثعلب(٢)...». اهـ

(۲) ينظر مجمع الأمثال ٥٣/٢ (٢٦٤٢).
(۳) (مخطوط).
Chapter Two: Study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. He (i.e., the advanced scholar and the beginner) focused on studying it, and the one who is followed and the follower clung to reading it, for what it contains of good conciseness, elegance of miraculousness, soundness of meanings, strength of structures, abundance of needed issues, sound and agreed-upon expressions, and that it is blessed for its students, auspicious for its readers and memorizers. And people are too intelligent to praise something without seeing effects of goodness in it. The end. Imam al-Marghinani, d. 593 AH, said in the introduction of his book 'Bidayat al-Mubtadi', which he explained in 'al-Hidayah': 'Wherever I found agreement by traversing the Iraqi roads, I found the mukhtasar attributed to al-Quduri to be the finest book, in the best conciseness and admiration.' The end. And Allah had written for this mukhtasar acceptance beyond what eyes can bear, until Imam al-Samarqandi, d. 537 AH, said in the introduction of his book 'Tuhfat al-Fuqaha' (approximately one hundred years after the death of al-Quduri): 'The desire of the jurists for this book has become widespread.' The end. And Allah benefited countless people through it. The end. (1) i.e., the advanced student of knowledge. (2) i.e., he stuck to and established. See Mukhtar al-Sihah (lbb). (3) Manuscript, and this introduction was not printed with al-Hidayah which is the commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi. (4) Al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 6/1, 247-248 quoting from Imam al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH). Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi 'Ali ibn Ahmad, d. 598 AH, said in the introduction of his book 'Takmilat al-Quduri': 'To proceed: The highest rank of the later scholar, if he is unable to attain the status of the predecessor, is to follow in his footsteps or glance at his traces. The Shaykh Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Baghdadi al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, authored a mukhtasar that excelled in its composition, good in its arrangement and structure, and enriched despite its concise wording and weighty meaning with abundance of issues and allusion to evidences, such that the beginner has no need beyond studying and reading it, and the advanced has no alternative to reviewing and perusing it. Whoever aspires to produce something like it is more ambitious than Ash'ba and more incapable than Tha'lab.' The end. Imam al-Faqih Najm al-Din al-Zahidi Mukhtar ibn Mahmud, d. 658 AH, said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri, called 'al-Mujtaba': 'It—i.e., Mukhtasar al-Quduri—is the greatest book of fiqh in blessing and importance, the highest in rank and value, the most circulated in the circles of the virtuous and schools, and the most beneficial for the teacher and student.' The end. (1) Ash'ba: a man from Madinah, known as 'Ash'ba the greedy', with many stories about his greed, until he became a proverbial example. See Majma' al-Amthal by al-Maydani 1/439 (2333). (2) See Majma' al-Amthal 2/53 (2642). (3) Manuscript.
Source pages p. 308

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and prefatory section (front matter) focusing on the praise and widespread acceptance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by later Hanafi scholars. It opens by stating that both the advanced student (al-muhtadi) and the beginner (al-mubtadi) engage in studying this work, emphasizing its balanced conciseness, strength of meaning, and the blessing it carries. The author then quotes several prominent Hanafi imams:

1. Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), author of al-Hidayah, declares that after traversing the Iraqi lands, he found al-Quduri's Mukhtasar to be the finest book in its concise and admirable style.
2. Imam al-Samarqandi (d. 537 AH) notes that within about a century after al-Quduri's death, the desire of jurists for this book had become widespread.
3. Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi (d. 598 AH) praises the work as being excellent in composition, concise yet rich in content, and indispensable for both beginners and advanced scholars.
4. Imam Najm al-Din al-Zahidi (d. 658 AH) describes it as the greatest book of fiqh in blessing, importance, and circulation.

These quotations serve to establish Mukhtasar al-Quduri as a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab, universally accepted and blessed. The footnotes clarify terms (e.g., 'al-muhtadi' as the advanced student) and identify sources. This passage is not a legal ruling but rather a testimonial to the book's authority and pedagogical value.

Key Terms
المختصر (al-mukhtasar): A concise legal manual summarizing the essential rulings of the Hanafi madhhab, specifically referring to Al-Quduri's work.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a leading Hanafi jurist from Baghdad, author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
المحتدي والمبتدي (al-muhtadi wa al-mubtadi): Al-muhtadi: the advanced student of knowledge who has reached a high level. Al-mubtadi: the beginner just starting his studies.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a universally praised foundational Hanafi text, blessed and beneficial for all levels of students.
