Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Prestige of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi School
Scholarly testimonials to the value of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three scholarly praises of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain why it is considered an indispensable foundational text in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is revered as a concise yet comprehensive Hanafi manual, vital for both beginners and advanced scholars.

This lesson presents historical testimonials from prominent Hanafi scholars that highlight the enduring value of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. These praises underscore the text's unique balance of brevity and depth, making it a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh education. By studying these quotes, you will appreciate why this matn has remained central for centuries.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scholars and their eras
Read the passage and list the names of the scholars quoted, along with their death dates (e.g., al-Razi d. 598, al-Zahidi d. 658). This helps contextualize the enduring praise across generations.
Note that the scholars range from the 6th to the 13th century AH, showing sustained recognition.
2
Extract the key attributes praised
For each scholar, note the specific qualities they attribute to the Mukhtasar: 'brevity with depth', 'allusion to proofs', 'comprehensiveness', 'beneficial for teacher and student'.
Focus on the Arabic phrases like 'الإيماء إلى الدلائل' and 'أجمل كتاب في الإيجاز'.
3
Distinguish audience and purpose
Observe that some scholars emphasize the text's necessity for beginners ('لا غنية للمبتدي') while others highlight its value for advanced students ('ولا مندوحة للمنتهي'). This dual utility is a key reason for its status.
The Mukhtasar is not merely an introductory text; it remains a reference for experts.
4
Synthesize the overall consensus
The passage concludes calling it an 'esteemed composition' (تصنيفا معتبرا). Reflect on how the combined praises establish the Mukhtasar as a canonical text in the Hanafi school.
The term 'معتبر' indicates it is relied upon for fatwa and study.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

وقال الإمام حسام الدين الرازي علي بن أحمد، المتوفى سنة ٥٩٨هـ، في مقدمة كتابه : «تكملة القدوري»:
أما بعد : فإن أعلى مراتب اللاحق إذا عَجَزَ عن إدراك شأن السابق، أن يَشقَ غباره، أو يَرْمُقَ بالعين آثاره، والشيخ الإمام أبــو الحسين البغدادي القدوري رحمة الله عليه ألف مختصراً برز في تصنيفه، وجود في ترتيبه وترصيفه وأغنى بـه مـع وجازة لفظه وجزالة المعنى مع كثرة المسائل، والإيماء إلى الدلائل.
حيث لا غنية للمبتدي عن دراسته وقراءته، ولا مندوحة للمنتهي عن مراجعته ومطالعته ، فمَن طَمِعَ أن يأتي بمثله : كان أطمـع مـن أشعب(۱)، وأعجز من ثعلب(٢)...». اهـ

وقال الإمام الفقيه نجم الدين الزاهدي مختار بن محمود، المتوفى سنة ٦٥٨هـ ، في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري، المسمى: المجتبى» (۳) :
وهو ـ أي مختصر القدوري ـ أعظم دواوين الفقه بركةً وخطراً، وأرفعها شأناً وقَدْراً، وأدورها في أندية الفضلاء والمدارس، وأيمنهـا للمدرس والدارس». اهـ

وقال العلامة أبو عبد الرحمن عمر بن دانشمند، المتوفى بعد سنة ٨٠٠هـ، في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري(۱):
إن كتاب القدوري قد تباهَجَ به الطالبون، وتفاخر به الراغبون حتى صار عمدةً بينهم، وفَخَرَةً في مجالسهم، فلم يزالوا مشتغلين به في كل زمان ويتدارسونه في كل مكان.
وذلك لكونه أجمل كتاب في الإيجاز، وأشملـه علـى مختار الفتوى...». اهـ

وقال شارح القدوري الإمام الفقيه عبد الأول بـن حـسـيـن بـن حامد، المتوفى سنة ٩٥٠ هـ، في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري، المسمى: (حَدَق العيون (۲):
لما كان مختصر القدوري كتاباً شريفاً، ومختصراً لطيفاً شرحته...». اهـ

وقال العلامة شهاب الدين المرجاني، المتوفى سنة ١٣٠٦هـ : إن مختصر القدوري متن متين مفتخر، وتصنيف رصين معتبر، قد شاع بين الأئمة الأعيان وشهرته وظهور حاله تغني عن الإطناب بالبيان (۳). اهـ

Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi Ali ibn Ahmad (d. 598 AH) said in the introduction of his book 'Takmilat al-Quduri':
'To proceed: The highest rank of a successor, when unable to grasp the status of the predecessor, is to follow his dust or glance at his traces. Shaykh Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Baghdadi al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, authored a concise work that excelled in its composition, was beautiful in its arrangement and ordering, and sufficed—despite brevity of wording and depth of meaning—with numerous issues and allusion to proofs.
The beginner cannot do without studying and reading it, nor can the advanced avoid reviewing and consulting it. Whoever aspires to produce something like it would be more greedy than Ash'ab and more incapable than Tha'lab.'

Imam Faqih Najm al-Din al-Zahidi Mukhtar ibn Mahmud (d. 658 AH) said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri called 'al-Mujtaba':
'It—meaning Mukhtasar al-Quduri—is the greatest of the books of fiqh in blessing and gravity, the highest in status and worth, the most circulated in gatherings of the virtuous and schools, and the most beneficial for teacher and student.'

Allama Abu Abd al-Rahman Umar ibn Danishmand (d. after 800 AH) said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri:
'Indeed, the book of al-Quduri has been delighted in by seekers and prided in by aspirants until it became a mainstay among them and a boast in their assemblies. They have not ceased to occupy themselves with it in every time and to study it in every place. That is because it is the most beautiful book in conciseness and the most comprehensive of the chosen fatwa rulings...'

Sharh author Imam Faqih Abd al-Awwal ibn Husayn ibn Hamid (d. 950 AH) said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri called 'Hadaq al-Uyun':
'Since Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a noble book and a subtle concise work, I have commented upon it...'

Allama Shihab al-Din al-Marjani (d. 1306 AH) said: 'Indeed, Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a solid, distinguished text, a firm, esteemed composition that has spread among eminent imams, and its fame and clear state suffice from lengthy explanation.'

Thus this noble volume and excellent book became 'an esteemed composition.'
Source pages p. 309

Commentary
This passage is a collection of scholarly testimonials to the prestige and utility of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh primer by Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). The author of this book (likely the commentator on Lubab) gathers remarks from several Hanafi authorities spanning the 6th to 13th centuries AH. Each scholar emphasizes the book's comprehensive brevity, its synthesis of numerous masail alongside references to proofs, and its indispensability for both beginners and advanced students. The quotes also mention commentaries written on it, such as Takmilat al-Quduri by al-Razi, al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi, and Hadaq al-Uyun by Abd al-Awwal. The final line affirms that the Mukhtasar became widely recognized as an 'esteemed composition' (tasnif mu'tabar) in the Hanafi school. The passage serves to establish the canonical status of the text and to encourage its study.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, a primary text of Hanafi fiqh.
الإيماء إلى الدلائل (al-ima' ila al-dala'il): Allusion to the proofs; the author indicates evidence for rulings without detailed exposition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Imam Husam al-Din al-Razi
B) Imam Najm al-Din al-Zahidi
C) Allama Abu Abd al-Rahman Umar ibn Danishmand
D) Allama Shihab al-Din al-Marjani

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi text praised across centuries for its concise comprehensiveness and utility for all levels of students.

The Authority of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi School
Assembling commendations of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state three reasons why Mukhtasar al-Quduri became the most widely relied-upon matn in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the most widely taught and authoritative Hanafi matn for its concise selection of the mufta bihi opinions.

This lesson introduces the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational concise manual of Hanafi fiqh. It is not a legal ruling but a gateway to understanding why this text carries such weight in the school. Through testimonies of classical scholars, you'll learn how this book became the standard for students and jurists alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the passage
Recognize that this is a collection of scholarly praises (taqrīẓ) establishing the authority and utility of the Mukhtasar.
It is a meta-discussion, not a ruling.
2
Note the key characteristics praised
Look for specific phrases: 'أجمل كتاب في الإيجاز وأشمله على مختار الفتوى' – it is praised for brevity and comprehensiveness in conveying the operative fatwa.
The phrase 'مختار الفتوى' is crucial.
3
Understand the impact on the school
The passage states that scholars competed over it and students memorized and taught it, making it the central text for Hanafi education.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري
وقال العلامة أبو عبد الرحمن عمر بن دانشمند، المتوفى بعد سنة ٨٠٠هـ، في مقدمة شرحه على القدوري(۱): إن كتاب القدوري قد تباهَجَ به الطالبون، وتفاخر به الراغبون حتى صار عمدةً بينهم، وفَخَرَةً في مجالسهم، فلم يزالوا مشتغلين به في كل زمان ويتدارسونه في كل مكان. وذلك لكونه أجمل كتاب في الإيجاز، وأشملـه علـى مختار الفتوى...». اهـ

وقال العلامة شهاب الدين المرجاني، المتوفى سنة ١٣٠٦هـ : إن مختصر القدوري متن متين مفتخر، وتصنيف رصين معتبر، قد شاع بين الأئمة الأعيان وشهرته وظهور حاله تغني عن الإطناب بالبيان (۳). اهـ
وهكذا غدا هذا السفر الجليل، والكتاب النبيل «تصنيفاً معتبراً، وتأليفاً معتمداً، وقد تداوله العلماء، وتنافس فيه الفقهاء، وأُولعوا فيه حفظاً ورواية، ودرساً وقراءة وتفقهاً، ودراية وشرحاً وتعليقاً (۱). اهـ وعكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، وازدحموا على تعلمه وتعليمه» (۲) ، وأكبوا عليه، وصار المفرع إليه ) (۳). الأمصار
وشاء الله تعالى فضلاً وكرماً لهذا المختصر اللطيف أن «طار في الأقطار، وسار في الأمصار وفاق في الاشتهار في جميع والأعصار على الشمس في رابعة النهار»(4). وقد وصف هذا الكتاب أيضاً بأنه «جامع صغير، ونافع كبير، وأنه أحسن متون الفقه وأفضلها ، وأتمها فائدة وأكملها، فهو بحر زاخر، وغيث ماطر (٥). «وهذا الكتاب مع صغر حجمه، ووجازة نظمه، لكن جميع الواقعات من المسائل قد يوجد في قعره أو في الساحل، وهو أنفع متون المذهب وأجلّ، وأتمها فائدة وأكمل ، خال عن الزوائد المملة،
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. And the scholar Abu Abd al-Rahman Umar ibn Danishmand, who died after 800 AH, said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri: 'Indeed, the book of al-Quduri is rejoiced by the students and boasted by the desirous, until it became a chief among them and a pride in their gatherings; they never ceased occupying themselves with it in every time and studying it in every place. That is because it is the most beautiful book in brevity and the most comprehensive on the chosen fatwa...' End quote. And the commentator of al-Quduri, the jurist imam Abd al-Awwal ibn Husayn ibn Hamid, who died in 950 AH, said in the introduction of his commentary on al-Quduri, named Hadq al-Uyun: 'Since Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a noble book and a graceful epitome, I have commented on it...' End quote. And the scholar Shihab al-Din al-Marjani, who died in 1306 AH, said: 'Indeed, Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a strong and proud text, a solid and reputable composition; it has spread among the great imams, and its fame and clear condition suffice from elaborating explanation.' End quote. Thus this venerable work and noble book became 'a reputable composition and a relied-upon authorship; scholars passed it around and jurists competed over it; they were devoted to it in memorization and narration, study and reading, fiqh comprehension, mastery, commentary and annotation.' End quote. 'Students dedicated themselves to understanding it and making others understand, crowded over learning it and teaching it, focused on it, and it became the reference.' 'And Allah by His bounty and generosity willed for this graceful epitome that it flew across regions, traveled across cities, and surpassed in fame in all districts and times like the sun at noon.' And this book was also described as 'a small comprehensive work and a great benefit, that it is the best and most excellent of fiqh texts, the most complete in benefit and perfection; it is a deep sea and a pouring rain.' 'And this book, despite its small size and concise composition, all occurrences of issues may be found in its depth or on its shore; it is the most beneficial and greatest of the texts of the school, the most complete in benefit and perfection, free from tiresome additions.'
Source pages p. 310

Commentary
This passage is a collection of eulogies from various Hanafi scholars praising the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise legal manual by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). It is not a legal ruling but an introductory study on the book's status. The first quote by Ibn Danishmand highlights the book's popularity among students and its role as a standard reference. The second by Abd al-Awwal emphasizes its nobility as a subject for commentary. Al-Marjani's testimonial affirms the text's robustness and widespread acceptance. The passage then synthesizes these praises, asserting that the book has been universally adopted in the Hanafi school for memorization, study, and commentary. The description of it as a 'small comprehensive work' (jami' saghir) and 'navigable sea' underscores its depth despite brevity. This section sets the stage for the detailed commentary (al-Lubab) that follows, affirming the authority and utility of the base text for Hanafi fiqh education.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri, a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
فتوى (fatwa): The chosen legal opinion relied upon for practice, as referenced in the phrase 'مختار الفتوى'.
متن (matn): A concise text forming the core of a legal work, here referring to the Mukhtasar itself.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri's authority rests on its concise embodiment of the operative Hanafi rulings (mufta bihi), making it the central text for study and practice in the school.

The Scholarly Status and Features of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describing the scholarly status and features of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the key features and scholarly status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as described in this passage.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a compact yet comprehensive Hanafi fiqh text containing 12,000 issues.

This passage from al-Lubab introduces Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational matn of the Hanafi school. It praises the book's widespread acceptance, its balanced scope, and its utility for both beginners and advanced scholars. Understanding this front matter helps you appreciate why this text remains central to Hanafi study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text and its author
Recognize that the passage is describing Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). This is a core Hanafi matn.
2
List the described features
Note the key attributes: it is widely studied, contains 12,000 issues, is concise yet comprehensive, avoids rare cases, and is beneficial for beginners.
Focus on phrases like 'جامع جُمَلاً من الفقه مستعملة' and 'عدد مسائله اثنتا عشر ألف مسألة'.
3
Understand the scholarly reception
The passage mentions that scholars competed in memorizing, teaching, and commenting on it, indicating its authority and acceptance.
The phrase 'صار المفرع إليه' shows it became the reference.
4
Connect to madhhab study
Reflect on why such a text is foundational: it provides a complete yet digestible overview of Hanafi fiqh, serving as a starting point for deeper study.
This contrasts with lengthy works like al-Mabsut or concise ones like Nur al-Idah.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري وتأليفاً معتمداً، وقد تداوله العلماء، وتنافس فيه الفقهاء، وأُولعوا فيه حفظاً ورواية، ودرساً وقراءة وتفقهاً، ودراية وشرحاً وتعليقاً (۱). اهـ وعكفت الطلبة على تفهمه وتفهيمه، وازدحموا على تعلمه وتعلميه» (۲) ، وأكبوا عليه، وصار المفرع إليه ) (۳). الأمصار وشاء الله تعالى فضلاً وكرماً لهذا المختصر اللطيف أن «طار في الأقطار، وسار في الأمصار وفاق في الاشتهار في جميع والأعصار على الشمس في رابعة النهار»(4). وقد وصف هذا الكتاب أيضاً بأنه «جامع صغير، ونافع كبير، وأنه أحسن متون الفقه وأفضلها ، وأتمها فائدة وأكملها، فهو بحر زاخر، وغيث ماطر (٥). «وهذا الكتاب مع صغر حجمه، ووجازة نظمه، لكن جميع الواقعات من المسائل قد يوجد في قعره أو في الساحل، وهو أنفع متون المذهب وأجلّ، وأتمها فائدة وأكمل ، خال عن الزوائد المملة، والاختصارات المخلة (١) «وقد بلغ عدد مسائله اثنتا عشر ألف مسألة» (٢). ومن المزايا العلمية لهذا المختصر : أن القدوري ضمنه المسائل العلمية المتداولة، وتجنَّب المسائل النادرة الوقوع، وفي هذا يقول الإمام السمرقندي صاحب تحفة الفقهاء (٣) (ت ٥٣٧هـ) : اعلم أن المختصر المنسوب إلى الشيخ أبي الحسين القدوري رحمه الله ، جامع جُمَلاً من الفقه مستعملة، بحيث لا تراهـا مـدى الدهر مهملة، يهدي بها الرائض (4) في أكثر الحوادث والنوازل
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It is a reliable work; scholars have circulated it, jurists have competed in it, and they were devoted to memorizing, narrating, studying, reading, comprehending, teaching, commenting, and annotating it. Students busied themselves with understanding and teaching it, crowded to learn and teach it, and they engaged with it, and it became the reference. And Allah Almighty, by His grace and generosity, willed that this elegant summary should fly across regions, travel through cities, and surpass in fame in all lands and ages the sun at midday. This book has also been described as a small collection, great in benefit, the best and most excellent of fiqh texts, most complete in benefit and perfection; it is a vast sea and a pouring rain. This book, despite its small size and concise composition, contains all kinds of occurring issues; they can be found in its depths or on its shore. It is the most beneficial and greatest of the texts of the madhhab, most complete in benefit and perfection, free from tedious additions and harmful abbreviations. Its number of issues has reached twelve thousand issues. Among its scientific merits is that al-Quduri included in it commonly used scientific issues and avoided rarely occurring issues. In this regard, Imam al-Samarqandi, author of Tuhfat al-Fuqaha (d. 537 AH), said: Know that the summary attributed to Shaykh Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, is a collection of commonly used fiqh phrases, such that you will not find them neglected over time; it guides the beginner in most incidents and issues.
Source pages p. 311

Commentary
This passage is an introduction praising Mukhtasar al-Quduri (the concise work of Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi matn). The author of al-Lubab (the sharh we are studying) opens a study chapter on this work, highlighting its broad acceptance and scholarly engagement. He notes that scholars and jurists competed in memorizing, teaching, and commenting on it, and that it became the primary reference text. He uses poetic language to describe its fame spreading like the sun at midday. The passage then cites a description of the book as a 'small collection with great benefit,' being the best of fiqh texts, a vast sea, and containing all types of issues despite its size. It emphasizes that the book is free from tedious additions and harmful abbreviations. A key piece of information provided is that it contains twelve thousand masaa'il (legal issues). The author also mentions that al-Quduri selected commonly used issues, avoiding rare ones, and quotes Imam al-Samarqandi (a Hanafi scholar from the 6th century) who confirms that the book is a collection of commonly used fiqh that aids a beginner in most situations. This front matter sets the stage for the reader, establishing the authority and comprehensiveness of the matn that will be commented upon.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise Hanafi fiqh text authored by Imam Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH/1037 CE).
المسائل (al-masā'il): Legal issues, questions, or cases in fiqh.
النوازل (al-nawāzil): Newly occurring incidents, events, or legal cases that require a ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Fame of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and a Corrected Attribution
Historical and textual correction on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the unique status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as 'al-Kitab' in the Hanafi tradition and correct a common misattribution of a famous quote to al-Jami' al-Saghir.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is 'al-Kitab' — the Hanafi school's foundational text.

This passage introduces Mukhtasar al-Quduri's extraordinary reputation. It explains why it was called simply 'al-Kitab' and corrects a widespread error about a famous praise quote. Understanding this helps you appreciate the hierarchy of Hanafi texts and avoid confusions in scholarly references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Main Claim
Recognize that the passage claims Mukhtasar al-Quduri is so famous that when 'al-Kitab' is used unrestrictedly, it refers to this book. Note the phrase 'ما هذا الإطلاق... إلا لشهرة هذا المختصر'.
This is an honorific usage unique to this text in the Hanafi school.
2
Trace Historical Usage
List the scholars who used this term: Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah, Imam al-Yazdi in his commentary title 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab', and later al-Maydani.
Al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) is a key transmitter of the Hanafi tradition.
3
Analyze the Correction
Read the 'تنبيه على خطأ' section. Understand that the quote from Abu Ali al-Shashi about 'whoever memorizes this book...' is often misattributed to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, but the author of Kashf al-Zunun correctly attributed it to al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Al-Jami' al-Saghir is by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, a foundational Hanafi text.
4
Evaluate Chronological Evidence
Note that al-Quduri was born about 18 years after al-Shashi's death (344 AH). Thus al-Shashi could not have praised al-Quduri's book. This confirms the misattribution.
Chronology is a key tool in textual criticism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري
وما هذا الإطلاق - والله أعلم - إلا لشهرة هذا المختصر وفضله، وكثرة الثناء عليه، وأنه لم يؤلف كتاب مثله، وأن كتب المذهب عليه عيال، وله عليها فضل عال.
وهم بهذا كأن لسان حالهم يقول : إن مختصر القدوري هو الكتاب الفريد الذي حُقَّ له دون غيره أن يشتهر ويُعرف إذا أُطلق لفظ : «الكتاب»، وأنه هو المراد.
وتاريخ هذا الإطلاق قديم فقد ذكره الإمام المرغيناني (ت ٥٩٣ هـ) بهذا اللفظ مراراً في «الهداية»، وفي القرن السادس نفسه ألف الإمام اليزدي المطهر بن الحسين (ت بعد ٥٥٩هـ) شرحه على مختصر القدوري، وسماه : «اللباب شرح الكتاب».
وهكذا تتابع علماء الحنفية على هذا، حتى جاء العلامة الشيخ عبد الغني الميداني (ت ۱۲۹۸هـ)، فسمى شرحه الذي بين أيدينا باسم شرح اليزدي، ولا أدري هل أخذ الميداني هذه التسمية من اليزدي إعجاباً بها، أم أنه لم يطلع على اسم كتابه، فتوافقا فيها؟ الله تعالى أعلم.
تنبيه على خطأ :
ذكر كثيرون - خطأ - من الثناء على مختصر القدوري ما نقله صاحب كشف الظنون عن أبي علي الشاشي أنه كان يقول: «مَن حفظ هذا الكتاب : فهو أحفظ أصحابنا، ومن فهمه : فهو أفهم أصحابنا» . اهـ
والصواب أن هذه المقولة قيلت في كتاب: «الجامع الصغير»، لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، وليست في مختصر القدوري، فإن صاحب كشف الظنون ذكرها في حق الجامع الصغير حين تكلم ذكره وتكلم عنه.
وأيضاً فإن القدوري قد ولد بعد ۱۸ سنة من سنة وفاة الشاشي هذا، فقد توفي أبو علي الشاشي سنة ٣٤٤هـ، كما في الجواهر المضية، وسيأتي بيان أكثر لهذا التصحيح عند الكلام عن عمل القدوري في مختصره، ومنهجه فيه، وبيان هل كتب القدوري مقدمة له أم لا؟
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
And this unrestricted reference - and Allah knows best - is only due to the fame of this Mukhtasar, its merit, the abundance of praise upon it, that no book like it has been authored, and that the books of the school are dependent on it, and it has high superiority over them.
And by this, it is as if their state of affairs says: Indeed Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the unique book which deserves, without any other, to be famous and known when the word 'al-Kitab' is used unrestrictedly, and that it is the intended meaning.
And the history of this unrestricted reference is old; Imam al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) mentioned it with this wording repeatedly in 'al-Hidayah', and in the same sixth century, Imam al-Yazdi al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn (d. after 559 AH) authored his commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and named it 'al-Lubab Sharh al-Kitab'.
And thus the Hanafi scholars continued this practice until the eminent scholar Shaykh Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani (d. 1298 AH) named his commentary, which is before us, after the name of al-Yazdi's commentary. And I do not know whether al-Maydani took this name from al-Yazdi out of admiration for it, or he did not come across the name of his book and they coincidentally agreed on it? Allah knows best.
Alert to an error:
Many have mentioned - erroneously - from the praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri what the author of Kashf al-Zunun narrated from Abu Ali al-Shashi that he used to say: 'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizing among our companions, and whoever understands it is the most understanding among our companions.' End quote.
The correct view is that this statement was said about the book 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, and not about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. For the author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned it in respect of al-Jami' al-Saghir when he discussed it and spoke about it.
And also, al-Quduri was born 18 years after the death of this al-Shashi, for Abu Ali al-Shashi died in 344 AH, as in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah, and a fuller explanation of this correction will come when discussing al-Quduri's work in his Mukhtasar, his methodology in it, and whether al-Quduri wrote an introduction for it or not.
Source pages p. 314

Commentary
This passage is a front matter section from the study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It discusses the high status of this book within the Hanafi school, noting that it is so famous that when the term 'al-Kitab' (the Book) is used without qualification, it is understood to refer to Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author traces this usage back to Imam al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah and others. He then corrects a common error: a famous praise attributed to Abu Ali al-Shashi about memorizing 'this book' was actually said about al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, not about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Evidence includes that al-Quduri was born after al-Shashi's death, making it chronologically impossible.

Key Terms
الكتاب (al-Kitab): In this context, an honorific title specifically referring to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, indicating its preeminence in the Hanafi school.
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A major work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani (d. 189 AH), one of the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to this passage, to which book does the well-known praise by Abu Ali al-Shashi actually belong?
A) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
B) al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) al-Hidayah
D) al-Lubab

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is uniquely called 'al-Kitab' in the Hanafi school, and the famous praise quote belongs to al-Jami' al-Saghir, not to al-Quduri.

Correction of a Misattributed Saying in Hanafi Fiqh
Correction of a historical misattribution in Hanafi literature

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to correctly attribute the saying of Abu Ali al-Shashi about memorizing a book to al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani and explain the historical evidence for the correction.

Core Idea
The famous saying about memorizing a Hanafi book was intended for al-Jami' al-Saghir, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This passage corrects a common misunderstanding in Hanafi circles. Many students think that Abu Ali al-Shashi praised al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, but the historical record shows he was referring to an earlier, foundational text. Understanding this helps us appreciate the chain of transmission and the importance of accurate attribution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Claim
Recognize that the saying 'Whoever memorizes this book...' is often associated with Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
2
Locate the Original Source
The author of Kashf al-Zunun records the saying and attributes it to Abu Ali al-Shashi.
3
Examine the Context in Kashf al-Zunun
The saying appears in the entry on al-Jami' al-Saghir, not on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
4
Check Chronological Evidence
Abu Ali al-Shashi died in 344 AH, while al-Quduri was born in 362 AH, so al-Shashi could not have praised al-Quduri's work.
5
Draw the Conclusion
The saying applies to al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad al-Shaybani, correcting a historical error.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب كشف الظنون عن أبي علي الشاشي أنه كان يقول: «مَن حفظ هذا الكتاب : فهو أحفظ أصحابنا، ومن فهمـه : فهو أفهم أصحابنا» . اهـ والصواب أن هذه المقولة قيلت في كتاب: الجامع الصغير»، لمحمد بن الحسن الشيباني، وليست في مختصر القدوري»، فإن صاحب كشف الظنون ذكرها في حق الجامع الصغير» حين تكلـم ذكره وتكلم عنه. وأيضاً فإن القدوري قد ولد بعد ١٨ سنة من سنة وفاة الشاشي هذا، فقد توفي أبو علي الشاشي سنة ٣٤٤هـ، كما في الجواهر المضية، وسيأتي بيان أكثر لهذا التصحيح عنـد الكـلام عـن عمـل القدوري في مختصره، ومنهجه فيه، وبيان هل كتب القدوري مقدمـة له أم لا؟
The author of Kashf al-Zunun reported from Abu Ali al-Shashi that he used to say: 'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizer of our companions, and whoever understands it is the most understanding of our companions.' The correct view is that this statement was said about the book al-Jami' al-Saghir by Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani, not about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. For the author of Kashf al-Zunun mentioned it in relation to al-Jami' al-Saghir when he discussed and spoke about it. Moreover, al-Quduri was born 18 years after the death of this al-Shashi: Abu Ali al-Shashi died in 344 AH, as in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya. A fuller explanation of this correction will come when discussing al-Quduri's work in his Mukhtasar, his methodology therein, and whether al-Quduri wrote an introduction to it or not.
Source pages p. 315

Commentary
This passage is a biographical clarification about the famous saying attributed to Abu Ali al-Shashi. The author of Kashf al-Zunun quotes the saying but then corrects a common misconception: the saying actually refers to Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani's al-Jami' al-Saghir, not to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The evidence is twofold: (1) Kashf al-Zunun itself attributes it to al-Jami' al-Saghir, and (2) al-Quduri was born after al-Shashi's death, making it impossible for al-Shashi to have praised al-Quduri's work. This is a typical scholarly correction that protects the historical accuracy of Hanafi textual transmission.

Key Terms
الجامع الصغير (al-Jami' al-Saghir): A foundational Hanafi fiqh work by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, known as one of the six Zahir al-Riwayah books.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A widely used introductory text in Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Mukhtasar al-Quduri
B) al-Jami' al-Saghir
C) al-Hidayah
D) al-Mabsut

Key Takeaway
The saying of Abu Ali al-Shashi about memorizing a book applies to al-Jami' al-Saghir, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri, based on textual and chronological evidence.

The Blessedness of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Relating a pious anecdote about the composition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to relate the story of al-Quduri seeking blessing for his Mukhtasar and explain its significance for the Hanafi school's reception of the text.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's prayer at the Kaaba made his Mukhtasar the most widely studied Hanafi text.

This lesson recounts a cherished tradition about the origins of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, one of the foundational texts of the Hanafi school. According to the story, after completing his book, al-Quduri hung it on the curtains of the Kaaba and prayed for divine blessing. This anecdote, attested in multiple manuscripts and early commentaries, underscores the reverence the Hanafi tradition holds for this work and helps explain its enduring popularity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the historical claim
What did al-Quduri do according to the story? The passage says he went to the Kaaba, hung the book on its curtains, and prayed for blessing.
The story is found in manuscripts and printed editions, indicating its widespread acceptance.
2
Examine the corroborating sources
The author cites three sources: a manuscript of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, another manuscript of the Mukhtasar itself, and an old printed edition. This shows the story is not isolated.
Also mentions Imam Ahmad al-Razi (d. 500 AH) as an early commentator who attested to the book's blessing.
3
Interpret the significance
Why is this story important? It explains why the Mukhtasar is considered a blessed text and why it became a central textbook in Hanafi fiqh.
The number of mas'ala (12,500) is also given, emphasizing comprehensiveness.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
رأيت على وجه الصفحة الأولى من نسخة مخطوطة لكتاب السراج الوهاج شرح مختصر القدوري للحدادي، المودعة في المكتبة المحمودية بالمدينة المنورة، برقم ١٠٣٦، وتاريخ نسخها في القرن التاسع، رأيتُ مكتوباً عليها ما نصه: الما صنف القدوري هذا الكتاب، عمد إلى بيت الله الحرام، وعلقه في أستار الكعبة، وسأل الله تعالى أن يبارك فيه، فاستجيب له، وجعله مباركاً، وعدد مسائله اثنتا عشر ألفاً وخمسمائة». اهـ ورأيت هذا الخبر بعينه في آخر نسخة مخطوطة من مختصر القدوري، مودعة في مكتبة قره باش، ضمن مكتبة الملك عبد العزيز بالمدينة المنورة، برقم ۲۳۱ في ٢٢٥ ورقة، وتاريخ نسخها سنة ١٠٣٣هـ. كما ذكر هذا الخبر أيضاً على الصفحة الأولى من طبعة قديمة لمختصر القدوري، طبعت سنة ١٣٠٩هـ، في المطبعة العثمانية باسطنبول، زمن السلطان عبد الحميد. وقد صرح ببركته ويُمْنه أحد الشرَّاح القدامى للقـدوري، وهـو الإمام أحمد بن محمد بن مظفر الرازي المتوفى سنة ٥٠٠ هـ، في
I saw on the first page of a manuscript copy of the book al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Haddadi, deposited in the Mahmudiyya Library in Medina, number 1036, copied in the ninth century, written on it the following text: 'When al-Quduri composed this book, he headed to the sacred House of Allah and hung it on the curtains of the Kaaba, and asked Allah Almighty to bless it. His prayer was answered, and He made it blessed. The number of its mas'ala is twelve thousand five hundred.' I saw the same report at the end of another manuscript copy of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, deposited in the Qarabash Library, within the King Abdulaziz Library in Medina, number 231, 225 folios, copied in 1033 AH. This report is also mentioned on the first page of an old printed edition of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, printed in 1309 AH at the Ottoman Press in Istanbul during the reign of Sultan Abdul Hamid. And one of the early commentators of al-Quduri explicitly stated its blessing and grace, namely Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Muzaffar al-Razi (d. 500 AH), in
Source pages p. 316

Commentary
This passage is a biographical anecdote about the blessedness of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author reports having seen a manuscript of al-Siraj al-Wahhaj (a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri) containing a story: al-Quduri, after finishing his book, went to the Kaaba, hung his book on its curtains, and prayed for Allah's blessing. The prayer was accepted, and the book became widely accepted. The number of mas'ala (legal cases) in the book is given as 12,500. The author corroborates this story from multiple sources: another manuscript in the Qarabash Library and an old printed edition. This highlights the esteem in which the Mukhtasar was held and explains its widespread acceptance in the Hanafi school. The mention of Imam Ahmad al-Razi as an early commentator who attested to its blessing further strengthens the narrative.

Key Terms
أستار الكعبة (astar al-ka'bah): The curtains or covering of the Kaaba (the kiswa).
مسائل (masa'il): Legal cases or issues; the individual rulings contained in a fiqh work.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway

The Barakah of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi Tradition
Praise and testimonies about the blessedness of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key testimonies about the barakah of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain the Hanafi practice of seeking blessing through recitation.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a blessed book whose recitation brings provision and safety from poverty.

This passage from al-Lubab collects reports from Hanafi scholars about the virtues of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author presents testimonies that the book is blessed, its blessing is known by necessity, and many have experienced ease in provision after reciting it upon a pious teacher. These reports are presented as verified experiences (mujarrabat).

Guided Path
1
Identify the sources of testimonies
List the authors and works quoted: Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri, Miftah al-Sa'adah, Kashf al-Zunun, and the personal account of Ahmad Khayri from al-Kawthari.
These are well-known Hanafi references.
2
Understand the claims about barakah
Note each claim: the matn is blessed for students, recitation during hardship brings ease, memorization protects from poverty, reciting upon a pious teacher with prayer facilitates provision.
The claims are multiple and cumulative.
3
Recognize the epistemological claim
The author emphasizes that these are 'al-mujarrabat' (experimentally proven) and that people are too intelligent to praise without seeing effects.
This establishes the reliability of the reports in the Hanafi tradition.
4
Apply the concept of barakah
Barakah is a divine blessing that comes through means; studying this matn with sincerity and under a pious teacher is a means, not a guarantee.
Sincerity and conditions are crucial.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مقدمة كتابه : حل مشكلات القدوري، فإنه قال في ثنائه على مختصر القدوري، كما تقدم: ما فيه من حسن الإيجاز ... وكونه مباركاً على طالبيه ميموناً على قارئيه وضابطيه، والناس أعقلُ من أن يمدحوا ما لم يروا عنده آثار إحسان. اهـ
وهكذا اتفقت كلمة علماء المذهب وغيرهم على أن مختصر القدوري كتاب مبارك، وأنه قد شاعت بركته حتى صارت كالعلم الضروري. اهـ
وقال صاحب مفتاح السعادة: اعلم أن هذا المختصر مما تبرك به العلماء، حتى جربوا قراءته أوقات الشدائد، وأيام الطاعون. اهـ
ونقل صاحب كشف الظنون عن صاحب «مصباح أنوار الأدعية» أنه قال: «إن الحنفية يتبركون بقراءته في أيام الوباء، وأن من حفظه يكون آمناً من الفقر، حتى قيل : إن من قرأه على أستاذ صالح، ودعا له عند ختم الكتاب بالبركة، فإنه يكون مالكاً لدراهم على عدد مسائله، وفي بعض شروح المجمع : أنه يشتمل على اثنتي عشر ألف مسألة». اهـ
قلت : وهذه الأخبار هي من الواقع والمجربات، والناس أعقل أن يمدحوا ما لم يروا عنده آثار إحسان، كما تقدم قبل قليل من كلام الإمام أحمد بن محمد الرازي، (ت ٥٠٠هـ)
* ومما وقفت عليه من الأخبار المجربة في ذلك، ما ذكره الأستاذ أحمد خيري تلميذ العلامة الكوثري في ترجمته للكوثري، المطبوعة مع المقالات، قال: ومما قرأته على الكوثري : متن «القدوري»، وهو كتاب مبارك، تواتر عند الأحناف أنه إذا قرئ على شيخ صالح كان سبباً لتيسير الرزق، ولما لم أجد أصلح من الأستاذ - الكوثري - بمصر، وذلك لأني لم أكن عرفت يومئذ الأخ الصالح السيد إبراهيم أبي العيون، شيخ معهد المينا حالياً، فقد قرأته عليه سنة ١٣٥٩هـ، ودعا لي في ختامه، وكتب لي الإجازة بخطه، فيسر الله تعالى رزقي تيسيراً لم يكن على بالي، من حل مبارك، لا شبهة فيه ولا ريبة، فلله الحمد والشكر والمنة. اهـ
Introduction to his book: Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri, for he said in praise of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, as previously mentioned: 'What it contains of excellent conciseness... and that it is blessed for its students, auspicious for its readers and memorizers, and people are more intelligent than to praise something they do not see signs of goodness from it.' End. And thus the word of the scholars of the school and others agreed that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a blessed book, and that its blessing has become widespread to the point of being common knowledge (al-ilm al-daruri). End. And the author of Miftah al-Sa'adah said: 'Know that this mukhtasar is among what scholars have sought blessing from, such that they experimented with reciting it during times of hardship and days of plague.' End. And the author of Kashf al-Zunun transmitted from the author of 'Misbah Anwar al-Ad'iyah' that he said: 'The Hanafis seek blessing by reciting it during days of epidemic, and that whoever memorizes it is safe from poverty. It is even said that whoever recites it upon a pious teacher and prays for him at the completion of the book for blessing, then he will own dirhams according to the number of its issues. And in some commentaries on al-Majma': that it contains twelve thousand issues.' End. I say: These reports are from reality and experience, and people are more intelligent than to praise something they do not see signs of goodness from it, as was stated shortly before from the words of Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Razi (d. 500 AH). And among the experiential reports I have come across in this regard is what was mentioned by Ustadh Ahmad Khayri, student of the illustrious al-Kawthari, in his biography of al-Kawthari, printed with the articles. He said: 'Among what I recited to al-Kawthari was the matn of al-Quduri, and it is a blessed book. It is mutawatir among the Hanafis that when it is recited upon a pious teacher, it becomes a cause for the facilitation of provision. And since I found no one more pious than Ustadh al-Kawthari in Egypt at that time—and I did not yet know the righteous brother Sayyid Ibrahim Abi al-Uyun, currently the teacher of the Mina Institute—I recited it to him in the year 1359 AH, and he prayed for me at its conclusion and wrote me the ijazah in his own hand. Then Allah, may He be exalted, facilitated my provision in a way I had never conceived, from a blessed source, free from any suspicion or doubt. So to Allah belongs praise, thanks, and favor.' End.
Source pages p. 317

Commentary
This passage is from the introduction of al-Lubab, a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Maydani. It presents a collection of testimonies about the blessedness (barakah) of the matn Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author begins by quoting the author of Hall Mushkilat al-Quduri, who praises the matn for its excellent conciseness and its blessing upon students, readers, and memorizers. He notes that people are too intelligent to praise something without seeing its beneficial effects. Then he states that scholars of the Hanafi school and others agree that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a blessed book, and its blessing has become widespread to the point of being considered known by necessity (al-ilm al-daruri). Then he quotes Sahib Miftah al-Sa'adah, who says that scholars have sought blessing by it, even reciting it during times of hardship and plague. He then quotes from Kashf al-Zunun, citing the author of Misbah Anwar al-Ad'iyah, who says the Hanafis seek blessing by reciting it during epidemics, and that whoever memorizes it is safe from poverty. It is even said that whoever recites it upon a pious teacher and asks for blessing at the completion, will own dirhams according to the number of its issues. In some commentaries on al-Majma', it is said to contain twelve thousand issues. Then the author (al-Maydani) adds his own comment: these reports are from reality and experience, and people are too intelligent to praise something without seeing its beneficial effects. He then provides a personal experiential testimony from Ahmad Khayri, a student of al-Kawthari, who relates that he recited Mukhtasar al-Quduri upon al-Kawthari, who was a pious teacher, and after completion, al-Kawthari prayed for him and wrote an ijazah, and Allah made his provision easy in a blessed way. This passage serves as a testimony to the barakah of the matn and encourages students to approach it with reverence and seek its blessings.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh matn by Imam al-Quduri, described in this text as a blessed book whose recitation brings barakah and ease in provision.
البركة (al-barakah): Divine blessing that brings increase and goodness, demonstrated here through experiential reports of ease in provision and safety from poverty after reciting the matn.
المجربات (al-mujarrabat): Things that have been experimentally proven through repeated experience, used here to describe the verified effects of reciting Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory to recite it during plague.
B) Memorizing it protects from poverty.
C) It contains exactly 10,000 issues.
D) Only scholars can read it.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is celebrated in the Hanafi tradition as a source of barakah, with multiple experiential testimonies affirming its spiritual and material benefits.

The Barakah and Manuscript Proliferation of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Anecdotal and historical evidence for the text's barakah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of barakah as applied to classical Hanafi texts and identify the evidence for the widespread acceptance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
The barakah of a text is known through its acceptance and the tangible blessings experienced by its students.

Before we dive into the fiqh rulings of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, it is important to appreciate the place this text holds in the Hanafi tradition. This lesson explores the reports of its barakah (divine blessing) and its astonishing manuscript proliferation — evidence that its value goes beyond mere scholarly content.

Guided Path
1
Understand the concept of barakah in Hanafi tradition
Identify how the Hanafis historically viewed barakah in connection with righteous texts and scholars, especially in seeking provision and protection.
Barakah is not a legal category but a spiritual benefit recognized by the community.
2
Examine the anecdotal evidence from the passage
Read the reports: recitation during plagues, memorization protecting from poverty, the story of Ahmad Khayri reciting under al-Kawthari and subsequent ease of provision.
These are considered 'mujarrabat' (tested experiences) in Hanafi culture.
3
Analyze the manuscript evidence
Note the numbers: 566 copies worldwide, 288 in Sulaymaniyah Library alone. Consider the context of no printing presses.
Such numbers indicate exceptional demand and reverence.
4
Evaluate the counterargument and response
The passage anticipates an objection: perhaps small size caused abundance. The response: many similar-sized books did not achieve this.
This suggests barakah is a distinct factor.
5
Conclude with the testimony of Imam al-Sam'ani
His statement that Allah benefited countless people through this book reinforces the idea of divine acceptance.
This testimony adds scholarly authority to the anecdotal claims.

Source Text

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري
«إن الحنفية يتبركون بقراءته في أيام الوباء، وأن من حفظه يكون أميناً من الفقر، حتى قيل : إن من قرأه على أستاذ صالح، ودعا له عند ختم الكتاب بالبركة، فإنه يكون مالكاً لدراهم على عدد مسائله، وفي بعض شروح المجمع : أنه يشتمل على اثنتي عشر ألف مسألة». اهـ قلت : وهذه الأخبار هي من الواقع والمجربات، والناس أعقل أن يمدحوا ما لم يروا عنده آثار إحسان، كما تقدم قبل قليـل مـن كلام الإمام أحمد بن محمد الرازي، (ت ٥٠٠هـ)
* ومما وقفت عليه من الأخبار المجربة في ذلك، ما ذكره الأستاذ أحمد خيري تلميذ العلامة الكوثري في ترجمته للكوثري، المطبوعة مع المقالات، قال:
ومما قرأته على الكوثري : مَتَنَ القدوري»، وهو كتاب مبارك، تواتر عند الأحناف أنه إذا قُرى على شيخ صالح كان سبباً لتيسير الرزق، ولما لم أجد أصلح من الأستاذ - الكوثري ـ بمصر، وذلك لأني لم أكن عرفتُ يومئذ الأخ الصالح السيد إبراهيم أبي العيون، شيخ معهد المينا حالياً، فقد قرأته عليه سنة ١٣٥٩هـ، ودعا لي في ختامه، وكتب لي الإجازة بخطه، فيسر الله تعالى رزقي تيسيراً لم يكن على بالي، من حل مبارك ، لا شُبهة فيه ولا ريبة، فلله الحمد والشكر والمنة». اهـ
كشف الظنون: مصباح الأنوار في أدعية الليل والنهار».
(۱) ص ٥٩ .

القدوري
۳۱۹
وكانت قراءته للمختصر على العلامة الكوثري في بيت الشيخ في
العباسية، في عشرة مجالس
(1)
* ومن الصور الواقعية لبركة هذا المختصر، أنه انتشر انتشاراً عجيباً في جميع الأمصار والأعصار، وذلك في وقت لم يكن للمطابع وجود أصلاً، فلا تخلو مكتبة من مكتبات العالم، إلا وتجد فيهـا عشرات النسخ المخطوطة من هذا الكتاب، وقد ذكر أصحاب الفهرس الشامل (٣) (٥٦٦) نسخة من هذا الكتاب في العالم.
(۲)
وفي مكتبة السليمانية فقط في اسطنبول من مكتبات تركيا، توجد (۲۸۸) نسخة مخطوطة من مختصر القدوري(٣)، وهكذا لو فتّش الباحث في سائر المكتبات سيجد عدداً كبيراً.
وقد يقول قائل : لعل سبب هذه الكثرة صغر حجمه، وسهولة نسخه، والجواب : أن هذا وارد ، ولكن كم كتاب مثله بحجمه، لكن لم يكتب له القبول والانتشار كما كتب لهذا؟
و
وفي هذا يقول عنه الإمام السمعاني (ت ٥٦٢ هـ) ـ كما تقدم ـ : نفع الله به خلقاً لا يُحصون» (٤) . اهـ
(۱) التحرير الوجيز ص ۱۰۲ ، في إجازته لتلميذه الأستاذ أحمد خيري.

حين راجع لي ما في المكتبة من نسخ للقدوري.

Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
"The Hanafis seek blessing by reciting it during plague days, and whoever memorizes it will be safeguarded from poverty, to the extent that it is said: whoever recites it under a righteous teacher and the teacher prays for him at the completion of the book for blessing, he will own dirhams equal to the number of its issues. And in some commentaries of al-Majma': it contains twelve thousand issues." End. I say: These reports are from reality and experience, and people are too intelligent to praise something without seeing traces of its goodness, as was mentioned shortly before from the words of Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Razi (d. 500 AH).
* Among the reports I have come across regarding such experience is what Professor Ahmad Khayri, student of the scholar al-Kawthari, mentioned in his biography of al-Kawthari printed with the articles. He said:
"Among what I recited to al-Kawthari was 'Matn al-Quduri', and it is a blessed book. It has been widely transmitted among the Hanafis that if it is recited under a righteous teacher, it becomes a means for the facilitation of provision. When I could not find anyone more righteous than the teacher al-Kawthari in Egypt - and that was because I had not yet known the righteous brother Sayyid Ibrahim Abu al-'Uyun, currently the shaykh of the Mina Institute - I recited it to him in the year 1359 AH. He prayed for me at its conclusion and wrote me an ijazah in his hand. Then Allah facilitated my provision in a way I had not imagined, from blessed lawful sources free from any doubt or suspicion. So praise and gratitude belong to Allah." End.
Kashf al-Zunun: Misbah al-Anwar fi Ad'iyat al-Layl wa al-Nahar.
(1) p. 59.

Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
319
And his recitation of the Mukhtasar to the scholar al-Kawthari took place in the shaykh's house in al-Abbasiyyah in ten sessions.
(1)
* Among the real examples of the blessing of this Mukhtasar is that it spread astonishingly throughout all regions and times, at a time when printing presses did not exist at all. Few libraries in the world are devoid of dozens of handwritten copies of this book. The Comprehensive Index authors have mentioned (566) copies of this book in the world.
(2)
In the Sulaymaniyah Library alone in Istanbul, Turkey, there are (288) handwritten copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri (3). Likewise, if a researcher investigates other libraries, he will find a large number.
Someone might say: Perhaps the reason for this abundance is its small size and ease of copying. The answer: This is possible, but how many books of similar size have not been granted acceptance and spread like this one?
And regarding this, Imam al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH) - as previously mentioned - said: "Allah has benefited countless people by it" (4). End.
(1) al-Tahrir al-Wajiz p. 102, in his ijazah to his student Ahmad Khayri.
(2) 9/305 - 343
(3) As communicated to me by the noble brother, His Excellency Dr. Shaykh Khalil Qutlay, may Allah preserve him, when he reviewed the copies of al-Quduri in the library for me.
(4) al-Jawahir al-Mudiyyah 6/1, 247, quoting from him.
Source pages p. 318

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion about the barakah (blessing) and historical spread of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author presents multiple anecdotal reports to emphasize the spiritual benefits and wide acceptance of the book. First, he quotes a reported tradition that Hanafis recite it during plagues and that memorizing it protects from poverty. A more specific anecdote from Ahmad Khayri, a student of the well-known Hanafi scholar al-Kawthari, testifies that reciting the text under a righteous teacher leads to the facilitation of provision (rizq). The author then provides tangible evidence of the book's popularity: the large number of manuscript copies worldwide, specifically 566 copies in the Comprehensive Index and 288 in the Sulaymaniyah Library alone. He anticipates and refutes the objection that the book's small size caused its proliferation, noting that many similarly sized books did not achieve the same acceptance. He concludes with the testimony of Imam al-Sam'ani that Allah has benefited countless people through it. The style is that of a teacher establishing the credibility and blessed nature of the text before delving into its juridical content.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh primer by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely memorized and used as a foundational text in the Hanafi school.
البركة (al-barakah): Spiritual blessing from Allah that brings increase in goodness and sustenance, often associated with righteous deeds and texts.
المجربات (al-mujarrabat): Tested experiences; reports of practices that have been observed to yield positive spiritual or material results.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) 288
C) 12,000
D) 102

Key Takeaway
The barakah of Mukhtasar al-Quduri is evidenced by experiential reports and its extraordinary manuscript proliferation, confirming its special acceptance among Hanafis.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Widespread Acceptance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Discussion of the unprecedented spread and number of manuscripts of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the historical phenomenon of the widespread acceptance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, citing specific evidence such as manuscript counts and the testimony of Imam al-Sam'ani.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri spread miraculously across centuries due to divine baraka, not just its small size.

This lesson explores the remarkable history of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh manual. Despite the absence of printing presses, it spread to every corner of the Muslim world with hundreds of manuscript copies. The passage attributes this to divine blessing (baraka) and refutes the idea that it was simply due to its small size. Understanding this history helps us appreciate the authority and centrality of this text in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phenomenon
The passage describes an extraordinary spread of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. What is the phenomenon and what evidence is given?
2
Analyze the evidence
Look at the manuscript counts (566 worldwide, 288 in Suleymaniyya). What does this tell us?
3
Examine the counterargument
The author considers that small size might cause spread. Why does he reject this explanation?
4
Understand the concept of baraka
How does the author use the concept of divine blessing to explain the book's acceptance?
5
Connect to authority
How does this historical evidence strengthen the status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi school?

 وفي مكتبة السليمانية فقط في اسطنبول من مكتبات تركيا، توجد (۲۸۸) نسخة مخطوطة من مختصر القدوري، وهكذا لو فتّش الباحث في سائر المكتبات سيجد عدداً كبيراً. 
 وقد يقول قائل : لعل سبب هذه الكثرة صغر حجمه، وسهولة نسخه، والجواب : أن هذا وارد، ولكن كم كتاب مثله بحجمه، لكن لم يكتب له القبول والانتشار كما كتب لهذا؟

Chapter Two: Study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. And his reading of the Mukhtasar to the scholar al-Kawthari in the sheikh's house in al-Abbasiyya, in ten sessions. Among the actual manifestations of the blessing of this Mukhtasar is that it spread miraculously in all regions and eras, at a time when there were no printing presses at all. No library in the world is empty of dozens of manuscript copies of this book. The authors of the Comprehensive Index mentioned (566) copies of this book in the world. In the Suleymaniyya Library alone in Istanbul, Turkey, there are (288) manuscript copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Similarly, if a researcher searches in other libraries, he will find a large number. Someone might say: perhaps the reason for this abundance is its small size and ease of copying. The answer: this is possible, but how many books of similar size have not achieved the acceptance and spread that this one did? On this, Imam al-Sam'ani (d. 562 AH) said about it—as previously mentioned: 'Allah benefited innumerable people through it.' End.
Source pages p. 319

Commentary
This passage is a biographical discussion of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, focusing on its extraordinary spread and acceptance. The author notes that despite the absence of printing presses during the time of al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), the book spread massively, with hundreds of manuscript copies found worldwide. He cites specific numbers: 566 copies recorded in the Comprehensive Index and 288 in the Suleymaniyya Library alone. The author then addresses a potential objection: that the book's small size made it easy to copy. He counters by pointing out that many books of similar size did not achieve such widespread acceptance, thus attributing it to the book's inherent blessing (baraka). He supports this with the testimony of Imam al-Sam'ani, who stated that Allah benefited countless people through this book. This passage serves to establish the authority and significance of the Mukhtasar as a foundational text for Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual authored by Abu al-Hasan Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text for the Hanafi madhhab.
بركة (baraka): Spiritual blessing and divine favor that caused the book to be widely accepted and preserved.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri's unprecedented spread across regions and eras is a testament to its divine blessing (baraka) and forms the basis of its authority in the Hanafi school.

The Baraka of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Speed of Copying and Ease of Memorization
Anecdotes illustrating the baraka of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state two specific manifestations of baraka associated with Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain their significance for Hanafi learning.

Core Idea
Allah facilitated copying and memorization of al-Quduri, making it the cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh education.

The Mukhtasar al-Quduri is not just a legal text; its acceptance and widespread use are considered a divine blessing. This lesson presents two remarkable anecdotes that illustrate this baraka: a scholar copying the entire book in a single day, and the text becoming the most memorized Hanafi primer. These stories highlight the unique role of this work in the Hanafi tradition.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two anecdotes of baraka
Read the passage and list the two specific events described: the copying feat and the widespread memorization.
One involves a specific scholar, the other is a general phenomenon.
2
Analyze the first anecdote: copying in one day
Consider why the author finds this remarkable. What does it say about the book's size and the scribe's ability? The author explicitly calls it a baraka.
The speed is attributed to baraka, not just skill.
3
Analyze the second anecdote: ease of memorization
Note the quote from Ibn Kathir and the scholars of the madhhab. How does this establish the book's central role in Hanafi education?
Memorization became a hallmark of the text itself.
4
Connect to the broader Hanafi tradition
Reflect on how these anecdotes explain the enduring use of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as the standard beginner text for Hanafi fiqh.
This book is still widely taught today.

ومن الأخبار النادرة التي وقفتُ عليها في تيسير نسخه لبركته، ما ذكره صاحب الشقائق النعمانية في ترجمة العالم العامل، الفاضل الكامل المولى إلياس بن إبراهيم السينابي، من علماء القرن التاسع الهجري، وله عدة مصنفات منها شرح الفقه الأكبر، قال في ترجمته : وكان خطه حسناً جداً، وكان سريع الكتابة، سمعت من والدي أنه كتب مختصر القدوري في الفقه في يوم واحد» . اهـ وهذا من بركة هذا الكتاب، فإنه لا يتأتى نسخه في مثل هذا الوقت. ومن بركة هذا المختصر أيضاً أن الله يسر حفظه للطلبة ممن يريد أن يتفقه على مذهب أبي حنيفة النعمان، حتى صار سمةً ووصفاً يوصف به هذا المختصر، فقد قال الحافظ ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية في ترجمة القدوري : صاحب المصنف المختصر الذي يُحفظ كثيراً» . اهـ وهكذا قال علماء المذهب : إن كتاب الشيخ الإمام القدوري كثر استعماله، وحاز من القبول سهماً، وتوفّرت الدواعي إلى الاعتناء به حفظاً وفهماً ...» . اهـ
Among the rare reports I have come across regarding the facilitation of copying it due to its blessing, is what the author of al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya mentioned in the biography of the pious scholar, the virtuous and perfect master, Mulla Ilyas ibn Ibrahim al-Sinabi, one of the scholars of the ninth century AH. He had several works, including a commentary on al-Fiqh al-Akbar. He said in his biography: 'His handwriting was very good, and he wrote quickly. I heard from my father that he wrote Mukhtasar al-Quduri in fiqh in one day.' End. This is from the blessing of this book, for it is not possible to copy it in such a time. And from the blessing of this Mukhtasar also is that Allah facilitated its memorization for students who wish to gain understanding of the madhhab of Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, so much so that it became a hallmark and description of this Mukhtasar. Indeed, al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir said in al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya in the biography of al-Quduri: 'The author of the concise work that is much memorized.' End. Similarly, the scholars of the madhhab said: 'The book of Shaykh Imam al-Quduri is widely used, attained a share of acceptance, and there were many motivations to take care of it in memorization and understanding...' End.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on the blessings of Mukhtasar al-Quduri by presenting two specific anecdotes. First, it reports that Mulla Ilyas al-Sinabi was able to copy the entire Mukhtasar in a single day due to his fast handwriting—something remarkable for a book of this length. The author emphasizes that this is a manifestation of baraka. Second, the passage highlights that Allah facilitated the memorization of this book for students of the Hanafi madhhab, to the extent that it became famously known as 'the book that is much memorized' (al-mukhtasar alladhi yuhfazu kathiran), as quoted from Ibn Kathir. The passage concludes with a general statement from Hanafi scholars affirming the widespread acceptance and care devoted to this book in terms of memorization and understanding. These anecdotes serve to establish the book's central role in Hanafi education and its divinely blessed nature.

Key Terms
الشقائق النعمانية (al-Shaqa'iq al-Nu'maniyya): A biographical dictionary of Ottoman scholars by Tashkopruzade (d. 968 AH).
البداية والنهاية (al-Bidaya wa al-Nihaya): A universal history by Ibn Kathir (d. 774 AH).
بركة (baraka): Divine blessing or positive spiritual energy that increases benefit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is the most widely used book in fiqh.
B) It is a concise work that is much memorized.
C) It was copied in one day by a scholar.
D) It has no equal in the Hanafi school.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is considered blessed because Allah facilitated its copying and memorization, making it the central text for Hanafi learning.

The Blessings of Memorizing Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Praising the book and recounting its memorization by scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the blessings of Mukhtasar al-Quduri described in the passage and identify the role of memorization (hifdh) in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri was memorized by generations of Hanafi scholars, a testament to its barakah and foundational role.

This passage is not a legal ruling but a front-matter celebration of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It reveals how the Hanafi school revered this concise text, making its memorization a hallmark of scholarship. Understanding this context helps appreciate the text's authority and the importance placed on oral transmission in the madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the blessing highlighted
Read the first sentence: 'And from the blessings of this Mukhtasar is also that Allah facilitated its memorization...' Recognize that the author presents hifdh as a divine gift.
2
Note the scholarly citations
The author quotes Ibn Kathir, scholars of the madhhab, al-Marjani, al-Qurashi, al-Abbasi, and al-Sakhawi. Understand that this chain of authorities reinforces the book's stature.
Al-Sakhawi counted over forty scholars who memorized it.
3
Observe the social practice
The passage ends with parents giving gifts to encourage memorization. Reflect on how this created a culture of learning.
This shows the book's integration into family life.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن بركة هذا المختصر أيضاً أن الله يسر حفظه للطلبـة مـمـن يريد أن يتفقه على مذهب أبي حنيفة النعمان، حتى صار سمةً ووصفاً يوصف به هذا المختصر، فقد قال الحافظ ابن كثير في البداية والنهاية في ترجمة القدوري : صاحب المصنف المختـصـر الـذي كثر يُحفظ». اهـ وهكذا قال علماء المذهب : إن كتاب الشيخ الإمام القدوري استعماله، وحاز من القبول سهماً، وتوفّرت الدواعي إلى الاعتناء بـه حفظاً وفهماً ...» (٣) . اهـ بل قال الشهاب المرجاني حين ذكر مختصر القدوري، واهتمام الحنفية به قال: أولعوا فيه حفظاً، ورواية...» (۱). اهـ * وممن كان يحفظه : ما ذكره الإمام القرشي صاحب الجواهر المضية أن والده كان يحفظ هذا المختصر، وكذلك كان يحفظه أخوه الشقيق، وكان يحفظه هو. كما كان يحفظه الإمام شهاب الدين أحمد بن محمد العباسي، المتوفى سنة ٨٩٠هـ، كما صرح هو في مقدمة كتابه: «العقـود المفصلة في الجمع بين القدوري والتكملة». بل عد السخاوي في كتابه الضوء اللامع أكثر من أربعين مترجمـاً كان يحفظ مختصر القدوري. وهكذا كان الآباء يشجعون أبناءهم على حفظه، ويكثرون لهم العطاء والهدايا في مقابل ذلك. فقد جاء في معجم الأدباء لياقوت الحموي ، في ترجمة مؤرّخ مدينة حلب الشهباء المحدّث كمال الدين ابن العديم عمر بن أحمد
And from the blessings of this Mukhtasar is also that Allah facilitated its memorization for students among those who wish to gain fiqh according to the madhhab of Abu Hanifa al-Nu'man, until it became a distinguishing mark and description by which this Mukhtasar is described. Al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir said in al-Bidayah wa al-Nihayah in the biography of al-Quduri: 'The author of the concise work that is frequently memorized.' And thus said the scholars of the madhhab: 'Indeed the book of Shaykh Imam al-Quduri has been used extensively, gained acceptance, and there were many incentives to care for it in memorization and understanding.' Moreover, al-Shihab al-Marjani, when mentioning Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the Hanafis' dedication to it, said: 'They were devoted to memorizing it and transmitting it.' And among those who memorized it: al-Imam al-Qurashi, author of al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah, mentioned that his father memorized this Mukhtasar, and likewise his full brother memorized it, and he himself memorized it. Also, al-Imam Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abbasi (d. 890 AH) memorized it, as he stated in the introduction to his book 'al-Uqud al-Mufassalah fi al-Jam' bayna al-Quduri wa al-Takmilah.' Furthermore, al-Sakhawi in his book al-Daw' al-Lami' counted more than forty biographical subjects who memorized Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Thus fathers would encourage their sons to memorize it and would give them abundant gifts and rewards in return. This is found in Mu'jam al-Udaba' by Yaqut al-Hamawi, in the biography of the historian of the city of Aleppo, the muhaddith Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Adim Umar ibn Ahmad.
Source pages p. 320

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion about the unique blessings of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author begins by highlighting another blessing of this book: Allah made its memorization easy for students who wish to study Hanafi fiqh, to the point that the book itself became a hallmark — if someone is described as having memorized al-Quduri, that indicates their knowledge. The author then cites al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir, who in his biographical dictionary described al-Quduri as 'the author of the concise work that is frequently memorized.' This indicates the widespread practice of memorizing this text. The author then quotes scholars of the madhhab who affirmed the extensive use and acceptance of the book, noting the keen interest in memorizing and understanding it. Next, al-Shihab al-Marjani is quoted: 'They were devoted to memorizing it and transmitting it' — showing how Hanafis loved this book. The passage then provides specific examples of scholars who memorized it: Imam al-Qurashi (author of al-Jawahir al-Mudi'ah) mentions that his father, his brother, and he himself memorized it; Shihab al-Din Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Abbasi (d. 890 AH) also memorized it; and al-Sakhawi counted over forty scholars in his biographical work who memorized this Mukhtasar. Finally, a social custom is mentioned: parents would encourage their children to memorize it by offering rewards and gifts, as exemplified in the biography of Kamal al-Din Ibn al-Adim from Yaqut al-Hamawi's dictionary. This passage underscores the central role of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi tradition as a foundational text for memorization and study.

Key Terms
بركة (barakah): Divine blessing that causes a small thing to bring much good and facilitate ease.
حفظ (hifdh): Memorization of a text verbatim, a traditional method of learning in Islamic education.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Hafiz Ibn Kathir say about Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) It was written in one day
B) It is the most comprehensive Hanafi text
C) It is frequently memorized
D) It has many commentaries

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri's barakah is manifested in Allah making its memorization easy for students, turning it into a defining feature of Hanafi scholarship.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Veneration of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi Tradition
Biographical anecdotes praising Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to summarize the significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as evidenced by anecdotes of memorization, divine preservation, and prophetic dream, and explain how these reinforce its central role in Hanafi education.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is divinely preserved and central to Hanafi learning, as shown by memorization rewards, karama, and prophetic dreams.

This lesson presents historical anecdotes from the introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri, demonstrating the high esteem the Hanafi school holds for this text. Through stories of memorization incentives, a post-Hajj miracle, and a dream of the Prophet (SAW), we see how the book's baraka and reliability became legendary. These narratives are not intended as rigorous historical proofs but as expressions of the text's revered status.

Guided Path
1
Identify each anecdote
Locate the three main stories: the father offering money for memorization, al-Quduri's Hajj prayer for errors, and the dream of the Prophet requesting the book.
The anecdotes appear in sequence: (1) memorization incentive, (2) qadi memorizing a commentary, (3) al-Halabi tested by a Shafi'i, and (4) the miracle and dream.
2
Understand the purpose of each story
The memorization story highlights the text's primacy in traditional Hanafi education. The Hajj story suggests divine approval of the Mukhtasar's accuracy. The dream elevates the status of those who teach and transmit the book.
These are not legal proofs but hagiographic accounts that build reverence.
3
Recognize the culture of memorization (hifz)
The anecdote about the son memorizing al-Lum'a and al-Quduri for monetary reward reflects the classical method of learning: memorization before commentary. This shows the text's accessibility and importance.
Memorization was a common pedagogical tool; al-Quduri was a standard text for Hanafi fiqh.
4
Analyze the miracle (karama) of error erasure
Al-Quduri found erased spots after praying for error revelation. This is presented as a karama (divine favor) confirming the book's correctness. Consider how such stories reinforce confidence in the text.
Karama stories are common in Islamic tradition for saints (awliya).
5
Evaluate the dream as a legitimizing device
The dream involves the Prophet (SAW), Abu Bakr, and Umar honoring the father of the dreamer and requesting the Mukhtasar. Dreams of the Prophet are considered truthful in Islam, thus powerfully endorsing the book's status.
This dream is recorded in biographical works, emphasizing the text's spiritual value.

Page 322 Chapter Two: Study about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Ibn Hibba Allah, died 660 AH, said Yaqut: Kamal al-Din narrated to me - may Allah perpetuate his highness - he said: My father said to me: Memorize al-Lum'a until I give you such and such, so I memorized it and recited it to the shaykh of Aleppo at that time, al-Diya' ibn Dahn al-Asa. Then he said to me: Memorize 'al-Quduri' until I grant you such and such dirhams, also a lot, so I memorized it in a short period. (A) Even greater than this is what al-Qurashi mentioned in the biography of Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Muslim al-Qadi al-Maragh, died 563 AH, that he memorized the Sharh Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta'. Similar to this is the report that came in the biography of Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Halabi, one of the Hanafi jurists of the eighth century AH (his death date not mentioned), that he memorized the book al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani in his youth, and presented it to the scholar Ibn al-Wardi the Shafi'i jurist. He tested him with it and was impressed, and wrote him a good ijazah in 744 AH. (4) Similarly, al-Sakhawi mentioned in the biography of Abd al-Rahman ibn Ubayd Allah al-Ardabili, died 811 AH, that he used to memorize the book al-Badi' in usul al-fiqh by Ibn al-Sa'ati, and al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani. The Error: The honor that Allah granted to al-Quduri in the soundness of his Mukhtasar. Al-Ayni said: I heard from some senior teachers: Al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, when he performed Hajj, took the Mukhtasar with him. When he finished his tawaf, he asked Allah to show him any error or mistake that had occurred from his pen. Then he opened the Mukhtasar and turned it page by page to the end, and found in it five or six places that were erased. This is considered a miracle. End. Among the righteous dreams that foretell the great status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: What the Hanafi jurist Siraj al-Din Abu Bakr ibn al-Hanafi Ali ibn Musa al-Hamli al-Yamani (d. 769 AH) saw. He saw the Prophet, peace and blessings be upon him, and Abu Bakr and Umar, may Allah be pleased with them, standing in a circle of people near his father's mosque. He said: O Abu Bakr and O Umar, stand and kiss the head of the jurist Ali ibn Musa, for I love him. So they stood and kissed his head. Then the Prophet asked for 'Kitab al-Quduri'. So a copy was brought to him, and he (the father) read from it before him. End.
Source pages p. 322

Commentary
This passage is from the introductory study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It narrates several historical anecdotes underscoring the significance and reverence of this foundational Hanafi text. The first anecdote tells of a father encouraging his son to memorize al-Quduri with a monetary reward, demonstrating its priority in traditional education. The second mentions a qadi who memorized a commentary on the Mukhtasar, showing its scholarly depth. The third relates a Hanafi jurist memorizing al-Hidayah, another major text. Then comes the story of Imam al-Quduri himself: after Hajj, he prayed to discover any errors in his book and found five or six erased spots—seen as a divine sign of its correctness (karama). Finally, a dream is recounted where the Prophet Muhammad (SAW) requested the book, even having Abu Bakr and Umar kiss the father of the dreamer, indicating the high station of those who transmit and honor this work. These stories collectively emphasize the blessed nature of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and its central place in Hanafi learning.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh text by Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely memorized and commented upon.
كرامة (karama): A miracle or supernatural favor granted to a saint (wali) as a sign of divine pleasure.

The Sanctity of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and the Absence of a Preface
Biographical accounts and textual analysis of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of the miraculous preservation of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar and identify the implications of its lack of a preface for studying Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Allah preserved al-Quduri's Mukhtasar from error, and its missing preface means its method must be inferred.

This passage presents two extraordinary accounts that establish the spiritual stature of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, followed by a critical observation: the author did not write a preface. As a student of Hanafi fiqh, understanding these details helps you appreciate the work's authority and the need to study it with supplementary commentaries. The stories of divine protection and a visionary encounter with the Prophet underline that this is no ordinary textbook but a blessed legacy.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the two accounts of preservation
Read the story from al-Ayni and the vision of Siraj al-Din. Note how each establishes the Mukhtasar's sanctity.
The first is a miracle (karama), the second a righteous dream (ru'ya sāliha).
2
Identify the absence of a preface
The passage explains that no manuscript includes a preface; the book starts directly with the wudu verse. Understand that this is unusual.
Most authors include a preface outlining methodology and sources.
3
Reflect on the implication for study
Since there is no preface, students must rely on commentaries and internal clues to understand al-Quduri's methodology.
Commentaries like al-Lubab serve as essential guides.
