الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

عبيد الله الأردبيلي، المتوفى سنة ٨١١هـ ، أنه كان يحفظ كتاب «البديع» في أصول الفقه لابن الساعاتي، و«الهداية» للمرغيناني.

الخطأ :
إكرام الله تعالى للقدوري في سلامة مختصره من قال الإمام العيني(۱): «سمعتُ من بعض الأساتذة الكبار يقول: إن القدوري رحمه الله لما حج أخذ المختصر معه، ولما فرغ من طوافه ، سأل الله سبحانه أن يُوقِفَه على خطأ فيه، أو سهو منه وقع عن قلم.
ثم إنه فَتَحَ المختصر، وتصفّحه ورقة ورقة إلى آخره، فوجـد فيـه خمسة مواضع ، أو ستة مواضع مَمْحُوَّة ، وهذا يُعد من كرامته». اهـ

ومن المرائي الصالحة المبشرة بعظيم شأن مختصر القدوري : ما رآه الفقيه الحنفي سراج الدين أبو بكر ابن الفقيه الحنفي علي بن موسى الهاملي اليمني (ت ٧٦٩ هـ) ، رأى النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم وأبا بكر وعمر الله عنهما قائمين في حلقة من الناس عند مسجد والده، فقال : يا أبا بكر ويا عمر قوما فقبلا رأس الفقيه علي بن موسى، أحبُّه، فقاما وقبلا رأسه، ثم طلب النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم «كتاب الـقــدوري»، فأحضرت له نسخة ،والدي وقرأت بين يديه منها (٢). اهـ

(۱) في البناية ١٢٧/٥ (ط باكستان).
(۲) كما في إرغام أولياء الشيطان للمناوي ٤٧٧/٤، وتنظر ترجمة ووالده في هدية العارفين ٢٣٥/١ ، كشف الظنون ١٨٦٨/٢ ، الأعلام ٦٧/٢.

المبحث الثالث
منهج الإمام القدوري وأسلوبه في مختصره

بيان أن القدوري لم يكتب مقدمة لمختصره :
يغلب على الظن أن الإمام القدوري رحمه الله لم يكتب مقدمـةً لمختصره في الفقه، والتي كان يمكن من خلالها التعرف على خطة عمله فيه، ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، والمصادر التي استقى منها معلومات هذا الكتاب ونحو هذا مما يذكره المؤلفون عادة في مقدمات كتبهم. ومن هنا لم نستطع التعرف على شيءٍ من ذلك إلا عن طريق الدراسة، وما يلمحه الباحث المتأمل فيه.
وإن عدم وجود مقدمة لهذا المختصر مما أجمعت عليه نُسَخ هذا المختصر المخطوطة والمطبوعة، وذلك حسب استقرائي لعشرات النسخ . منه، ولعشرات من شروحه التي ضمت هذا المختصر . وهكذا، فالنسخ كلها تبدأ بعد البسملة، وبعـد عنـوان: (كتـاب الطهارة، تبدأ بآية الوضوء التي افتتح بها القدوري مختصره، ثم يأتي ذكر فرائض الوضوء، وهكذا إلى تمام نهاية المختصر، دون أن تُذكر له أي مقدمة.
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. ... The error: Allah's honoring al-Quduri in the soundness of his Mukhtasar from error. Al-Ayni said: 'I heard from some great teachers: When al-Quduri performed Hajj, he took the Mukhtasar with him, and after finishing his circumambulation, he asked Allah to show him an error or mistake that had slipped from his pen. Then he opened the Mukhtasar and leafed through it page by page until the end, and found in it five or six erased places, and this is considered a miracle from him.' ... And among the righteous visions foretelling the great status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: what the Hanafi jurist Siraj al-Din Abu Bakr ... saw: he saw the Prophet ... and Abu Bakr and Umar standing... then the Prophet requested the 'Kitab al-Quduri' ... Third Topic: The Method of Imam al-Quduri and His Style in His Mukhtasar. Statement that al-Quduri did not write a preface for his Mukhtasar: It is most likely that Imam al-Quduri did not write a preface for his Mukhtasar on fiqh, through which one could have known his plan, his method, and his sources. Therefore we cannot know anything about that except through study and what the researcher may infer. The absence of a preface is agreed upon by all manuscript and printed copies of this Mukhtasar, based on my survey of dozens of copies and dozens of commentaries that contain this Mukhtasar. Thus, all copies begin after the Basmala and after the title 'Kitab al-Tahara' with the verse of wudu with which al-Quduri began his Mukhtasar, then the obligations of wudu are mentioned, and so on until the end, without any preface.
Source pages p. 323

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and textual study of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It opens with two accounts highlighting the book's sanctity and miraculous preservation. The first, from al-Ayni, narrates that al-Quduri himself, after Hajj, prayed to be shown any error, and found several erased spots—indicating divine protection. The second is a dream vision where the Prophet Muhammad (peace be upon him) honors the book by requesting it. These stories establish the high esteem of the Mukhtasar in the Hanafi tradition. The passage then transitions to a critical analysis: al-Quduri did not write a preface, which is unusual for a scholarly work. The author confirms this by examining numerous manuscripts and commentaries. As a result, the Mukhtasar begins abruptly with the verse on wudu (Quran 5:6) and the list of fara'id al-wudu (obligatory acts of ablution). This insight is important for students because it means the work's methodology must be inferred rather than read explicitly. The passage underscores the reliance on oral tradition and the careful study of the text itself to understand its structure.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied and commented upon.
كرامة (karama): A divine miracle bestowed upon a righteous servant (wali), in this case, the preservation of al-Quduri's book from error.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Quduri find when he opened his Mukhtasar after praying for guidance during Hajj?
A) A complete list of errors needing correction
B) Five or six erased places, indicating divine protection
C) A preface he had forgotten to include
D) Additional chapters he had not written

Key Takeaway
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, preserved by divine will and lacking a preface, remains a cornerstone of Hanafi fiqh study.

Introduction and Front Matter

The Correct Attribution of a Famous Hanafi Praise
Historical correction of a famous praise attribution

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the actual source of the famous praise 'Man hafiza hadha al-kitab...' and explain why it is not from Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Core Idea
The well-known praise belongs to Al-Jami' al-Saghir, not Mukhtasar al-Quduri, as proven by chronological evidence.

You may have heard the high praise: 'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizing of our companions, and whoever understands it is the most understanding.' Many attribute this to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, but the evidence shows otherwise. This lesson clarifies the correct source and dispels a common misconception in Hanafi history.

Guided Path
1
Identify the famous praise
Recognize the statement: 'Man hafiza hadha al-kitab fahuwa ahfaz ashabina, wa man fahimahu fahuwa afham ashabina.' This is the key phrase in question.
This praise is also found in some modern introductions to the Mukhtasar.
2
Examine the chronological discrepancy
Note that Abu Ali al-Shashi (d. 344 AH) died before al-Quduri was born (born 362 AH). He could not have praised al-Quduri's work. Therefore, the original attribution is impossible.
Al-Quduri was born about 18 years after al-Shashi's death.
3
Trace the correct source in Kashf al-Zunun
Kashf al-Zunun (by Hajji Khalifa) states that this praise was said by Ali al-Razi regarding Al-Jami' al-Saghir of Imam Muhammad, not al-Quduri's Mukhtasar.
The same wording is used for Al-Jami' al-Saghir, with an additional practice: judges were tested on their memorization of it.
4
Conclude the correct attribution
The praise belongs to Al-Jami' al-Saghir, a foundational text by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. The misattribution to al-Quduri arose due to later copyists or commentators who confused the two texts.
This correction does not diminish the status of Mukhtasar al-Quduri; it is also a highly esteemed work.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري وقد كان أبو علي الشاشي ) يقول : مَن حَفِظَ هذا الكتاب : فهـو أحفظ أصحابنا، ومن فهمه : فهو أفهم أصحابنا. وهو كتاب مختلف الترتيب؛ لأنه ابتدأه على أن يكون كتاباً ثم زاد فيه بعد مضي العبادات، فلما تجاوز (الرهن)، بَسَطَ صغيراً، بسطاً مستوفياً. وقد عمدت على إملاء كتاب جامع في شرحه، أعتمد فيـه بيــان الفروع والروايات، وأورد فيه من مسائل الخلاف ما يحصل (يستقل) وهذا الخطأ هو الذي جعل البعض يقول إن القدوري كتب مقدمة لمختصره، ومنها هذه الجملة في الثناء على المختصر . (۱) ترجم صاحب الجواهر المضية ٢٦٢/١ لأحمد بن محمد أبي علي الشاشي تلميذ الكرخي وأنه توفي سنة ٣٤٤هـ ، وقد ولد القدوري سنة ٣٦٢هـ، وعلى هذا فقد ولد بعد وفاة الشاشي هذا بنحو ١٨ سنة، وعليه يبعد تماماً أن يقـول الرازي هذا ما تقدم من الثناء على مختصر القدوري. وقد جعل كثيرون خطأ هذه المقولة في الثناء على مختصر القدوري، مع أن الشاشي المذكور هو قبل القدوري. ومما يؤكد أن هذه المقولة ليست في مختصر القدوري، أن صاحب كشف الظنون ٥٦١/١ حين ذكر كتاب «الجامع الصغير»، للإمام محمد بن الحسن، ذكرهـا الثناء عليه، فقال: «وكان علي الرازي يقول : من فهم هذا الكتاب : فهو أفهـم أصحابنا، ومن حفظه : كان أحفظ أصحابنا، وأن المتقدمين من مشايخنا كانوا لا يقلدون أحداً القضاء حتى يمتحنوه، فإن حفظه : قلدوه، وإلا أمروه بالحفظ. اهـ. ويظهر أن حسام الدين الرازي قال هذا الثناء أيضاً في شرحه على الجامع الصغير كما قالها الشاشي، وزاد عليها ، وفي الأعلام ۲٥٦/٤ أن لعلي الرازي هذا شرحاً على الجامع الصغير، وأن منه جزءاً أو قطعة في شستربتي (٣٣١٦). الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري ۳۲۷ به مزيد بسط ؛ لأني استوفيت ذلك في كتاب: «التجريد»، وأُلحـق بفروعه ما يليق بها، ليعتدل أول الكتاب وآخره في الاستيفاء، ثم ألحق به ما أغفله من الكتب، وأستوفي شرح جميعه، وأُقدم على ذلك مسألة في تقديم قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في الجملة على سائر فقهاء الأمصار...الخ». اهـ من كشف الظنون. فهذا الكلام في تكملة القدوري وشرحها، للرازي، كما بينت أسفل في الحاشية، لا في مختصر القدوري، والله أعلم. * أما عن عمل القدوري في المختصر، ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، فقد جَمَعَ الإمام القدوري في مختصره هذا المسائل المحتاج إليهـا، واستوعب ما يكثر وقوعه، مع ذكره القول المعتمد فيهـا، المختار للفتوى، وبذا صار مختصره خالياً عن الزوائد المملة، والاختصارات المخلة. كما ضم هذا المختصر أبواب الفقه كلها، وختمها القدوري بالفرائض وأحكام المواريث. ويُذكّر هنا، أن الإمام المرغيناني صاحب الهداية، لما جَمَعَ بين مختصر القدوري والجامع الصغير في بداية المبتدي، اعتمد ترتيب الجامع الصغير وأبوابه، ولم يعتمد ترتيب القدوري، ولما كان الجامع الصغير خالياً من كتاب المواريث خلا كتاب بداية المبتدي منه ، وكذلك أيضاً جاء كتاب الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي خالياً منه أيضاً. - وهكذا كان من عمل القدوري في مختصره أنه عَرَض الخلاف أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد، وأحياناً يذكر بين
Chapter Two: A Study of the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri. Abu Ali al-Shashi used to say: 'Whoever memorizes this book is the most memorizing of our companions, and whoever understands it is the most understanding of our companions.' It is a book of varying arrangement; because he began it as a book, then added to it after the section on acts of worship. When he passed (al-rahn), he expanded it concisely, a comprehensive expansion. I intended to dictate a comprehensive book in its commentary, relying in it on the exposition of branches and narrations, and I include in it issues of disagreement that suffice. This error is what made some say that al-Quduri wrote an introduction to his Mukhtasar, and among it is this sentence praising the Mukhtasar. (1) The author of al-Jawahir al-Mudi'a translated Ahmad ibn Muhammad Abu Ali al-Shashi, the student of al-Karkhi, and that he died in 344 AH, while al-Quduri was born in 362 AH. Based on this, he was born after the death of this al-Shashi by about 18 years, so it is extremely unlikely that al-Razi said this preceding praise of the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri. Many have mistakenly placed this statement as praise for the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, while that al-Shashi is before al-Quduri. Confirming that this statement is not in the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri is that the author of Kashf al-Zunun, when mentioning the book 'al-Jami' al-Saghir' by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan, mentioned praise of it, saying: 'Ali al-Razi used to say: Whoever understands this book is the most understanding of our companions, and whoever memorizes it is the most memorizing of our companions, and that the early scholars among our teachers would not appoint anyone as judge until they examined him; if he memorized it, they appointed him, otherwise they ordered him to memorize it.' End quote. It appears that Husam al-Din al-Razi said this praise also in his commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir as al-Shashi said it, and added to it. In al-A'lam, it is stated that Ali al-Razi has a commentary on al-Jami' al-Saghir, and that a part or section of it is in Chester Beatty (3316). Chapter Two: A Study of the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri 327 with more expansion; because I covered that fully in the book 'al-Tajrid', and I appended to its branches what befits them, so that the beginning and end of the book are balanced in comprehensiveness, then I appended to it what he omitted of books, and I cover the commentary of all of it, and I preface that with an issue regarding giving precedence to the statement of Abu Hanifa, may Allah have mercy on him, in general over other jurists of the regions... etc.' End quote from Kashf al-Zunun. So this speech is in the completion of al-Quduri and its commentary, by al-Razi, as indicated below in the footnote, not in the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri, and Allah knows best. * As for the work of al-Quduri in the Mukhtasar and his methodology that he followed: Imam al-Quduri gathered in this Mukhtasar of his the needed issues, and covered those that frequently occur, while mentioning the relied-upon opinion in them, the chosen one for fatwa. Thus his Mukhtasar became free from tedious additions and deficient abbreviations. This Mukhtasar also included all chapters of fiqh, and al-Quduri concluded it with fara'id and inheritance rulings. It is noted here that Imam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidaya, when he combined the Mukhtasar of al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, adopted the arrangement of al-Jami' al-Saghir and its chapters, and did not adopt the arrangement of al-Quduri. Since al-Jami' al-Saghir lacked the book of inheritance, the book Bidayat al-Mubtadi lacked it, and likewise the book al-Hidaya, the commentary of Bidayat al-Mubtadi, also lacked it. - And such was the work of al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar: he presented the disagreement among the imams of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and sometimes he mentions between.
Source pages p. 326

Commentary
This passage is a front matter study of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. It begins by quoting a famous praise from Abu Ali al-Shashi about a book that is memorized and understood, noting that this statement is often mistakenly attributed to the Mukhtasar. The author then clarifies that al-Shashi died before al-Quduri was born, so he could not have praised al-Quduri's work; the praise actually belongs to al-Jami' al-Saghir by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, as confirmed by Kashf al-Zunun. The author then discusses al-Quduri's methodology: he compiled essential issues, mentioned the relied-upon position for fatwa, and covered all fiqh chapters, ending with inheritance. The passage also notes that al-Marghinani, in his Bidayat al-Mubtadi, combined al-Quduri's Mukhtasar with al-Jami' al-Saghir but used the latter's arrangement, which is why the chapter on inheritance is missing from both Bidayat al-Mubtadi and al-Hidaya. Finally, it mentions that al-Quduri sometimes records the differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text in the Hanafi school covering all fiqh chapters.
الجامع الصغير (Al-Jami' al-Saghir): A collection of Hanafi rulings compiled by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani, covering most fiqh topics except inheritance.
كشف الظنون (Kashf al-Zunun): A biographical and bibliographical encyclopedia by Hajji Khalifa (d. 1067 AH), used here to trace the original attribution.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it impossible for the famous praise to have been said about Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) Because al-Quduri never wrote an introduction.
B) Because the praise contains grammatical errors.
C) Because Abu Ali al-Shashi died before al-Quduri was born.
D) Because Kashf al-Zunun says so.

Key Takeaway
Always verify attributions of famous sayings by checking chronological consistency and authoritative sources like Kashf al-Zunun.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
8 min
Al-Quduri's Methodology in His Mukhtasar
Methodology of compilation in Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe al-Quduri's methodology in compiling his Mukhtasar, including his selection criteria, presentation of opinions, and the relationship with other Hanafi texts.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri compiled only essential, frequently occurring issues with the relied-upon opinion, making his Mukhtasar a concise yet comprehensive manual.

After clarifying the misconception about the famous praise, the passage moves to al-Quduri's actual methodology. Understanding how he selected and arranged content reveals his pedagogical goal: to provide a practical, authoritative reference for students and judges. This lesson explores those choices and their impact on later works like Bidayat al-Mubtadi and Al-Hidayah.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Quduri's criteria for inclusion
The passage states that he gathered 'the needed issues' and 'covered those that frequently occur.' He also mentions the relied-upon opinion (al-qawl al-mu'tamad) chosen for fatwa.
He avoided tedious additions and deficient abbreviations.
2
Note the scope of the Mukhtasar
It includes all chapters of fiqh and concludes with fara'id (inheritance). This made it a complete manual.
This completeness is one reason it became a standard matn.
3
Understand his treatment of ikhtilaf
Al-Quduri recorded the disagreements among the three main Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.
He sometimes mentions between them, i.e., he may present variant positions.
4
Recognize the impact on later works
Al-Marghinani later combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri with Al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, but used the arrangement of Al-Jami' al-Saghir, which lacked the inheritance section. Consequently, Bidayat al-Mubtadi and Al-Hidayah both omit inheritance.
This explains why Al-Hidayah has no inheritance chapter.

Why does Al-Hidayah not contain a chapter on inheritance?
A) Because al-Quduri omitted it from his Mukhtasar.

Key Takeaway

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
The Purpose and Methodology of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describes al-Quduri's purpose and method in his Mukhtasar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the purpose of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and describe its methodology: selection of relied-upon rulings, coverage of all fiqh chapters, and inclusion of intra-madhhab differences.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri provides the practical fruit of Hanafi fiqh without proofs, for easy memorization and application.

Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a foundational Hanafi text, but understanding its purpose and method is essential for using it correctly. This passage explains that al-Quduri gathered necessary and frequently occurring rulings, stating only the mufta bihi (relied-upon) opinion, while occasionally noting differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar. He intentionally omitted proofs except for a blessing verse and one hadith, focusing instead on the 'thamara' (fruit) of the madhhab. This lesson unpacks his methodology, so you can appreciate why the Mukhtasar is structured as it is.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's main goal
Read the passage to determine what al-Quduri aimed to achieve with his Mukhtasar. Look for phrases like 'جَمَعَ... المسائل المحتاج إليها' and 'ذكر القول المعتمد'.
He wanted a concise, practical reference.
2
Note the content scope
See which fiqh topics are included, and how the text is organized. The passage says he included all chapters and ended with fara'id.
The Mukhtasar is comprehensive in topics.
3
Examine how differences are treated
Look for mentions of intra-madhhab ikhtilaf. The text states he presents differences of the three imams and sometimes Zufar, but rarely other schools.
This is a key feature for students of the Hanafi school.
4
Understand the role of proofs
The passage explicitly says the Mukhtasar is devoid of proofs except for the opening verse and one hadith. Consider why this was done.
Al-Quduri prioritized the 'fruit' over the evidence.
5
Connect to the concept of thamara
Define 'thamara' in this context: the practical rulings that a muqallid needs to apply. The passage emphasizes this as the central benefit.
The Mukhtasar is a source of applied fiqh, not theoretical usul.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

به مزيد بسط ؛ لأني استوفيت ذلك في كتاب: «التجريد»، وأُلحـق بفروعه ما يليق بها، ليعتدل أول الكتاب وآخره في الاستيفاء، ثم ألحق به ما أغفله من الكتب، وأستوفي شرح جميعه، وأُقدم على ذلك مسألة في تقديم قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في الجملة على سائر فقهاء الأمصار...الخ». اهـ من كشف الظنون.
فهذا الكلام في تكملة القدوري وشرحها، للرازي، كما بينت أسفل في الحاشية، لا في مختصر القدوري، والله أعلم.
* أما عن عمل القدوري في المختصر، ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، فقد جَمَعَ الإمام القدوري في مختصره هذا المسائل المحتاج إليهـا، واستوعب ما يكثر وقوعه، مع ذكره القول المعتمد فيهـا، المختار للفتوى، وبذا صار مختصره خالياً عن الزوائد المملة، والاختصارات المخلة.
كما ضم هذا المختصر أبواب الفقه كلها، وختمها القدوري بالفرائض وأحكام المواريث.
ويُذكّر هنا، أن الإمام المرغيناني صاحب الهداية، لما جَمَعَ بين مختصر القدوري والجامع الصغير في بداية المبتدي، اعتمد ترتيب الجامع الصغير وأبوابه، ولم يعتمد ترتيب القدوري، ولما كان الجامع الصغير خالياً من كتاب المواريث خلا كتاب بداية المبتدي منه ، وكذلك أيضاً جاء كتاب الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي خالياً منه أيضاً. - وهكذا كان من عمل القدوري في مختصره أنه عَرَض الخلاف أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد، وأحياناً يذكر خلاف زفر، ولا يتعرض لذكر خلاف المذاهب الأخرى إلا نادراً. وهو مختصر خال من الأدلة إلا ما افتتح به مختصره مـن ذكـره لآية الوضوء تبركاً بالقرآن الكريم، ثم ذكره لحديث واحد فقط، وهـو حديث المغيرة بن شعبة رضي الله عنه في وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، مع إيمائه في عباراته أحياناً للدلائل إيماء.
وقد كانت عناية القدوري في هذا المختصر متوجهةً لذكر ثمرة المذهب الحنفي، وزبدة أحكامه، حيث ذكر فيه مسائل فقه المذهب الحنفي المحتاج لها، دون ذكر لدلائلها.
ومعلوم أن ذكر هذه الثمرة بهذا الاختصار الشديد أمـر لـيـس بالسهل، بل البسط في الكتابة أسهل وأيسر.
وهذه الثمرة التي ذكرها القدوري في مختصره، هي التي يسعى إليها المسلم المقلد المتفقه على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة، ليقـوم بتطبيقها، والالتزام بها، فيعرف الشروط والأركان والفرائض والسنن وهكذا، ويعرف المبطلات والمفسدات وكيفية الأعمال، وحكم كل فعل، من حلال أو حرام أو مكروه، وهكذا.
وأما البحث عن الأدلة التي أوصلت إلى هذه الأحكام، وكيف تم استنباطها، ووجه دلالتها ، فهذا أمر مهم ومفيد جداً، ومن أهم فوائده أنه يُورث في نفس المسلم المقلّد لإمامه طمأنينة وسكينة لما يفعله ويقوم به، وما يعتمده من أحكام، وأن مصدرها التشريعي كذا وكذا، ووجه دلالتها كذا وكذا.
ولكن في الوقت نفسه، فإن الدخول في باب الأدلة ودلالتها أمر
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

It has additional expansion; because I have covered that fully in the book 'al-Tajrid', and I append to its branches what befits them, so that the beginning and end of the book are balanced in comprehensiveness. Then I append to it what he omitted from the books, and I complete the commentary on all of it, and I preface that with an issue regarding giving precedence to Abu Hanifa's opinion generally over the other jurists of the regions... etc.' End quote from Kashf al-Zunun.
So this speech is regarding the completion of al-Quduri and its commentary, by al-Razi, as I clarified below in the footnote, not about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. And Allah knows best.
* As for al-Quduri's work in the Mukhtasar, and the methodology he followed: Imam al-Quduri gathered in his Mukhtasar the necessary issues, and included those that frequently occur, while mentioning the relied-upon opinion in them, the one chosen for fatwa. Thus his Mukhtasar became free from tedious additions and defective abbreviations.
He also included all chapters of fiqh in this Mukhtasar, and concluded it with fara'id (inheritance rulings).
It is recalled here that Imam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, when he combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, adopted the order of al-Jami' al-Saghir and its chapters, and did not adopt al-Quduri's order. And since al-Jami' al-Saghir lacked the book of inheritance, Bidayat al-Mubtadi also lacked it; likewise al-Hidayah, the commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, also lacked it. - And thus it was from al-Quduri's practice in his Mukhtasar that he presented the differences among the imams of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and sometimes he mentions the difference of Zufar, and he rarely addresses the differences of other schools. It is a Mukhtasar devoid of proofs, except that he opened his Mukhtasar by mentioning the verse of wudu' for blessing of the Holy Quran, then he mentioned only one hadith, which is the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning the wudu' of the Prophet (peace be upon him), with an occasional allusion to proofs in his expressions.
Al-Quduri's concern in this Mukhtasar was directed to stating the fruit of the Hanafi madhhab and the essence of its rulings, as he mentioned in it the necessary issues of Hanafi fiqh without mentioning their proofs.
It is known that stating this fruit with such extreme conciseness is not an easy matter; rather, elaboration in writing is easier and simpler.
This fruit that al-Quduri mentioned in his Mukhtasar is what the Muslim layperson who is studying the Hanafi madhhab seeks, in order to apply it and adhere to it, so that he knows the conditions, pillars, obligatory acts, sunnahs, and so on, and knows the invalidators and nullifiers and the manner of actions, and the ruling of every action, whether halal or haram or makruh, etc.
As for researching the proofs that lead to these rulings, how they were deduced, and their point of indication, this is an important and very beneficial matter. Among its most important benefits is that it instills in the heart of the layperson who follows his imam tranquility and peace of mind for what he does and performs, and what he relies upon of rulings, and that their legislative source is such and such, and their point of indication is such and such.
But at the same time, entering into the realm of proofs and their indication is a matter...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a front_matter study of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, the foundational text for the Hanafi school. The author, al-Maydani (or the editor), explains the nature and methodology of the Mukhtasar. He begins by clarifying that a previous remark in Kashf al-Zunun about 'completion of al-Quduri' refers to al-Razi's work, not the original Mukhtasar. Then he describes al-Quduri's purpose: to compile necessary and frequently occurring issues, stating only the relied-upon (mu'tamad) opinion for fatwa. The Mukhtasar covers all fiqh chapters, ending with fara'id. It includes intra-Hanafi differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and occasionally Zufar, but rarely other schools. Importantly, it is almost entirely devoid of proofs (adillah), except for the opening verse of wudu' and one hadith. Al-Quduri's focus is the 'fruit' (thamara) of the madhhab—practical rulings without their evidences. The passage notes that al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah used the order of al-Jami' al-Saghir, not al-Quduri, and thus omitted inheritance. Finally, the author highlights the value of proofs for a muqallid's tranquility, but acknowledges that delving into proofs is a separate, more advanced matter. This passage serves as an introduction to the study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining its place and method in Hanafi legal education.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal compendium by Imam al-Quduri, a central Hanafi text containing relied-upon rulings without proofs.
الثمرة (al-thamara): The practical outcome of fiqh: the rulings themselves as opposed to their evidences.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A layperson who follows a madhhab without independent ijtihad; here it refers to a student of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Why did al-Quduri omit proofs from his Mukhtasar?
A) He considered proofs unimportant.
B) He wanted to focus on the practical rulings needed for everyday practice.
C) He did not know the proofs.
D) He only wrote for scholars.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a concise, proof-free reference of relied-upon Hanafi rulings designed for practical application by muqallids.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Al-Quduri's Treatment of Intra-Madhhab Differences
Explains how al-Quduri presents differences among Hanafi imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe how al-Quduri presents differences among Hanafi imams and identify which imams' views are included.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri includes differences of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and occasionally Zufar, but rarely other schools.

A key feature of Mukhtasar al-Quduri is its inclusion of intra-madhhab differences. This is crucial for a Hanafi student to understand that the madhhab is not monolithic and to know the preferred position. This lesson focuses on the passage's explanation of how al-Quduri deals with ikhtilaf among the Hanafi imams, and why he largely ignores other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the imams whose differences are presented
Look in the passage for the names: أبو حنيفة، أبو يوسف، ومحمد. Also note the mention of زفر.
These are the major early Hanafi authorities.
2
Note the frequency of other schools' mention
The text says 'لا يتعرض لذكر خلاف المذاهب الأخرى إلا نادراً'. This is key for understanding the scope.
The Mukhtasar is focused on the Hanafi school.
3
Understand why this is significant
Consider the pedagogical purpose: a Hanafi student needs to know which positions are mufta bihi (relied upon). Al-Quduri's selection helps in that.
This saves the student from having to consult multiple sources.
4
Contrast with al-Marghinani's approach
The passage also mentions that al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah used a different ordering and omitted fara'id. Why might that be relevant?
It shows that later scholars adapted the content.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

The Value of Thamara and the Role of Proofs
Discusses the concept of thamara and the supplementary role of proofs

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the concept of 'thamara' in the context of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and articulate the relationship between practical rulings and their proofs.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar provides the thamara (fruit) of fiqh—applied rulings—while proofs are a separate, complementary study.

The passage distinguishes between two levels of fiqh study: the thamara (the practical rulings themselves) and the adillah (proofs from which they are derived). Al-Quduri designed his Mukhtasar to present only the thamara, making it accessible for muqallids to learn and apply. However, the author also emphasizes that researching proofs is important and brings tranquility. This lesson explores that balance.

Guided Path
1
Define 'thamara' as used in the passage
Find where the author says 'ثمرة المذهب الحنفي'. The context shows it means the actual rulings (halal, haram, conditions, etc.).
It is the outcome of ijtihad.
2
Identify the target audience for the thamara
The passage mentions 'المسلم المقلد المتفقه'. Who is that?
It is the layperson or student who follows the madhhab.
3
Contrast thamara with adillah
The passage later discusses the benefits of studying proofs. What are they?
Proofs bring tranquility and certainty.
4
Understand the pedagogical sequence
The passage implies that thamara comes first, then proofs. Why might that be?
One must know what to practice before understanding why.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

به مزيد بسط ؛ لأني استوفيت ذلك في كتاب: «التجريد»، وأُلحـق بفروعه ما يليق بها، ليعتدل أول الكتاب وآخره في الاستيفاء، ثم ألحق به ما أغفله من الكتب، وأستوفي شرح جميعه، وأُقدم على ذلك مسألة في تقديم قول أبي حنيفة رحمه الله تعالى في الجملة على سائر فقهاء الأمصار...الخ». اهـ من كشف الظنون.
فهذا الكلام في تكملة القدوري وشرحها، للرازي، كما بينت أسفل في الحاشية، لا في مختصر القدوري، والله أعلم.
* أما عن عمل القدوري في المختصر، ومنهجه الذي سار عليه، فقد جَمَعَ الإمام القدوري في مختصره هذا المسائل المحتاج إليهـا، واستوعب ما يكثر وقوعه، مع ذكره القول المعتمد فيهـا، المختار للفتوى، وبذا صار مختصره خالياً عن الزوائد المملة، والاختصارات المخلة.
كما ضم هذا المختصر أبواب الفقه كلها، وختمها القدوري بالفرائض وأحكام المواريث.
ويُذكّر هنا، أن الإمام المرغيناني صاحب الهداية، لما جَمَعَ بين مختصر القدوري والجامع الصغير في بداية المبتدي، اعتمد ترتيب الجامع الصغير وأبوابه، ولم يعتمد ترتيب القدوري، ولما كان الجامع الصغير خالياً من كتاب المواريث خلا كتاب بداية المبتدي منه ، وكذلك أيضاً جاء كتاب الهداية شرح بداية المبتدي خالياً منه أيضاً. - وهكذا كان من عمل القدوري في مختصره أنه عَرَض الخلاف أئمة المذهب أبي حنيفة وأبي يوسف ومحمد، وأحياناً يذكر خلاف زفر، ولا يتعرض لذكر خلاف المذاهب الأخرى إلا نادراً. وهو مختصر خال من الأدلة إلا ما افتتح به مختصره مـن ذكـره لآية الوضوء تبركاً بالقرآن الكريم، ثم ذكره لحديث واحد فقط، وهـو حديث المغيرة بن شعبة رضي الله عنه في وضوء النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم، مع إيمائه في عباراته أحياناً للدلائل إيماء.
وقد كانت عناية القدوري في هذا المختصر متوجهةً لذكر ثمرة المذهب الحنفي، وزبدة أحكامه، حيث ذكر فيه مسائل فقه المذهب الحنفي المحتاج لها، دون ذكر لدلائلها.
ومعلوم أن ذكر هذه الثمرة بهذا الاختصار الشديد أمـر لـيـس بالسهل، بل البسط في الكتابة أسهل وأيسر.
وهذه الثمرة التي ذكرها القدوري في مختصره، هي التي يسعى إليها المسلم المقلد المتفقه على مذهب الإمام أبي حنيفة، ليقـوم بتطبيقها، والالتزام بها، فيعرف الشروط والأركان والفرائض والسنن وهكذا، ويعرف المبطلات والمفسدات وكيفية الأعمال، وحكم كل فعل، من حلال أو حرام أو مكروه، وهكذا.
وأما البحث عن الأدلة التي أوصلت إلى هذه الأحكام، وكيف تم استنباطها، ووجه دلالتها ، فهذا أمر مهم ومفيد جداً، ومن أهم فوائده أنه يُورث في نفس المسلم المقلّد لإمامه طمأنينة وسكينة لما يفعله ويقوم به، وما يعتمده من أحكام، وأن مصدرها التشريعي كذا وكذا، ووجه دلالتها كذا وكذا.
ولكن في الوقت نفسه، فإن الدخول في باب الأدلة ودلالتها أمر
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

It has additional expansion; because I have covered that fully in the book 'al-Tajrid', and I append to its branches what befits them, so that the beginning and end of the book are balanced in comprehensiveness. Then I append to it what he omitted from the books, and I complete the commentary on all of it, and I preface that with an issue regarding giving precedence to Abu Hanifa's opinion generally over the other jurists of the regions... etc.' End quote from Kashf al-Zunun.
So this speech is regarding the completion of al-Quduri and its commentary, by al-Razi, as I clarified below in the footnote, not about Mukhtasar al-Quduri. And Allah knows best.
* As for al-Quduri's work in the Mukhtasar, and the methodology he followed: Imam al-Quduri gathered in his Mukhtasar the necessary issues, and included those that frequently occur, while mentioning the relied-upon opinion in them, the one chosen for fatwa. Thus his Mukhtasar became free from tedious additions and defective abbreviations.
He also included all chapters of fiqh in this Mukhtasar, and concluded it with fara'id (inheritance rulings).
It is recalled here that Imam al-Marghinani, author of al-Hidayah, when he combined Mukhtasar al-Quduri and al-Jami' al-Saghir in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, adopted the order of al-Jami' al-Saghir and its chapters, and did not adopt al-Quduri's order. And since al-Jami' al-Saghir lacked the book of inheritance, Bidayat al-Mubtadi also lacked it; likewise al-Hidayah, the commentary on Bidayat al-Mubtadi, also lacked it. - And thus it was from al-Quduri's practice in his Mukhtasar that he presented the differences among the imams of the madhhab: Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and sometimes he mentions the difference of Zufar, and he rarely addresses the differences of other schools. It is a Mukhtasar devoid of proofs, except that he opened his Mukhtasar by mentioning the verse of wudu' for blessing of the Holy Quran, then he mentioned only one hadith, which is the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba (may Allah be pleased with him) concerning the wudu' of the Prophet (peace be upon him), with an occasional allusion to proofs in his expressions.
Al-Quduri's concern in this Mukhtasar was directed to stating the fruit of the Hanafi madhhab and the essence of its rulings, as he mentioned in it the necessary issues of Hanafi fiqh without mentioning their proofs.
It is known that stating this fruit with such extreme conciseness is not an easy matter; rather, elaboration in writing is easier and simpler.
This fruit that al-Quduri mentioned in his Mukhtasar is what the Muslim layperson who is studying the Hanafi madhhab seeks, in order to apply it and adhere to it, so that he knows the conditions, pillars, obligatory acts, sunnahs, and so on, and knows the invalidators and nullifiers and the manner of actions, and the ruling of every action, whether halal or haram or makruh, etc.
As for researching the proofs that lead to these rulings, how they were deduced, and their point of indication, this is an important and very beneficial matter. Among its most important benefits is that it instills in the heart of the layperson who follows his imam tranquility and peace of mind for what he does and performs, and what he relies upon of rulings, and that their legislative source is such and such, and their point of indication is such and such.
But at the same time, entering into the realm of proofs and their indication is a matter...
Source pages p. 327

Commentary
This passage is a front_matter study of Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, the foundational text for the Hanafi school. The author, al-Maydani (or the editor), explains the nature and methodology of the Mukhtasar. He begins by clarifying that a previous remark in Kashf al-Zunun about 'completion of al-Quduri' refers to al-Razi's work, not the original Mukhtasar. Then he describes al-Quduri's purpose: to compile necessary and frequently occurring issues, stating only the relied-upon (mu'tamad) opinion for fatwa. The Mukhtasar covers all fiqh chapters, ending with fara'id. It includes intra-Hanafi differences among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and occasionally Zufar, but rarely other schools. Importantly, it is almost entirely devoid of proofs (adillah), except for the opening verse of wudu' and one hadith. Al-Quduri's focus is the 'fruit' (thamara) of the madhhab—practical rulings without their evidences. The passage notes that al-Marghinani in al-Hidayah used the order of al-Jami' al-Saghir, not al-Quduri, and thus omitted inheritance. Finally, the author highlights the value of proofs for a muqallid's tranquility, but acknowledges that delving into proofs is a separate, more advanced matter. This passage serves as an introduction to the study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, explaining its place and method in Hanafi legal education.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal compendium by Imam al-Quduri, a central Hanafi text containing relied-upon rulings without proofs.
الثمرة (al-thamara): The practical outcome of fiqh: the rulings themselves as opposed to their evidences.
المقلد (al-muqallid): A layperson who follows a madhhab without independent ijtihad; here it refers to a student of Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary benefit of studying proofs (adillah) for a muqallid?
A) To become a mujtahid.
B) To attain tranquility and peace of mind.
C) To write new fatwas.
D) To criticize other madhahib.

Key Takeaway
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar provides the thamara for immediate practice, while studying proofs brings deeper conviction and tranquility.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
8 min
Understanding the Purpose of Mukhtasar al-Quduri: Thamarah, Taqlid, and the Role of Proofs
Introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri: methodology and purpose

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why al-Quduri omitted proofs from his Mukhtasar and identify the intended audience and the concept of thamarah in Hanafi pedagogy.

Core Idea
A muqallid needs the fruit (ruling), not the root (proof); the Mukhtasar serves practice, not research.

This passage sets the stage for the entire Mukhtasar by explaining its philosophy: it is a practical guide for the layperson, not a scholarly treatise. Understanding this helps us appreciate the structure and content of the fiqh texts we will study. Al-Quduri intentionally omitted detailed proofs to make the rulings accessible to every Muslim, while directing those who seek deeper evidence to his larger works.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's purpose
Read the passage to determine what al-Quduri aimed to achieve with his Mukhtasar. Look for phrases like 'thamar' (fruit) and 'without proofs'.
The purpose is to provide the essential rulings for practice, not to engage in scholarly debate.
2
Distinguish between thamarah and dalil
The passage contrasts the 'fruit' (thamar) of the madhhab—the practical rulings—with the 'proofs' (adilla) from which they are derived. Recognize that thamarah is the outcome, while dalil is the evidence.
This distinction is central to Hanafi educational methodology.
3
Recognize the intended audience
The passage identifies the muqallid (follower) as the primary reader. This person needs to know what to do (conditions, pillars, sunan, etc.) without necessarily understanding the proof.
The muqallid is contrasted with specialists who can handle proofs.
4
Note the relationship to advanced texts
Al-Quduri directed those seeking proofs to his larger works like 'al-Tajrid' in 12 volumes and his explanation of Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. This shows the Mukhtasar is part of a tiered curriculum.
This hierarchy ensures each level of student gets appropriate material.
5
Summarize stylistic features
The passage praises the Mukhtasar's style: comprehensive, clear, elegant, concise, yet solid. These features make it easy to memorize and apply.
The style is deliberately crafted to serve the purpose of accessibility.

ولكن في الوقت نفسه، فإن الدخول في باب الأدلة ودلالتها أمر عظيم، ومهيع خطير، لا يقدر على الدخول فيه إلا من كان أهلاً لذلك، وهو شأن المختصين، بل خاصة المتخصصين، وليس هو من شأن عامة الناس المشغولين بطلب المعاش، والسعي على العيال. هنا ألف القدوري هذا المختصر العظيم المبارك ليستفيد منه كل مسلم، ويقطف ثمرته بيسر دون عناء.
وأما من أراد البسط في الأدلة، وبيان وجه دلالتها، مع مناقشة أدلة غيره، فقد ألف له القدوري كتاب «التجريد» في ١٢ مجلداً، كما شرح مختصر الكرخي في خمس مجلدات كبار مخطوطة، تكون بالطباعة الحديثة في عشرين مجلداً، وقد بَسَط فيه الأدلة أيما بسط، مع المناقشات والأخذ والرد.
وهكذا من أراد التوسط في ذلك، فهناك مؤلفات كثيرة في المذهب، تفي بالرغبات المتنوعة لكل طالب محتاج، والأمر واسع، والعلم في هذا بحر لا ساحل له عَرَفه مَن عَرَفه، وجَهله مَن جَهله.
* أما أسلوب القدوري في مختصره:
فقد ساق الإمام القدوري مسائل المذهب الحنفي في مختصره، ورَصَفَها ورتَّبها بعبارة شاملة حسنة رفيعة، قوية رصينة، سهلة واضحة، وأسلوب جميل، مع حُسن الإيجاز، ولطف الإعجاز، وجودة المعاني ومتانة المباني، وبألفاظ فصيحة متفق عليها»(۱).
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. ... (except the disagreement of Zufar, and it does not mention the disagreement of other madhhabs except rarely. It is a summary devoid of proofs except what it opened with: mentioning the verse of wudu as a blessing from the Noble Quran, then mentioning only one hadith, the hadith of al-Mughira ibn Shu'ba, may Allah be pleased with him, concerning the wudu of the Prophet, peace be upon him, with an allusion in its expressions sometimes to the proofs. The attention of al-Quduri in this summary was directed to mentioning the fruit of the Hanafi madhhab and the cream of its rulings, for he mentioned in it the needed issues of Hanafi fiqh, without mentioning their proofs. It is known that mentioning this fruit with such extreme conciseness is not easy; rather, elaboration in writing is easier and simpler. This fruit that al-Quduri mentioned in his summary is what the Muslim muqallid who studies the madhhab of Imam Abu Hanifa seeks, to implement it and adhere to it, so that he knows the conditions, pillars, obligations, sunnas, and so on, and knows the invalidators and nullifiers, and the manner of actions, and the ruling of every action, whether halal, haram, makruh, etc. As for researching the proofs that led to these rulings, how they were derived, and the aspect of their indication, this is an important and very beneficial matter, and among its most important benefits is that it instills in the heart of the muqallid of his imam tranquility and serenity for what he does and performs, and what he adopts of rulings, and that their legislative source is such-and-such, and the aspect of their indication is such-and-such. But at the same time, entering the door of proofs and their indication is a great matter and a dangerous path; none can enter it except those who are qualified, and it is the concern of specialists, indeed the elite of specialists, and it is not the concern of the general public busy seeking livelihood and striving for their families. Here al-Quduri authored this great blessed summary so that every Muslim may benefit from it and pluck its fruit with ease without toil. As for one who wants elaboration on the proofs and explanation of their indication, along with discussing the proofs of others, al-Quduri authored for him the book 'al-Tajrid' in 12 volumes, and he also explained the Mukhtasar of al-Karkhi in five large manuscript volumes, which would be in modern printing twenty volumes, and he elaborated the proofs extensively, with discussions and give-and-take. Likewise, whoever wants something moderate in that, there are many works in the madhhab that satisfy the diverse desires of every needy student, and the matter is vast, and knowledge in this is a sea without shore: he knows it who knows it, and he is ignorant of it who is ignorant of it. * As for al-Quduri's style in his Mukhtasar: Imam al-Quduri arranged the issues of the Hanafi madhhab in his Mukhtasar, organizing and ordering them with a comprehensive, good, lofty, strong, solid, easy, clear expression, and a beautiful style, with excellent conciseness, gentle brevity, good meanings, solid structure, and eloquent, agreed-upon words.)
Source pages p. 328

Commentary
This passage is an introduction explaining the nature and purpose of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It tells us that al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is a concise compilation of Hanafi fiqh rulings, stripped of detailed proofs, designed for the average Muslim (muqallid) who needs to know the practical outcomes (thamar) of the madhhab. The author notes that al-Quduri only included one hadith for blessing, and alludes to proofs only briefly. The passage emphasizes that while studying proofs is beneficial and brings tranquility, it is the domain of specialists; for the common person, the Mukhtasar suffices. Those who seek proofs are directed to al-Quduri's larger works like 'al-Tajrid'. The style of the Mukhtasar is praised for its comprehensive, clear, and elegant wording. This is not a ruling but a methodological preface, setting the stage for the fiqh content that follows.

Key Terms
مختصر (mukhtasar): A concise summary of fiqh issues, containing only the essential rulings without detailed proofs.
ثمرة (thamarah): The 'fruit' or outcome of the madhhab: the practical rulings that a layperson needs to act upon.
مقلد (muqallid): A Muslim who follows a particular madhhab without independently verifying proofs, relying on the authority of the Imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the primary purpose of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar?
A) To provide detailed proofs for every ruling
B) To present the practical rulings (thamar) of the Hanafi madhhab for muqallids
C) To compare all four madhhabs on every issue
D) To refute the arguments of other schools

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a practical handbook of Hanafi rulings designed for the muqallid, intentionally omitting proofs to prioritize accessibility and ease of practice.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Role of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in Hanafi Fiqh
Introduction to Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the purpose, target audience, and stylistic features of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and explain its place in the Hanafi madhhab curriculum.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a concise yet comprehensive summary accessible to all levels of Hanafi students.

This passage introduces the renowned Hanafi manual Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Imam al-Quduri. It highlights the work's accessibility to every Muslim, its clear and concise style, and how it complements more detailed works like al-Tajrid. Understanding the role of this mukhtasar is essential for navigating Hanafi legal studies efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the purpose of the Mukhtasar
Read the passage to find why al-Quduri authored this work. The phrase 'ليستفيد منه كل مسلم' indicates his goal was for every Muslim to benefit easily.
2
Determine the target audience
Note who the passage says can benefit. The author explicitly includes beginners, intermediates, and even advanced scholars who still need to review it.
Contrast with the statement that 'specialists' are the ones who delve into deeper works.
3
Analyze the stylistic features praised
Identify the adjectives used: 'شاملة حسنة رفيعة، قوية رصينة، سهلة واضحة' (comprehensive, good, lofty, strong, solid, easy, clear) and 'حسن الإيجاز' (good conciseness).
These stylistic choices make the text accessible yet authoritative.
4
Understand the complementary works
Al-Quduri also wrote al-Tajrid (12 volumes) for elaborate proofs, and a commentary on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (5 manuscript volumes). Note how these serve different needs.
The Mukhtasar is the entry point; advanced students can consult the detailed works.
5
Summarize the overall significance
The passage concludes that the Mukhtasar is one of the most beautiful, beneficial, and complete books, indicating its foundational status in Hanafi fiqh.
This text is a staple in traditional Hanafi curricula.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري
عظيم، ومهيع خطير ، لا يقدر على الدخول فيه إلا من كان أهلاً لذلك، وهو شأن المختصين، بل خاصة المتخصصين، وليس هو من شأن عامة الناس المشغولين بطلب المعاش، والسعي على العيال. هنا ألف القدوري هذا المختصر العظيم المبارك ليستفيد منه كل مسلم، ويقطف ثمرته بيسر دون عناء.
وأما من أراد البسط في الأدلة، وبيان وجه دلالتها، مع مناقشة أدلة غيره، ألف له القدوري كتاب «التجريد» في ١٢ مجلداً، كما شرح مختصر الكرخي في خمس مجلدات كبار مخطوطة، تكون بالطباعة الحديثة في عشرين مجلداً ، وقد بَسَط فيه الأدلة أيما بسط، مع المناقشات والأخذ والرد.
وهكذا من أراد التوسط في ذلك، فهناك مؤلفات كثيرة في المذهب، تفي بالرغبات المتنوعة لكل طالب محتاج، والأمر واسع، والعلم في هذا بحر لا ساحل له عَرَفه مَن عَرَفه، وجَهله مَن جَهله.
* أما أسلوب القدوري في مختصره :
فقد ساق الإمام القدوري مسائل المذهب الحنفي في مختصره، ورَصَفَها ورتَّبها بعبارة شاملة حسنة رفيعة، قوية رصينة، سهلة واضحة، وأسلوب جميل ، مع حُسن الإيجاز، ولطف الإعجاز وجودة المعاني ومتانة المباني، وبألفاظ فصيحة متفق عليها».
كما أنه أجاد في عرضه وترتيبه لأقوال أئمة المذهب، وذكـره للخلاف الحاصل بينهم.
وبهذا كله غدا مختصراً معتبراً لطيفاً من أجمل الكتب وأحسنها، وأتمها فائدة وأكملها، ليشترك فيه المبتدىء والمتوسط في فهمـه والانتفاع به ولا يستغني المنتهي من مراجعته ومطالعته.
Chapter Two: A Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Great and perilous path, none can enter it except those who are qualified, and it is the concern of specialists, indeed the elite of specialists, and it is not the concern of the general public occupied with seeking livelihood and striving for dependents. Here al-Quduri authored this great blessed concise work so that every Muslim may benefit from it and pluck its fruit with ease without hardship. As for those who desire elaboration of proofs, clarification of their indications, along with discussion of others' proofs, al-Quduri authored for them the book 'al-Tajrid' in 12 volumes, and he also commented on Mukhtasar al-Karkhi in five large manuscript volumes, which in modern printing would be twenty volumes, and he elaborated the proofs extensively, with discussions and rebuttals. Likewise, those who desire moderation in that, there are many works in the madhhab that fulfill the various desires of every needy student, and the matter is vast, and knowledge in this is a sea without shore, known to those who know it and unknown to those who are ignorant of it. * As for al-Quduri's style in his Mukhtasar: Imam al-Quduri presented the issues of the Hanafi madhhab in his Mukhtasar, arranging and ordering them with a comprehensive, good, lofty, strong, solid, easy, and clear expression, and a beautiful style, with good conciseness, graceful brevity, soundness of meanings, firmness of structure, and eloquent agreed-upon expressions. Also, he excelled in presenting and arranging the statements of the imams of the madhhab and mentioning the differences among them. With all this, it became a concise, esteemed, and elegant work, among the most beautiful and best books, the most complete in benefit and perfection, so that the beginner and intermediate may both partake in understanding and benefiting from it, and the advanced scholar does not dispense with reviewing and studying it.
Source pages p. 329

Commentary
This passage is an introductory study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the renowned Hanafi legal summary. The author describes the great value of the work, noting that it is accessible to all Muslims, not just specialists, while also offering advanced works like al-Tajrid for those seeking detailed proofs. He praises al-Quduri's style as clear, concise, and comprehensive, covering the issues of the Hanafi school and the differences among its imams. The passage concludes by stating that the Mukhtasar is beneficial for students at all levels: beginners, intermediates, and even advanced scholars who still need to consult it.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal manual authored by Imam al-Quduri, summarizing the Hanafi madhhab.
التجريد (al-Tajrid): A detailed work by al-Quduri expanding on proofs and rebuttals in 12 volumes.
مختصر الكرخي (Mukhtasar al-Karkhi): Another Hanafi summary that al-Quduri wrote a commentary on.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only advanced specialists
B) Every Muslim, including beginners and intermediates
C) Only the general public
D) Only scholars who want extensive proofs

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational, accessible Hanafi text that benefits students at all levels, from beginners to advanced scholars.

Sources and Significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Discusses the sources and composition method of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary sources used by Imam al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar and explain why it became a foundational text for all levels of Hanafi students.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri distilled the strongest Hanafi rulings from earlier compilations, especially Zahir al-Riwayah, creating a standard text for all students.

This lesson explores how Imam al-Quduri compiled his celebrated Mukhtasar. The passage from Al-Lubab commentary reveals that al-Quduri drew upon earlier summary works and the core books of Zahir al-Riwayah. It also highlights his skill in selecting the most reliable positions, making the Mukhtasar a versatile text for beginners, intermediates, and advanced scholars alike.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Immediate Sources
The passage lists earlier mukhtasars by al-Tahawi, al-Hakim al-Shahid, and al-Karkhi. Recognize that al-Quduri did not explicitly name his sources, but scholars infer he used these.
2
Recognize the Foundational Books
The Zahir al-Riwayah books (six works by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani) are the ultimate basis. Understand that these are the authoritative transmitted texts of the Hanafi madhhab.
3
Understand al-Quduri's Selection Method
He chose the strongest narrations and the mufta bihi positions, presenting them in a clear, ordered manner. This made his Mukhtasar comprehensive for all levels.

منها، ويصوغها ويقدمها منسقة مرتبةً في هذا المختصر المبارك.
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
He excelled in presenting and arranging the statements of the imams of the madhhab and mentioning the differences among them.

His style from a number of manuscript commentaries on al-Quduri.

Section Four
Sources of al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar
Imam al-Quduri did not explicitly state any source from which he derived the issues recorded in this Mukhtasar. It is expected that he benefited from the mukhtasars authored in the madhhab before him, such as Mukhtasar al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), Mukhtasar al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH), and he had another mukhtasar called al-Muntaqa, and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), and others.
Before these are the foundational books of the madhhab, which are the books of Zahir al-Riwayah, by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani: al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat.
Also, the commentaries written on them by scholars and imams of the madhhab.
It has been mentioned earlier that al-Quduri had a book called al-Taqrib, in which he mentioned the issues of disagreement among the imams of the Hanafi madhhab.
Thus, Imam al-Quduri, with his brilliance, his high status in the madhhab, his imamate in Hanafi fiqh, and his familiarity with the books of those before him, was able to select the strongest narrations in the madhhab, establish the relied-upon and preponderant view, and compose and present them in an orderly arrangement in this blessed Mukhtasar.
Source pages p. 330

Commentary
This passage is a scholarly introduction discussing the sources used by Imam al-Quduri in compiling his Mukhtasar, a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab. The author notes that al-Quduri did not explicitly name his sources, but it is inferred that he relied on earlier concise works (mukhtasars) by Hanafi scholars such as al-Tahawi, al-Hakim al-Shahid, and al-Karkhi. Additionally, he used the core books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani—the six foundational works that contain the primary transmitted rulings of the Hanafi school. Al-Quduri also wrote a separate work, al-Taqrib, dealing with intra-madhhab disagreements. The passage emphasizes al-Quduri's mastery: he selected the strongest narrations and the relied-upon positions (mu'tamad) and presented them in a well-organized manner. This Mukhtasar became a standard text for students at all levels, from beginner to advanced.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh work by Imam al-Quduri, a foundational text in the Hanafi madhhab covering rulings without detailed proofs.
ظاهر الرواية (Zahir al-Riwayah): The six core books of Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that contain the authoritative and widely transmitted rulings of the Hanafi madhhab.
المذهب (al-Madhhab): The legal school or doctrinal framework, specifically the Hanafi school in this context.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

D) Sharh al-Ma'ani al-Athar and Ikhtilaf al-Amsar

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a carefully selected compilation from earlier Hanafi works, especially Zahir al-Riwayah, serving as a standard text for all students.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Sources and Influence of Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar
Biographical and historical account of sources and influence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the primary sources al-Quduri relied upon for his Mukhtasar and explain why the Mukhtasar became a foundational text in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar synthesized earlier Hanafi compendiums and the authoritative Zahir al-Riwayah, becoming the mother of all later Hanafi works.

Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is one of the most important concise texts in Hanafi fiqh. In this lesson, we will explore the sources he used to compile it—primarily earlier Hanafi mukhtasars and the six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani. Understanding this transmission chain is crucial for appreciating the authority and reliability of the Mukhtasar in the Hanafi curriculum.

Guided Path
1
Identify al-Quduri's immediate sources
List the earlier Hanafi compendiums mentioned: Mukhtasar al-Tahawi, Mukhtasar al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid, and Mukhtasar al-Karkhi. Note that al-Quduri also had his own work al-Taqrib on intra-madhhab disputes.
These are earlier mukhtasars that predate al-Quduri's work.
2
Recognize the Zahir al-Riwayah corpus
Identify the six foundational books of Imam Muhammad: al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat. These form the most authoritative layer of Hanafi transmission.
Zahir al-Riwayah is distinct from later fatwa works.
3
Understand al-Quduri's selection method
Al-Quduri, with his deep knowledge, selected the strongest narrations and established the preponderant (rajih) views. He presented them in a well-organized format.
This is why the Mukhtasar is trusted as a reliable summary of the school.
4
Assess the impact on later Hanafi works
Note that many major Hanafi texts—Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', Bidayat al-Mubtadi, al-Wafi, al-Kanz, Majma' al-Bahrayn—are based on or incorporate al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. Over 123 scholarly works were produced on it.
This demonstrates its central role in Hanafi fiqh transmission.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث الرابع
مصادر القدوري في مختصره
لم يصرح الإمام القدوري بأي مصدرٍ استقى منه المسائل التي دونها في هذا المختصر، والمتوقع أنه استفاد من المختصرات التي ألفت في المذهب قبله مثل مختصر الطحاوي، (ت٣٢١هـ)، ومختصر (الكافي) للحاكم الشهيد، (ت٣٣٤هـ)، وله مختصر آخــر سماه (المنتقى)، ومختصر الكرخي (ت ٣٤٠هـ)، وغيرها.
ومن قبل هؤلاء كتب أصول المذهب، التي هي كتـب ظـاهر الرواية، للإمام محمد بن الحسن الشيباني: الأصل، والجامع الكبير، والجامع الصغير والسير الكبير والسير الصغير، والزيادات.
وأيضاً ما كُتب عليها من شروح لعلماء المذهب وأئمته.
وقد تقدم أن للقدوري كتاباً سماه : «التقريب»، ذكر فيه المسائل الخلافية بين أئمة المذهب الحنفي.
وهكذا استطاع الإمام القدوري ببراعته، وتقدمه الرفيع في المذهب، وإمامته في الفقه الحنفي، واطلاعه على كتـب مـن سـبقه، استطاع أن يختار أقوى الروايات في المذهب، ويُثبت المعتمد الراجح منها، ويصوغها ويقدمها منسقة مرتبةً في هذا المختصر المبارك.

المبحث الخامس
أثر مختصر القدوري فيمن بعده ومدى اعتمادهم عليه
هذا
لقد بارك الله تعالى في مختصر القدوري بركة عظيمة، وكتب القبول العظيم عند علماء المذهب، وطلابه، وقد تقدم شيء من الكلام على ثناء العلماء على المختصر. وكان من أثره فيمن ألف بعده من أئمة المذهب، أنهم اعتمدوه كل الاعتماد فيما كتبوه في فقه المذهب، حيث ضمنوه في كتبهم، وأودعوه في مؤلفاتهم، حتى صار مختصر القدوري أم كتب المذهب التي تلته، وأساسها وعمدتها.
فقد ضمنه وزاد عليه كل من السمرقندي في تحفة الفقهاء، والمرغيناني في بداية المبتدي والنسفي في الوافي، والكنز، وابن الساعاتي في مجمع البحرين والحلبي في مجمع الأبحر، وغيرهم. كما قامت عليه شروح كثيرة، منها المبسوط، ومنها المختصر، ودللوا لمسائله وأصلوا لها وهكذا قامت أعمال علمية كثيرة عليه، بلغت ١٢٣ عملاً، كلها تدل على أثره الكبير فيمن جاء بعده، وسيأتي قريباً إن شاء الله بيان تلك الأعمال العلمية التي قامت على مختصر القدوري.
Fourth Section: Sources of al-Quduri in his Mukhtasar
Imam al-Quduri did not explicitly state any source from which he derived the issues recorded in this Mukhtasar. It is expected that he benefited from the compendiums authored before him in the madhhab, such as Mukhtasar al-Tahawi (d. 321 AH), Mukhtasar al-Kafi by al-Hakim al-Shahid (d. 334 AH) – and he has another compendium called al-Muntaqa – Mukhtasar al-Karkhi (d. 340 AH), and others. Before these are the foundational books of the madhhab, which are the books of Zahir al-Riwayah of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani: al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat. Also what was written on them by way of commentaries by the scholars and imams of the madhhab. It has been mentioned earlier that al-Quduri has a book called 'al-Taqrib' in which he mentioned the disputed issues among the imams of the Hanafi madhhab. Thus Imam al-Quduri, with his brilliance, his high standing in the madhhab, his imamate in Hanafi fiqh, and his knowledge of the books of those before him, was able to select the strongest transmissions in the madhhab, establish the relied-upon and preponderant among them, and formulate and present them arranged in this blessed Mukhtasar.

Fifth Section: The Impact of Mukhtasar al-Quduri on Those After Him and the Extent of Their Reliance Upon It
Allah the Exalted has placed a great blessing in Mukhtasar al-Quduri and ordained immense acceptance among the scholars of the madhhab and its students. Some of the scholars' praise for the Mukhtasar has already been mentioned. Among its effects on those who authored after him from the imams of the madhhab is that they relied upon it completely in what they wrote in the fiqh of the madhhab, incorporating it into their books and depositing it in their works, until Mukhtasar al-Quduri became the mother of the madhhab books that followed it, their foundation and mainstay. For al-Samarqandi incorporated and added to it in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', al-Marghinani in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, al-Nasafi in al-Wafi and al-Kanz, Ibn al-Sa'ati in Majma' al-Bahrayn, al-Halabi in Majma' al-Abhar, and others. Many commentaries were also written upon it, among them al-Mabsut and al-Mukhtasar (another work). They provided proofs for its issues and established their principles. Thus many scholarly works were produced upon it, reaching 123 works, all indicating its great impact on those who came after. Soon, if Allah wills, an account of those scholarly works based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri will follow.
Source pages p. 331

Commentary
This passage is a biographical and historical introduction to Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, the foundational Hanafi text. It comprises two sections. The fourth section discusses al-Quduri's sources. Although he did not name them explicitly, the author explains that al-Quduri drew from earlier Hanafi compendiums (Mukhtasars) by al-Tahawi, al-Hakim al-Shahid (al-Kafi and al-Muntaqa), and al-Karkhi. More importantly, he relied on the Zahir al-Riwayah books of Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani—the six core texts: al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, and al-Ziyadat. He also used commentaries on these works. Additionally, al-Quduri authored 'al-Taqrib' on intra-Hanafi disagreements. His mastery allowed him to select the strongest narrations and establish the preponderant (rajih) view, presenting it in an organized manner.

The fifth section describes the unprecedented acceptance and influence of the Mukhtasar. Later Hanafi scholars relied on it as the basis for their own works, incorporating it and expanding upon it. Examples include al-Samarqandi's Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', al-Marghinani's Bidayat al-Mubtadi (which became the matn of al-Hidayah), al-Nasafi's al-Wafi and al-Kanz, Ibn al-Sa'ati's Majma' al-Bahrayn, and al-Halabi's Majma' al-Abhar. Numerous commentaries (shuruh) were written, such as al-Sarakhsi's al-Mabsut and others, totalling 123 works. This highlights the Mukhtasar's central role in Hanafi fiqh transmission.

Key Terms
ظاهر الرواية (Zāhir al-Riwāyah): The six core books authored by Imam Muhammad ibn al-Hasan al-Shaybani (al-Asl, al-Jami' al-Kabir, al-Jami' al-Saghir, al-Siyar al-Kabir, al-Siyar al-Saghir, al-Ziyadat) which form the most authoritative source of Hanafi rulings.
المختصر (al-Mukhtaṣar): Specifically, Mukhtasar al-Quduri – a concise summary of Hanafi fiqh by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH) that became a foundational text in the school.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is the ultimate foundation of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, according to the passage?
A) The Quran and Sunnah directly.
B) The earlier compendiums of al-Tahawi and al-Karkhi.
C) The six books of Zahir al-Riwayah by Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani.
D) The commentaries of later Hanafi scholars.

Key Takeaway
Al-Quduri's Mukhtasar is not an isolated work but a carefully curated summary of the most authoritative Hanafi transmissions, making it the cornerstone of later Hanafi scholarship.

The Influence and Dating of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Discussion of impact and dating of Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the influence of Mukhtasar al-Quduri on later Hanafi scholarship and state the approximate date of its composition based on biographical evidence.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri became the foundational text for over 123 Hanafi works, written by al-Quduri around 420 AH for his young son.

This passage from the introduction to al-Labab Sharh al-Quduri reveals how this concise manual became the 'mother' of later Hanafi compilations. It also provides a scholarly estimate of its composition date using the age of al-Quduri's son. Understanding this text's role helps appreciate the architecture of Hanafi fiqh literature.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main claim about influence
Read the passage and pinpoint the author's central assertion regarding how later scholars treated Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
Look for phrases like 'اعتمدوه كل الاعتماد' and 'أم كتب المذهب'.
2
List the authors who incorporated it
Identify the names of later Hanafi imams mentioned as having incorporated the Mukhtasar into their own works.
Al-Samarqandi, al-Marghinani, al-Nasafi, Ibn al-Sa'ati, al-Halabi, and others.
3
Note the number of works based on it
Find the total number of scholarly works that the passage says were built upon the Mukhtasar.
The number is 123 works.
4
Follow the dating argument
Trace the reasoning used to estimate the composition date: al-Quduri wrote it for his son Muhammad; his son died in 440 AH young; assume youth to 33 years, so birth around 410 AH; assume son was 10 when Mukhtasar was compiled.
The son's death and age are used as anchors.
5
Determine the approximate composition year
Combine the reasoning to derive the approximate year of composition.
Result: around 420 AH.

الفصل الثاني : دراسة عن مختصر القدوري المبحث الخامس أثر مختصر القدوري فيمن بعده ومدى اعتمادهم عليه هذا لقد بارك الله تعالى في مختصر القدوري بركة عظيمة، وكتب القبول العظيم عند علماء المذهب ،وطلابه، وقد تقدم شيء من عند الكلام على ثناء العلماء على المختصر . وكان من أثره فيمن ألف بعده من أئمة المذهب، أنهم اعتمدوه كل الاعتماد فيما كتبوه في فقه المذهب، حيث ضمنوه في كتبهم، وأودعوه في مؤلفاتهم، حتى صار مختصر القدوري أم كتب المذهب التي تلته، وأساسها وعمدتها. فقد ضمنه وزاد عليه كل من السمرقندي في تحفة الفقهاء، والمرغيناني في بداية المبتدي والنسفي في الوافي، والكنز، وابن الساعاتي في مجمع البحرين والحلبي في مجمع الأبحر، وغيرهم. كما قامت عليه شروح كثيرة، منها المبسوط، ومنها المختصر، ودللوا لمسائله وأصلوا لها وهكذا قامت أعمال علمية كثيرة عليه، بلغت ١٢٣ عملاً ، كلها تدل على أثره الكبير فيمن جاء بعده، وسيأتي قريباً إن شاء الله بيان تلك الأعمال العلمية التي قامت على مختصر القدوري، في فصل خاص موسع * ومن أثره فيمن بعده ما كتبه الله له من الانتشار الكبير العجيب في البلاد الإسلامية، وتداول العلماء والطلبة له في كل مكان، مما يدل على أثره الكبير الواضح في المذهب الحنفي، بل في أتباع المذاهب الأخرى، حيث اقتنوه ،واعتمدوه ونقلوا عنه، وهذا كله من فضل الله، والله يؤتي الفضل من يشاء. * تاريخ تأليف القدوري لمختصره : تقدم أن القدوري جمع هذا المختصر لولده محمد، وكانت وفاة ولده سنة ٤٤٠ هـ ، وهو شاب قبل أوان الرواية، وإذا كان سن الشباب إلى الثالثة والثلاثين ) ، فلتكن ولادته سنة ٤١٠هـ تقريباً. هذا، وليكن جَمْع القدوري لمختصره وعمر ولده عشر سنين، فيكون تاريخ تأليف المختصر تقريباً سنة ٤٢٠ هـ، أي في أواخر عمر الإمام القدوري، حيث توفي سنة ٤٢٨ هـ، والله أعلم. ***** (1) ينظر القاموس المحيط (كهل).
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Section Five: The Impact of Mukhtasar al-Quduri on Those After Him and the Extent of Their Reliance Upon It. Allah Almighty has blessed Mukhtasar al-Quduri with great blessing and granted it immense acceptance among the scholars of the madhhab and its students. Some of the praise of scholars for the Mukhtasar has preceded. Among its effects on those who authored after him from the imams of the madhhab is that they relied upon it completely in what they wrote on fiqh of the madhhab; they incorporated it into their books and deposited it in their works, until Mukhtasar al-Quduri became the mother of the books of the madhhab that followed it, their foundation and mainstay. Al-Samarqandi incorporated it and added to it in Tuhfat al-Fuqaha', al-Marghinani in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, al-Nasafi in al-Wafi and al-Kanz, Ibn al-Sa'ati in Majma' al-Bahrayn, al-Halabi in Majma' al-Abhar, and others. Many commentaries were written upon it, including al-Mabsut and al-Mukhtasar. They provided evidence for its issues and derived principles for them. Thus many scholarly works were based upon it, amounting to 123 works, all indicating its great impact on those who came after. Soon, Allah willing, a detailed exposition of those scholarly works that were based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri will come in a special extended chapter. * And among its impact on those after him is what Allah has written for it of wondrous widespread dissemination in Islamic lands, and the circulation of scholars and students of it everywhere, which indicates its great and clear impact in the Hanafi madhhab, and even among followers of other madhhabs, as they acquired it, relied upon it, and transmitted from it. All of this is from the favor of Allah, and Allah gives favor to whom He wills. * The Date of al-Quduri's Composition of His Mukhtasar: It has preceded that al-Quduri compiled this Mukhtasar for his son Muhammad, and his son died in the year 440 AH, being a young man before the age of narration. If youth extends to thirty-three years [by one definition], then let his birth be around 410 AH. Let al-Quduri's compilation of his Mukhtasar be when his son was ten years old, so the date of composition of the Mukhtasar is approximately 420 AH, i.e. in the later years of Imam al-Quduri's life, as he died in 428 AH. And Allah knows best. ***** (1) See al-Qamus al-Muhit (kahl).
Source pages p. 332

Commentary
This passage from the introduction to al-Labab Sharh al-Quduri discusses the profound impact of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar on later Hanafi scholarship. The author emphasizes that Allah blessed this concise work with wide acceptance, so much so that subsequent Hanafi imams—like al-Samarqandi, al-Marghinani, al-Nasafi, Ibn al-Sa'ati, al-Halabi, and others—incorporated it wholesale into their own works. This created a tradition where the Mukhtasar became the 'mother' (umm) of later Hanafi texts, their foundation and mainstay. Over 123 scholarly works were built upon it, including major commentaries like al-Mabsut. The passage also provides a scholarly estimate of the Mukhtasar's composition: al-Quduri wrote it for his son Muhammad, who died young around 440 AH. By calculating backwards, the author deduces that al-Quduri compiled the Mukhtasar around 420 AH, when his son was about ten years old, making it a late-life work of al-Quduri (he died in 428 AH).

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual authored by Imam Abu al-Husayn al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), which became a foundational text in the Hanafi school.
بداية المبتدي (Bidayat al-Mubtadi): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH) that is based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and later served as the basis for al-Hidayah.
تحفة الفقهاء (Tuhfat al-Fuqaha'): A Hanafi fiqh work by al-Samarqandi (d. 540 AH) that incorporates Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) 410 AH
B) 420 AH
C) 428 AH
D) 440 AH

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri, composed around 420 AH, became the backbone of Hanafi fiqh literature, with over 123 works relying on it.
