Influence and Dating of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Describes book's influence and composition date.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Mukhtasar al-Quduri became influential across madhhabs and estimate its composition date using the author's own biographical clues.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri spread across Islamic lands and was used even by non-Hanafis, showing its universal utility.

This passage introduces us to the extraordinary impact of a concise Hanafi manual and provides a window into how biographers reconstruct the timeline of a classical work. You will learn to appreciate the authority of this text and the reasoning behind its dating.

Guided Path
1
Identify the claim of influence
The passage states that the Mukhtasar spread greatly in Islamic lands and was used by scholars from other madhhabs. Note the phrase 'even among followers of other schools' as evidence of cross-madhhab acceptance.
2
Note the target audience and son's death
The Mukhtasar was compiled for al-Quduri's son Muhammad, who died in 440 AH as a youth (before age of narration, defined as up to 33). This gives a starting point for dating.
3
Reconstruct the dating logic
Since the son died young, his birth is estimated around 410 AH (440 - 30). The author assumes the father compiled when the son was ten, placing composition around 420 AH, near al-Quduri's death in 428 AH.
The author uses tentative language ('let it be', 'approximately') showing this is an inference.
4
Recognise the humility in the final remark
The passage ends with 'Allah knows best', acknowledging uncertainty. This reflects scholarly caution when dating classical texts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثاني: دراسة عن مختصر القدوري

ومن أثره: ما كتبه الله له من الانتشار الكبير العجيب في البلاد الإسلامية، وتداول العلماء والطلبة له في كل مكان، مما يدل على أثره الكبير الواضح في المذهب الحنفي، بل في أتباع المذاهب الأخرى، حيث اقتنوه واعتمدوه ونقلوا عنه، وهذا كله من فضل الله، والله يؤتي الفضل من يشاء.

تاريخ تأليف القدوري لمختصره: تقدم أن القدوري جمع هذا المختصر لولده محمد، وكانت وفاة ولده سنة 440هـ، وهو شاب قبل أوان الرواية، وإذا كان سن الشباب إلى الثالثة والثلاثين، فلتكن ولادته سنة 410هـ تقريباً. هذا، وليكن جمع القدوري لمختصره وعمر ولده عشر سنين، فيكون تاريخ تأليف المختصر تقريباً سنة 420هـ، أي في أواخر عمر الإمام القدوري، حيث توفي سنة 428هـ، والله أعلم.
Chapter Two: Study of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar

From its impact: what Allah wrote for it of great and amazing spread in Islamic lands, and the circulation of scholars and students with it everywhere, indicating its great and clear impact in the Hanafi school, and even among followers of other schools, as they acquired it, relied upon it, and transmitted from it. All this is from Allah's bounty, and Allah gives bounty to whom He wills.

Date of al-Quduri's authorship of his Mukhtasar: It was mentioned earlier that al-Quduri compiled this Mukhtasar for his son Muhammad, and his son died in 440 AH, while still a youth before the age of narration. If the age of youth extends to thirty-three, then his birth was around 410 AH. And let the compilation of the Mukhtasar be when his son was ten years old, so the date of authorship is approximately 420 AH, i.e., in the later years of Imam al-Quduri's life, as he died in 428 AH. Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 333

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion of the Mukhtasar al-Quduri's influence and the estimated date of its composition. The author first highlights the extraordinary spread of this work across Islamic lands, noting that it was not only adopted by Hanafis but also by followers of other madhhabs, who acquired, relied upon, and transmitted from it. This is attributed to divine favor. Then, the author provides a reasoned estimate of the date of authorship: since al-Quduri compiled it for his son Muhammad, who died in 440 AH as a youth (defined as up to 33 years of age), his birth would be around 410 AH. Assuming the father compiled it when the son was ten years old, the date would be around 420 AH, near the end of al-Quduri's life (he died in 428 AH). This is an inference based on available data and is presented with 'Allah knows best' to indicate uncertainty.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a foundational text of the Hanafi school.
القدوري (al-Quduri): Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, a prominent Hanafi jurist from Baghdad, author of the Mukhtasar.

Key Takeaway

Textual Variants in Mukhtasar al-Quduri: A Hanafi Scholarly Concern
Discussing the tradition of manuscript variant recognition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the significance of manuscript variants in Hanafi text transmission and describe the early scholarly efforts to resolve them.

Core Idea
Textual variants were recognized and addressed by early Hanafi commentators, including al-Quduri's own student.

This passage introduces the issue of manuscript variants in al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, a foundational Hanafi text. The author highlights how both the original author and later scholars engaged with these differences, establishing a tradition of textual criticism within the Hanafi school. Understanding this tradition is crucial for appreciating how the school preserved doctrinal consistency across manuscripts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main phenomenon
The author notes significant variation among manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Recognize that this is not a flaw but an accepted part of textual transmission.
The variation may affect legal rulings.
2
Trace the chain of commentators
The passage mentions al-Marghinani (author of al-Hidayah) and later commentators of al-Hidayah and the Mukhtasar itself. Note the chronological flow.
This shows a continuous scholarly concern.
3
Distinguish sources of variants
Scholars investigated whether the variant came from al-Quduri himself or from copyists. Understand that both possibilities are considered.
This distinction affects reliability.
4
Note the earliest commentator
Abu Nasr al-Aqta', a direct student of al-Quduri, is cited as the earliest commentator. His proximity to the author adds weight to his observations.
Death dates: al-Quduri 428 AH, al-Aqta' 474 AH.

المبحث السادس: اختلاف نُسَخ مختصر القدوري

مسألة اختلاف نُسَخ القدوري مسألة مهمة انتبهت إليها بفضل الله وتوفيقه في خلال عملي في تحقيق اللباب، وتحقيق أصله مختصر القدوري، وما وجدته من اختلاف كبير في نسخه.

وقد لاحظت أن صاحب الهداية الذي ضمن القدوري في بداية المبتدي أصل الهداية، يشير في الهداية في مواضع كثيرة إلى وجود اختلاف في نُسَخ القدوري في لفظ كذا، أو في جملة كذا.

وهكذا جاء بعده شراح الهداية يؤكدون ذلك، بل زادت عندهم الأمثلة على ذلك، وراحوا يجتهدون في بيان اللفظ الصحيح منها والخطأ، وبيان الصحيح والأصح.

كما كان لهم اهتمام ظاهر في بيان هل هذا الاختلاف من أصل كلام القدوري، أو بسبب نُساخ المختصر؟

وكذلك كان حال شراح مختصر القدوري، بدءاً بأقدمهم تلميذ القدوري أبي نصر الأقطع، ومن بعده كالزاهدي في المجتبى، والحدادي في السراج والجوهرة، وغيرهم، مما يدل على أن ذكر اختلاف نسخ القدوري قديم عهده، إذ كانت وفاة الأقطع تلميذ القدوري سنة 474هـ، ووفاة القدوري سنة 428هـ.
Sixth Section: Variant Manuscripts of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar

The issue of variant manuscripts of al-Quduri is an important matter that I noticed, by Allah's grace and facilitation, during my work in editing al-Lubab and editing its source, Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and what I found of great variation in its manuscripts.

I observed that the author of al-Hidayah, who included al-Quduri in the beginning of al-Mubtadi (the basis of al-Hidayah), points out in al-Hidayah in many places the existence of variation in al-Quduri's manuscripts in such-and-such a word or such-and-such a phrase.

Similarly, later commentators of al-Hidayah confirmed this; indeed, examples increased with them, and they strove to explain the correct wording and the error, and to clarify the correct and more correct.

They also had a clear interest in explaining whether this variation originated from al-Quduri's own wording or was due to copyists of the Mukhtasar.

The same was the case with commentators of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, starting with the earliest, al-Quduri's student Abu Nasr al-Aqta', and after him like al-Zahidi in al-Mujtaba, and al-Hadadi in al-Siraj and al-Jawhara, and others, indicating that mentioning the variation of al-Quduri's manuscripts is old, since al-Aqta', al-Quduri's student, died in 474 AH, and al-Quduri died in 428 AH.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion of the textual variants found in manuscripts of al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. The author, engaged in editing the commentary al-Lubab and its source the Mukhtasar, observed significant differences among manuscripts. He notes that the author of al-Hidayah (al-Marghinani) frequently pointed out such variants in his work. Later commentators of al-Hidayah expanded on this, attempting to identify correct readings. They also investigated whether the variants stemmed from al-Quduri himself or from scribes. The same concern appears among early commentators of the Mukhtasar, such as Abu Nasr al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), a direct student of al-Quduri, indicating that awareness of variants dates back very close to the author's own time.

Key Terms
الهداية (al-Hidayah): A major Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani, which comments on al-Quduri's Mukhtasar via the medium of al-Mubtadi.
أبو نصر الأقطع (Abu Nasr al-Aqta'): A direct student of al-Quduri and one of the earliest commentators on the Mukhtasar, died 474 AH.
نسخة (nuskhah): Manuscript copy; plural 'nusakh' (نسخ) refers to manuscript copies that may contain variants.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Al-Marghinani
B) Al-Zahidi
C) Abu Nasr al-Aqta'
D) Al-Hadadi

Key Takeaway
Hanafi scholars have long recognized and analyzed manuscript variants, with early commentators like Abu Nasr al-Aqta' addressing them soon after the author's death.

The Importance of Manuscript Variations in Hanafi Fiqh Texts
Introduction to manuscript variation in Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why manuscript variations in classical Hanafi texts matter and evaluate the scholarly response to such variations.

Core Idea
Manuscript errors in foundational texts can alter rulings; careful textual criticism safeguards the school's integrity.

Manuscript variations are not merely academic curiosities—they can directly affect the legal rulings derived from classical Hanafi texts. This passage from a study on Mukhtasar al-Quduri reveals that even the great al-Marghinani, author of Al-Hidayah, sometimes relied on flawed copies. Understanding how Hanafi scholars historically addressed these discrepancies is essential for anyone who relies on transmitted fiqh texts.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the medium
Understand that classical fiqh texts were transmitted by hand, making them susceptible to copyist errors.
This is the first layer: manuscript culture.
2
Identify the scope of error
The passage notes that variations range from minor to severe, sometimes changing the meaning or even the legal ruling.
Some errors are trivial; others are critical.
3
Trace the scholarly response
From al-Quduri's student al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH) to later commentators, scholars actively corrected errors based on school principles.
Al-Aqta' explicitly stated he corrected errors 'according to the school of our companions'.
4
Assess the impact on canonical works
The author of Al-Hidayah occasionally adopted incorrect readings from faulty manuscripts, leading to erroneous rulings that later commentators rectified.
This underscores the need for critical editions.
5
Apply the lesson
When using a classical Hanafi text today, check for critical editions and scholarly notes on variant readings; do not assume a single manuscript is infallible.
This is a practical takeaway for students and researchers.

وهذه الفوارق والاختلافات التي وقفت عليهـا بـيـن نـسـخ القدوري، منها ما أمره سهل، وليس له أثر ذو بال على النص، ومنها جداً، وله أثر كبير، إما في تغيير المعنى، أو تغيير الحكم الشرعي، ومنها ما بين ذلك في الأهمية، ومنها ما يتعلق بزيادة شرط في المسألة، أو في زيادة مسألة كاملة، وسقوطها من أخرى، أو تتعلق بنسبة الأقوال لأئمة المذهب، ونحو هذا.

القدوري، وشراح الهداية، وأولَوْها رعاية كبيرة، وعناية بالغة. وقد بلغ الحدُّ في اختلاف هذه النسخ وتغييرها للحكم، أن صاحب الهداية وهو من هو في المذهب : إمامةً وعلماً واعتماداً، قد وقع منه في الهداية اعتماد لنُسَخ خاطئة من القدوري، فيها خطأ في الحكم، وجرى على ذلك، وفاته التنبه إليه، لكن الله حافظ وشرعه، فقد هيأ سبحانه من بعد صاحب الهداية من جاء مـن شـراح الهداية ونبهوا إلى ذلك، وأعادوا الأمور إلى نصابها، وبينوا الصواب، كما هو في مسألة إقرار الزاني بالزنا، وهل يشترط أن يسأل
دینه
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri - Section Six: Variation of Manuscripts of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The issue of variation in the manuscripts of al-Quduri is an important matter that I became aware of, by the grace and guidance of Allah, during my work in the critical edition of Al-Lubab and its source Mukhtasar al-Quduri, and I found great variation in its copies. I noted that the author of Al-Hidayah, who incorporated al-Quduri in Bidayat al-Mubtadi, the basis of Al-Hidayah, indicates in Al-Hidayah in many places the existence of variation in the manuscripts of al-Quduri in a certain word or phrase. Similarly, the commentators of Al-Hidayah after him confirmed this, and even added examples, and they exerted effort to identify the correct wording and the error, and to clarify what is correct and more correct. They also showed apparent interest in clarifying whether this variation originated from al-Quduri's own words or from the copyists of the Mukhtasar. Likewise was the case with the commentators of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, starting with the earliest, al-Quduri's student Abu Nasr al-Aqta', and after him like al-Zahidi in al-Mujtaba, al-Hadadi in al-Siraj and al-Jawhara, and others, indicating that mentioning the variation of al-Quduri's manuscripts is old, since the death of al-Aqta', al-Quduri's student, was in 474 AH, and al-Quduri died in 428 AH. Al-Aqta' explicitly stated these variations in the conclusion of his commentary saying: 'I have found in most copies of the original errors in some issues, which are mistakes from the copyist, and I have corrected all of that according to what the school of our companions (may Allah have mercy on them) requires.' ... These differences and variations that I have come across between the manuscripts of al-Quduri: some are minor, without significant effect on the text; some are very significant, with major impact, either changing the meaning or changing the legal ruling; some are of intermediate importance; some involve the addition of a condition in an issue, or the addition of a complete issue and its omission from another, or relate to attribution of opinions to Imams of the school, and the like. These important differences awakened the attention of the scholars of the school, from the commentators of al-Quduri and the commentators of Al-Hidayah, and they gave them great care and utmost attention. The extent of variation in these manuscripts and their alteration of rulings reached such a level that the author of Al-Hidayah, despite his high rank in the school in terms of imamate, knowledge, and reliance, relied in Al-Hidayah on incorrect manuscripts of al-Quduri containing errors in ruling, and proceeded accordingly without noticing. But Allah protects His law, so He, glorified be He, prepared after the author of Al-Hidayah those from among the commentators of Al-Hidayah who pointed this out, corrected matters, and clarified the correct view, as in the case of the zani's confession of zina and whether it is required that he ask about his religion.
Source pages p. 334

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter discussion on the importance of manuscript variations in Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author explains that during his critical edition of Al-Lubab and its source, he noticed significant differences among manuscripts. He highlights that even the renowned Hanafi scholar al-Marghinani, author of Al-Hidayah, occasionally relied on erroneous copies, leading to incorrect rulings. This underscores the need for careful textual criticism in fiqh. The passage traces the awareness of these variations from al-Quduri's student Abu Nasr al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH) to later commentators like al-Zahidi and al-Hadadi. Al-Aqta' himself corrected errors in copies based on Hanafi school principles. The variations range from minor to severe, potentially altering legal rulings. The author cites the example of the zani's confession, but does not detail it here. This discussion establishes the scholarly tradition of verifying transmitted texts.

Key Terms
نُسَخ (nusakh): Manuscript copies of a text, specifically referring to the different handwritten versions of Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A foundational Hanafi fiqh manual by Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied and commented upon.
الهداية (Al-Hidayah): A famous Hanafi fiqh work by Burhan al-Din al-Marghinani (d. 593 AH), based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is a key lesson from the discussion on manuscript variations of Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) Manuscript variations are always minor and do not affect legal rulings.
B) Only the author of Al-Hidayah noticed these variations.
C) Even major Hanafi scholars like the author of Al-Hidayah could rely on erroneous copies, showing the need for careful textual criticism.
D) The variations were only discovered in modern times.

Key Takeaway
Manuscript variations in classical Hanafi texts can materially affect legal rulings, necessitating rigorous textual verification.

The Miracle of Imam al-Quduri: Safeguarding the Mukhtasar
Narrates a miracle attributed to Imam al-Quduri after completing his Mukhtasar

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to recount the story of al-Quduri's miracle and explain its significance for the reliability of Hanafi matn transmission.

Core Idea
Imam al-Quduri's karamah affirms the divine protection of his Mukhtasar from scribal errors.

This lesson narrates a well-known account from the Hanafi tradition about Imam al-Quduri, the author of the foundational text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The story illustrates how the final version of the matn was purified from scribal errors through a miracle, highlighting the care taken by early Hanafi scholars to preserve the accuracy of their texts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and event
Note that the subject is Imam al-Quduri, the author of the Mukhtasar. The event occurs after he finishes composing the book and performs Hajj.
2
Understand the purpose of the prayer
Al-Quduri prays to Allah to reveal any error or oversight that may have occurred. This shows his humility and concern for textual accuracy.
3
Analyze the result of the prayer
Upon reviewing the manuscript, he finds five or six erased places. The erasures indicate corrections made by scribes, not by him.
4
Extract the lesson for textual reliability
The miracle reinforces that the transmitted text is free from authorial mistakes, and any errors came from scribes and were corrected, ensuring the text's trustworthiness.

ولكن سمعت من بعض الأساتذة الكبار يقول: إن القدوري رحمه الله لما فرغ من تصنيف مختصره المنسوب إليه، حج، وأخذ المختصر معه، ولما فرغ من طوافه، سأل الله سبحانه أن يوقفه على خطأ فيه، أو سهو منه وقع عن قلم. ثم إنه فتح المختصر، وتصفحه ورقة ورقة إلى آخره، فوجد فيه خمسة مواضع، أو ستة مواضع ممحوة، وهذا يُعدُّ من كرامته وهذا مما يؤيد أن وقوع هذا الغلط من الكاتب، لا منه، والله أعلم.
But I heard from some senior teachers saying: Indeed al-Quduri, may Allah have mercy on him, when he finished composing his Mukhtasar attributed to him, performed Hajj and took the Mukhtasar with him. When he finished his circumambulation, he asked Allah, the Exalted, to make him aware of any error in it or any oversight from his pen. Then he opened the Mukhtasar and leafed through it page by page until the end, and found in it five or six erased places. This is considered among his miracles, and this supports that the occurrence of this mistake was from the scribe, not from him. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 341

Commentary
This is a biographical anecdote about Imam al-Quduri, the author of the renowned Hanafi text Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The passage relates a miracle (karamah) attributed to him: after completing his book, he performed Hajj and prayed to Allah to reveal any mistake in it. Upon reviewing, he found several places that had been erased, indicating that scribes had corrected errors, and thus the final version was free of mistakes. This story reinforces the reliability of the text's transmission.

Key Terms
القدوري (al-Quduri): Imam Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, the author of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh.
المختصر (al-Mukhtasar): A concise legal manual summarizing Hanafi rulings, referring specifically to Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Takeaway
Imam al-Quduri's karamah shows that his Mukhtasar was purified from scribal errors, underscoring the high standard of textual accuracy in the Hanafi madhhab.

The Impact of Manuscript Variants on Hanafi Rulings
Methodological discussion on manuscript variants

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why manuscript variants in Hanafi texts require careful verification and identify how they can affect rulings.

Core Idea
Manuscript variants can change a ruling; verifying the copy is as essential as understanding the fiqh.

In this lesson, we examine a methodological passage from a study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author presents two examples where different manuscripts of the same text give contradictory rulings. This is not a rare occurrence; it is a feature of hand-copied books. A student of Hanafi fiqh must learn to identify such variants and determine which version is authoritative. The passage compares this to hadith criticism, emphasizing that textual precision is part of the divine test for scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two examples of variants
Locate the two fiqh chapters mentioned: the Book of Pledge and the Book of Settlement. In each, note that some manuscripts include or exclude certain rulings.
These examples show that variants can be additions or omissions.
2
Determine the ruling difference in each
For the pledge: some copies mention Malik's objection (making it permissible with a note of disagreement), others omit it, implying only the Hanafi view. For the settlement: one version says the sulh is permissible, another says it is not.
The difference is binary (valid/invalid).
3
Recognize the justification for each variant
The passage notes that the permissibility version in sulh is justified as an increase in dowry, while the non-permissibility has its own reasoning. Both are recorded in authoritative commentaries like al-Hidayah.
Each variant may have a valid legal basis.
4
Understand the broader principle: variants require verification
The author explicitly states that manuscript differences are important, affect rulings and conditions, and demand precision and cross-checking, similar to the science of hadith criticism.
This is a fundamental methodological point.
5
Apply the principle to your own study
When reading any primary Hanafi text, always be aware that printed editions may have variants. Consult commentaries and multiple copies to determine the mufta bihi (relied-upon position).
Your teacher's notes (like al-Lubab) often resolve such variants.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وإذا اتفقا على وضع الرهن على يد العدل: جاز، وقال مالك: لا يجوز، ذكر قوله في بعض النسخ ...». اهـ من الهداية. قال العيني في البناية (۱) : قوله : في بعض النسخ: أشار به إلى أن في بعضها ليس كذلك». اهـ

ففي هذا المثال يظهر كيف أن الحكم يختلف من نسخة إلى نسخة
أخرى، بالجواز وعدمه، ولكل وجه.
وهكذا هناك أمثلة كثيرة على اختلاف نُسَخ القدوري، تتفاوت في درجة أهميتها، ومدى تأثيرها في النص، تجدها مبثوثة في تعليقاتي على اللباب مع بيان الصواب، أو وجهة كل منهما. وكل هذه الأمثلة تؤكد أن أمر اختلاف النسخ أمر مهم ويحتاج الباحث المتفقه إلى التريث والدقة والتثبت في نصوص الفقهاء من خلال نسخ الكتاب ; لِمَا يترتب على ذلـك مـن أثر في اختلاف الأحكام، وما يتصل بها من شروط ونحوها، كمـا هـو الحـال في نصوص علماء الجرح والتعديل وما يترتب على ذلك عندهم من توثيق الرجل، أو عدم توثيقه مما يكون له أثر في صحة الحديث وعدم الصحة.
،
ولعل من حكم تقدير الله في حصول الاختلاف في النُّسَخ في الكتب عموماً، هو تمحيص طلاب العلم، وتباين درجاتهم في الدقة والبحث والمتابعة، ليجتهدوا ويتيقظوا، مسددين مقاربين، وليعلم أن أمر العلم أمر ليس بالسهل.
Chapter Two: Study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Book of Pledge, Chapter on Pledge Placed with a Trustee:
If they both agree to place the pledge with a trustee: it is permissible, and Malik said: it is not permissible. Mentioned his saying in some copies... End from al-Hidayah. Al-'Ayni said in al-Binayah (1): His saying: 'in some copies': he indicated by it that in some of them it is not like that. End.
17 - The Seventeenth Example: Al-Marghinani said in al-Hidayah (2), in the Book of Settlement: If a woman claims marriage against a man, and he settles with her for wealth he gives to her: it is permissible.
Al-Marghinani said: Thus he mentioned it in some copies of the Mukhtasar, and in some of them: it is not permissible.
The justification of the first: that it is made an increase in her dowry, and the justification of the second: ... End from al-Hidayah.
Al-'Ayni said in al-Binayah (3): i.e., copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, ..., and al-Atrzai said: I saw in a reliable copy of the copies of al-Quduri written in the year five hundred and twenty-five: non-permissibility ... End from al-Binayah.
In this example it appears how the ruling differs from one copy to another, in permissibility and non-permissibility, and each has a justification.
And likewise there are many examples of the differences of the copies of al-Quduri, differing in their degree of importance and extent of their impact on the text. You find them scattered in my commentaries on al-Lubab with an explanation of the correct version or the perspective of each. And all these examples confirm that the matter of copy differences is important and requires the researcher and student of fiqh to exercise patience, precision, and verification in the texts of the jurists through the copies of the book; because of the resulting impact on the differences of rulings and what relates to them of conditions and the like, just as is the case in the texts of the scholars of jarh and ta'dil and what results from that regarding the authentication of a man or his non-authentication, which has an impact on the authenticity or non-authenticity of hadith.
And perhaps from the wisdom of Allah's decree in causing differences in copies in books generally is the testing of students of knowledge and the differentiation of their levels in precision, research, and follow-up, so that they strive and become vigilant, guided and close to correctness, and to know that the matter of knowledge is not easy.
Source pages p. 354

Commentary
This passage is a methodological discussion from the author's introduction to his study of Mukhtasar al-Quduri. It highlights the critical issue of manuscript variance in classical Hanafi texts. The author provides two concrete examples: first, from the chapter on pledging (rahin), where the ruling on placing a pledge with a trustee is 'permissible' according to Abu Hanifa, but Malik disagreed; a variant manuscript omits the mention of Malik's view. Second, from the chapter on settlement (sulh), where a woman claims marriage and settles for a payment: some copies say it is permissible (viewing it as an increase in dowry), others say it is not. The author then emphasizes that such differences are not trivial; they can change the ruling itself or its conditions. He compares this to the science of hadith criticism (jarh wa ta'dil), where variant readings affect authenticity. The passage concludes with a reflection that the existence of variants is a divine test for students to exercise diligence and precision. As a Hanafi teacher, note that the author's own work (al-Lubab) aims to resolve such variants. The passage does not give preference to any variant but underscores the need for verification.

Key Terms
العدل (al-‘adl): A trustworthy third party appointed by both parties to hold a pledge in a pawn transaction.
الصلح (al-sulh): A settlement or compromise between parties to resolve a dispute, often involving payment.
النسخ (al-nusakh): Manuscript copies of a book, which may have textual variants affecting rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) They are negligible and do not affect the rulings.
B) They require careful verification and can impact legal judgments.
C) They only occur in the chapter on pledge.
D) They are all resolved by the author's own commentary.

Key Takeaway
Manuscript variants are a real challenge in Hanafi fiqh; the careful scholar must verify the text before ruling.

Editions and Translations of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Bibliographic survey of editions and translations

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the major printed editions and translations of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and explain its significance in the Hanafi curriculum.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is the most widely printed Hanafi fiqh manual, with editions spanning India, Turkey, Russia, and Egypt.

This lesson introduces you to the printed history of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text in Hanafi fiqh. Understanding its publication history helps you appreciate the widespread acceptance and authority of this manual across the Muslim world and beyond.

Guided Path
1
Identify the earliest printed edition
Locate the oldest recorded edition according to Brockelmann and Fuad Sezgin: Delhi, 1262 AH. Note that this is about 170 years ago from the time of the text.
2
Trace the geographical spread of printing
List the cities and years mentioned: Lahore (1287 AH), Bombay (1303 AH), Istanbul (1291 & 1309 AH), Kazan (1315 AH), Cairo (1324 & 1377 AH). Observe that printing centers span India, Turkey, Russia, and Egypt.
This shows the global demand for the text.
3
Recognize translations and their significance
Note translations into Persian, Turkish, German (Nikah section), and French (Jihad section). These translations facilitated study by non-Arabic speakers and indicate the text's international reach.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المبحث السابع
طبعات مختصر القدوري
كان من فضل الله تعالى العظيم على الإمام القدوري أن كتب لمختصره قبولاً عظيماً في صفوف العلماء وطلاب العلم، فكان من مخطوطاته مئات من النسخ، بل أكثر منتشرة في كل فج عميق فيه طالب علم. وأما عن نُسخه المطبوعة فحدث ولا حرج، بدءاً من السنين الأولى لانتشار المطابع وإلى زماننا هذا.
(۲)
فقد سجل بروكلمان في تاريخ الأدب العربي، وفؤاد سزكين في تاريخ التراث العربي أقدم طبعة له في دلهي بالهند، سنة ١٢٦٢ هـ، أي من ١٧٠ سنة تقريباً، كما طبع في لاهور سنة ١٢٨٧هـ، وفي بومباي سنة ۱۳۰۳هـ، وفي اسطنبول بتركيا سنة ۱۲۹۱هـ، وسنة ١٣٠٩هـ، وطبع في قازان بروسيا سنة ١٣١٥هـ. كما طبع في القاهرة بمصر، في مطبعة مصطفى البابي الحلبي (المطبعة الميمنية)، سنة ١٣٢٤هـ، وكانت الطبعة الثالثة في مطبعة مصطفى البابي سنة ١٣٧٧هـ.
وهكذا توالت الطبعات هنا وهناك، وما يزال يطبع، وكل طبعة لا تقل عن آلاف النسخ.
* وكان عدد صفحاته في الطبعات السابقة ما بين ١٢٠ صفحة متوسطة الحجم، مرصوصة فيما بين كلماتها وسطورها، إلى ١٣٠ صفحة تقريباً.
هذا كله، مع طبعاته الأخرى التي طبع فيها ضمن شروح القدوري مثل اللباب والجوهرة وغيرها من الحواشي العديدة المنتشرة في بلاد الهند والسند وباكستان.
وأيضاً، فقد طبع مترجماً إلى عدة لغات، منها طبعة تُرجم فيها إلى الفارسية في بومباي بالهند سنة ١٣٠٧هـ، وطبع مع شرح له باللغة التركية في اسطنبول سنة ١٢٨١هـ، عمله أمين فهمي باشا. كما تُرجم منه ما يتعلق بكتاب النكاح إلى اللغة الألمانية، وطبع سنة ١٨٣٢م، وتُرجم منه كتاب الجهاد إلى اللغة الفرنسية، وطبع سنة ۱۸۲۹م.
وهكذا، سبحان الرزاق الفتّاح الوهاب، كم أجرى الله للإمام القدوري من خير في مختصره هذا وكم بارك له فيه، فنفع خلائق لا يُحصون.
The Seventh Section: Editions of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
It was from the great bounty of Allah Almighty upon Imam al-Quduri that He granted his Mukhtasar immense acceptance among scholars and students of knowledge, such that its manuscripts number in the hundreds, indeed more, spread in every deep valley where there is a student of knowledge. As for its printed editions, there is no limit, starting from the early years of the spread of printing presses up to our present time.
(2)
Brockelmann in his History of Arabic Literature and Fuad Sezgin in his History of Arabic Heritage recorded its oldest edition in Delhi, India, in the year 1262 AH (about 170 years ago). It was also printed in Lahore in 1287 AH, in Bombay in 1303 AH, in Istanbul, Turkey in 1291 AH and 1309 AH, and in Kazan, Russia in 1315 AH. It was also printed in Cairo, Egypt, at Mustafa al-Babi al-Halabi Press (al-Maimuniyya Press) in 1324 AH, and the third edition was at Mustafa al-Babi Press in 1377 AH.
Thus editions continued here and there, and it is still being printed, with each edition no less than thousands of copies.
* The number of pages in previous editions ranged from approximately 120 medium-sized pages, with compact spacing between words and lines, to about 130 pages.
All of this, in addition to its other editions that were printed within the commentaries of al-Quduri such as al-Lubab and al-Jawhara and other numerous glosses spread in the lands of India, Sindh, and Pakistan.
Also, it was printed translated into several languages, including an edition translated into Persian in Bombay, India in 1307 AH, and printed with a commentary in Turkish in Istanbul in 1281 AH, done by Amin Fahmi Pasha. Also, what relates to the Book of Marriage was translated into German and printed in 1832 CE, and the Book of Jihad was translated into French and printed in 1829 CE.
Thus, glorified be the Provider, the Opener, the Bestower – how much good did Allah bring to Imam al-Quduri through this Mukhtasar, and how much blessing did He give him in it, benefiting countless creations.
Source pages p. 356

Commentary
This passage is a bibliographic survey of the printed editions and translations of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author begins by noting the widespread acceptance of the work among scholars and students, leading to hundreds of manuscript copies. Then, he lists the earliest known printed editions: Delhi (1262 AH), Lahore (1287 AH), Bombay (1303 AH), Istanbul (1291 and 1309 AH), Kazan (1315 AH), and Cairo (1324 AH, with a third edition in 1377 AH). The text also mentions that later editions often appear within larger commentaries like al-Lubab and al-Jawhara. Additionally, it notes translations into Persian, Turkish, German (the Nikah section), and French (the Jihad section). The passage concludes with praise for the divine blessing upon Imam al-Quduri.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise fiqh manual by Imam Abu al-Hasan al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a core text in the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri has been printed in multiple centers worldwide and translated into several languages, attesting to its central role in Hanafi education.

Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Chapter heading listing works based on al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the content of Chapter Three of al-Lubab and explain the purpose of a bibliography of commentaries in the Hanafi tradition.

Core Idea
Chapter Three is a bibliographic guide to the scholarly tradition built upon Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

This lesson introduces the third chapter of al-Lubab. Rather than presenting fiqh rulings, this chapter provides a list and description of the many commentaries and scholarly works that have been written based on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understanding this bibliographic context helps you appreciate the depth of the Hanafi commentarial tradition and the centrality of al-Quduri's text.

Guided Path
1
Locate the chapter heading

Shuruh are comprehensive commentaries; a'mal 'ilmiyyah may include abridgments, glosses, super-commentaries, etc.

The author, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, includes this bibliographic section to orient the reader to the vast tradition surrounding al-Quduri's text. It shows how later scholars built upon, refined, and transmitted Hanafi fiqh through this foundational matn.
This is common in later sharh works – they often begin with a chapter on the author and his text.

Commentary
This is a chapter heading indicating that the following section will list and describe the various commentaries (shuruh) and scholarly works (a'mal 'ilmiyyah) that have been written based on the Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational text of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH). The author of al-Lubab, 'Abd al-Ghani al-Maydani, is providing a bibliographical orientation to help readers understand the tradition of scholarship that built upon al-Quduri's work.

Key Terms
شروح (shurūḥ): Commentaries or expositions that explain and expand upon a base text.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri, widely used as a foundational text for study.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Scholarly Legacy of Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Introduces the widespread acceptance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the many scholarly works built upon it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri in the Hanafi tradition and state the range of scholarly works produced on it.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri received countless commentaries, reflecting its central role in Hanafi fiqh education.

Before diving into the rulings of Hanafi fiqh, it is essential to understand the foundational texts that shape the madhhab. Mukhtasar al-Quduri is one such text, a concise manual that has been taught and commented upon for centuries. This lesson introduces you to the immense scholarly attention it received, setting the stage for deeper study.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the context
This passage is the opening of a chapter in al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri that lists commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Understand that you are reading about the text's scholarly reception.
2
Identify the author's claim
The author states that Allah granted great acceptance and widespread dissemination to Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Note the religious framing of the text's success.
3
Note the citation of al-Shihab al-Marjani
Al-Shihab al-Marjani is quoted as saying 'countless creatures have commented on it.' This hyperbolic phrase emphasizes the enormous number of commentaries.
4
Understand the scope of the list
The author says he will mention only what he has come across: commentaries, glosses, and other scholarly works. This shows the vastness of the literature.
5
Appreciate the significance in Hanafi tradition
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a pillar of Hanafi education; its many commentaries reflect its utility for teaching and learning.

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
شروح مختصر القدوري
والأعمال العلمية التي قامت عليه

تقدم أن الله تعالى كتب لمختصر القدوري قبولاً عظيماً عند العلماء وطلابهم وانتشر انتشاراً كبيراً عجيباً، وبارك الله فيه بركة عظمى، وكان من تمام بركته أن العلماء أقبلوا عليه بخدمته علمياً إقبالاً كبيراً، من وجوه متعددة، وذلك نتيجة تدريسهم له، وحاجة طلبة العلم إلى ذلك، فكتبت عليه شروح كثيرة، بل قال الشهاب المرجاني: «قد شرحه خلق لا تُحصى» ، وذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء.
وسأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من أعمال علمية قامت على هذا المختصر المبارك، من شروح خاصة به سواء للكتاب كله أو قطعة منه، أو مؤلفات لعلماء المذهب ممن جاؤوا بعده، فكان المختصر مما ضمنوه في مؤلفاتهم، أو زادوا عليه، وفرعوا عليه.
وكذلك ما وقفتُ عليه مما كتب عليه من حواش أو تعليقات، أو أي خدمات علمية قامت عليه، أو على شروحه، أو تابعة لذلك، من
(۱) كما قال صاحب كشف الظنون ١٦٣١/٢.
(۲) ناظورة الحق
ص
.٥٢
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the scholarly works based upon it.

It has preceded that Allah Almighty granted to Mukhtasar al-Quduri great acceptance among scholars and their students, and it spread in a vast and wondrous manner, and Allah blessed it with immense blessing. Part of its complete blessing was that scholars turned to serving it academically with great fervor in multiple ways, as a result of their teaching it and the need of students of knowledge for that. So many commentaries were written on it. Indeed, al-Shihab al-Marjani said: 'Countless creatures have commented on it.' That is the favor of Allah which He gives to whom He wills.

I will mention below what I have come across of scholarly works based on this blessed Mukhtasar: commentaries specific to it, whether for the entire book or a part of it, or works by scholars of the school who came after it, such that the Mukhtasar was included in their works, or they added to it and branched out from it.

And likewise what I have come across of glosses or annotations written on it, or any scholarly services based on it, or on its commentaries, or related to that.

(1) As stated by the author of Kashf al-Zunun 2/1631.
(2) Nazirat al-Haqq, p. 52.
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the third chapter of al-Lubab Sharh al-Quduri, which discusses the various commentaries written on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author begins by noting the extraordinary acceptance and widespread dissemination that Allah granted to this concise work. He highlights that scholars turned to serving it academically, which resulted in numerous commentaries. He quotes al-Shihab al-Marjani, who said 'countless creatures have commented on it,' emphasizing the immense number. The author then states his intention to list the scholarly works based on this Mukhtasar that he has encountered, including complete or partial commentaries, works by later Hanafi scholars that incorporated the Mukhtasar, as well as glosses, annotations, and other scholarly services related to it or its commentaries. He cites two sources: Kashf al-Zunun and Nazirat al-Haqq. This passage sets the stage for a detailed bibliography of works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Key Terms
شروح (shurūḥ): Commentaries or explanations written on a text, specifically here on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtaṣar al-Qudūrī): A concise manual of Hanafi fiqh by Imam Ahmad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), widely studied and commented upon.
حواش (ḥawāshī): Glosses or marginal notes added to a main text or its commentary, often by later scholars for clarification or critique.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what did al-Shihab al-Marjani say about Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) It is the best book in Hanafi fiqh.
B) It has been commented on by countless people.
C) It is difficult to understand without a teacher.
D) It is only used in Baghdad.

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi text that attracted countless commentaries, reflecting its immense scholarly acceptance.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
The Significance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri and Its Commentaries
Prefatory overview of scholarly works on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the importance of Mukhtasar al-Quduri as a foundational Hanafi text and identify three major commentaries and their distinctive features.

Core Idea
Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a core Hanafi text; its many commentaries reflect its central role in fiqh education.

This passage introduces you to the rich tradition of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a concise but comprehensive summary of Hanafi fiqh. Understanding this context helps you appreciate how Hanafi fiqh was transmitted and developed across generations. This knowledge is essential for navigating later Hanafi works and their references.

Guided Path
1
Identify the text being discussed
Recognize that Mukhtasar al-Quduri is a foundational Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam al-Quduri (d. 428 AH).
2
Recognize the purpose of the passage
The author catalogs commentaries and scholarly works to show the text's impact and to encourage further service to these works.
3
Distinguish the types of works
The passage mentions commentaries (shuruh), glosses (hawashi), versifications (manzum), translations, and hadith verifications.
4
Note the oldest and most important commentaries
The oldest is the commentary of Abu Nasr al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), followed by Zad al-Fuqaha' by al-Ispijabi (d. 591 AH) and al-Mujtaba by al-Zahidi (d. 658 AH).
5
Understand the current state of these works
Most commentaries remain unpublished manuscripts; only a few like al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and al-Lubab are printed.

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
شروح مختصر القدوري والأعمال العلمية التي قامت عليه

تقدم أن الله تعالى كتب لمختصر القدوري قبولاً عظيماً عند العلماء وطلابهم وانتشر انتشاراً كبيراً عجيباً، وبارك الله فيه بركة عظمى، وكان من تمام بركته أن العلماء أقبلوا عليه بخدمته علمياً إقبالاً كبيراً، من وجوه متعددة، وذلك نتيجة تدريسهم له، وحاجة طلبة العلم إلى ذلك، فكتبت عليه شروح كثيرة، بل قال الشهاب المرجاني: «قد شرحه خلق لا تُحصى، وذلك فضل الله يؤتيه من يشاء.

وسأذكر فيما يلي ما وقفتُ عليه من أعمال علمية قامت على هذا المختصر المبارك، من شروح خاصة به سواء للكتاب كله أو قطعة منه، أو مؤلفات لعلماء المذهب ممن جاؤوا بعده، فكان المختصر مما ضمنوه في مؤلفاتهم، أو زادوا عليه، وفرعوا عليه.

وكذلك ما وقفتُ عليه مما كتب عليه من حواش أو تعليقات، أو أي خدمات علمية قامت عليه، أو على شروحه، أو تابعة لذلك، من تخريج أحاديثها، أو التعريف بأعلامها، وكذلك الكتب التي نظمت هذا المختصر، والكتب التي ترجمته إلى لغات أخرى، كالتركية والفارسية والألمانية، وغيرها.

ولا أكتفي بذكر اسم صاحب العمل، واسم مؤلفه، بل أذكر مقدمة عمله إن تيسر، ليتبين للقارئ حال هذا العمل، ومنهج مؤلفه وأسلوبه، وقد أذكر منه نماذج مقارنة مع شروح أخرى كتب لها الشهرة، لتتبين قيمة كل عمل، وميزته عن غيره.

كما أني أذكر ما يتيسر لي من وصف هذا العمل، وحجمه، ومكان وجوده إن كان مخطوطاً، مع ذكر طبعاته إن كان مطبوعاً، ونحو هذا.

وهذا كله؛ ليكون القارئ على بينة من الأمر، وليكون حافزاً للقراء الكرام على خدمة هذه الشروح والأعمال العلمية التي لم تُخدم بعد، فإنه لم يطبع إلى الآن من الشروح القديمة للمختصر إلا الجوهرة النيرة، واللباب وطبعة نادرة في قازان بروسيا لخلاصة الدلائل، وأخرى جديدة مغلوطة، وأما باقي الشروح فكلها مخطوطة تستصرخ الهمم العالية لإحيائها وخدمتها ونشرها بين طلاب العلم، ميسرة مُخْرَجةً برونق جميل، ليعم نفعها، والاستفادة منها.

وإن أقدم الشروح وأحسنها هو شرح أبي نصر الأقطع، ت ٤٧٤هـ، تلميذ المؤلف القدوري، ومن أجملها شرح الإسبيجابي، ت ٥٩١ هـ، المسمى زاد الفقهاء، ويليهما شرح نجم الأئمة الزاهدي، ت ٦٥٨ هـ، المسمى: المجتبى، وهو أوسعها تفريعاً
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and the scholarly works based on it

It has been mentioned previously that Allah Almighty granted Mukhtasar al-Quduri immense acceptance among scholars and their students, and it spread widely and remarkably, and Allah blessed it with a great blessing. Part of its complete blessing was that scholars turned to serving it academically with great enthusiasm, from multiple aspects, and that was a result of their teaching it and the need of students of knowledge for that. So many commentaries were written on it. Indeed, al-Shihab al-Marjani said: 'Countless people have commented on it, and that is the favor of Allah which He gives to whom He wills.'

I will mention below what I have come across of scholarly works based on this blessed Mukhtasar, including commentaries specific to it, whether for the entire book or a part of it, or works by scholars of the madhhab who came after him, so the Mukhtasar was among what they included in their works, or added to it, or branched out from it.

Also, what I have come across of glosses or annotations written on it, or any scholarly services based on it, or on its commentaries, or related to that, such as verification of its hadiths, or identification of its notable figures, as well as books that versified this Mukhtasar, and books that translated it into other languages, such as Turkish, Persian, German, and others.

And I do not content myself with mentioning the name of the author of the work and the title of his work, but I mention the introduction of his work if possible, so that the reader may understand the status of this work, the methodology of its author and his style. And I may mention comparative examples with other well-known commentaries to show the value of each work and its distinction from others.

Also, I mention what is feasible for me of a description of this work, its size, its location if it is a manuscript, along with mentioning its printed editions if it is printed, and the like.

All this is so that the reader is well-informed about the matter, and to be an incentive for the honorable readers to serve these commentaries and scholarly works that have not yet been served. For only al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah, and al-Lubab, and a rare edition in Kazan, Russia of Khulasat al-Dala'il, and another new erroneous one have been printed from the old commentaries of the Mukhtasar so far. As for the rest of the commentaries, they are all manuscripts crying out for high ambitions to revive them, serve them, and publish them among students of knowledge, made easy and beautifully presented, so that their benefit and utilization become widespread.

Indeed, the oldest and best of the commentaries is the commentary of Abu Nasr al-Aqta', d. 474 AH, the student of the author al-Quduri. Among the most beautiful is the commentary of al-Ispijabi, d. 591 AH, called Zad al-Fuqaha'. They are followed by the commentary of Najm al-A'immah al-Zahidi, d. 658 AH, called al-Mujtaba, which is the most extensive in terms of branching (fur').
Source pages p. 361

Commentary
This passage is front matter from the introductory chapter of a modern scholarly work cataloging commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, a foundational Hanafi fiqh text. The author begins by noting the great acceptance and blessings Allah granted to al-Quduri's Mukhtasar, which led scholars to produce numerous commentaries and derivative works. He then outlines his plan to list all scholarly works based on the Mukhtasar, including complete or partial commentaries, works of later Hanafi scholars who incorporated it into their writings, glosses and annotations, hadith verification works, biographical works on its transmitters, versifications, and translations. The author will provide details about each work, such as its author, methodology, size, and availability (manuscript or printed). He aims to inform and encourage readers to serve the many unpublished commentaries. He notes that only a few old commentaries have been printed, such as al-Jawharah al-Nayyirah and al-Lubab, while most remain in manuscript form. He identifies the oldest and best commentary as that of Abu Nasr al-Aqta', a student of al-Quduri, followed by al-Ispijabi's Zad al-Fuqaha', and al-Zahidi's al-Mujtaba, which is the most extensive in terms of furu' (subsidiary rulings).

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): A concise Hanafi fiqh manual by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), which became a foundational text for the Hanafi madhhab.
شروح (shuruh): Commentaries explaining and expanding upon the Mukhtasar al-Quduri.
زاد الفقهاء (Zad al-Fuqaha'): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Ispijabi (d. 591 AH), known for its beauty and organization.
المجتبى (al-Mujtaba): A commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by Najm al-A'imma al-Zahidi (d. 658 AH), noted for its extensive treatment of furu'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Sharh Abi Nasr al-Aqta'
C) Zad al-Fuqaha'
D) al-Mujtaba

Key Takeaway
Mukhtasar al-Quduri generated a vast commentarial tradition, highlighting its central role in Hanafi fiqh education and scholarship.

Al-Aqta's Al-Sharh al-Kabir: The First Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri
Biographical and bibliographical introduction to the first commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the significance of al-Aqta's al-Sharh al-Kabir as the first major commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri and identify its author's relationship to al-Quduri.

Core Idea
Al-Aqta's al-Sharh al-Kabir is the earliest major commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, written by a direct student of al-Quduri himself.

This lesson introduces you to the first in a long line of commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, the foundational Hanafi text. You will learn about its author, al-Aqta', and the purpose behind his commentary as expressed in his own introduction. Understanding this work's place helps you appreciate the scholarly tradition that built upon al-Quduri's concise summary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author and his relation to al-Quduri
Determine the full name, death year, and teacher-student connection of the author of al-Sharh al-Kabir.
Al-Aqta' (Ahmad ibn Muhammad) is explicitly identified as a student of al-Quduri.
2
Understand the context of the commentary
Read the introduction snippet to find out who requested the commentary and what specific requests they made regarding its style and content.
The request came from a group of students; they wanted a balanced expansion that includes relied-upon rulings and subsidiary issues.
3
Examine the structure and content
Note the physical description of the manuscript: number of volumes, folios, lines per page, and the date of the copy described.
According to the text: two volumes, about 300 folios, 23 lines per page.
4
Contrast with other works by the same author
Al-Aqta' also wrote a shorter commentary called al-Muqni'. Compare the scope of the two works.
Al-Sharh al-Kabir is described as 'the great commentary', while al-Muqni' is simply mentioned as another commentary.
5
Grasp the significance
Reflect on why this commentary is considered the 'first' and how it fits into the broader Hanafi sharh tradition.
Being the first major commentary by a direct student, it set a precedent for later scholars like al-Marghinani (al-Hidayah).

الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري

وتدليلاً، ثم يليه في الحجم والنفع الشرح المسمى بـ: «السراج الوهاج»، للحدادي، ت٨٠٠هـ ، الذي اختصره في «الجوهرة النيرة». وقد دعتني الكتابة عن شروح القدوري والأعمال التي قامت عليه، إلى تصوير أكبر قدر ممكن من مخطوطات هذه الشروح والسعي للوقوف عليها من هنا وهناك، من قريب ومن بعيد. وقد بلغ عدد هذه الأعمال العلمية بتنوعهـا، قديمها وحديثها (۱۲۲) عملاً ، كلها قامت على خدمة هذا المختصر الصغير المبارك، جزى الله أصحابها عن العلم وأهله خير الجزاء. وفيما يلي أذكر هذه الشروح والأعمال، وما يلزم مـن الكـلام عنها بالتفصيل، مرتباً لها حسب تقدمها الزمني، وفي الأخير أذكر أسماءها مجملةً متتالية حسب حروف المعجم :

۱ - شرح مختصر القدوري للأقطع (الشرح الكبير).

للإمام أحمد بن محمد المعروف بأبي نصر الأقطع المتوفى سنة ٤٧٤هـ ، رحمه الله تعالى، ، وهو تلميذ القدوري "(1)

ولم يُعرف لهذا الشرح الكبير اسم، وله شرح آخر مختصر، يعرف باسم (المقنع)، وسيأتي ذكره بعد هذا.

(۱) له ترجمة في الجواهر المضية ،۳۱۱/۱ ، تاج التراجم ص ١٠٣ ، الوافي بالوفيات ۱۱۸/۸ ، الفوائد البهية ص ٤٠.

وفيما يلي نص مقدمة شرحه الكبير، حيث قال: ... ذكرتُم ـ وفقنا الله وإياكم إلى الصالح والرشاد ـ حاجتكم إلى شرح المختصر الذي عَمِله شيخنا أبو الحسين أحمـد بـن محمـد بـن جعفر القدوري شرحاً لا يخرج عن حد الاختصار، وأنكم رأيـتـم مـا كنتُ ابتدأت به من شرحه للشريف السعيد ضياء الشرف ذي المنصبين أبي الحسين عبد الله بن المطهر بن الحسين بن داود، الناصر لدين الله سبحانه وتعالى، فوجدتموه في غاية الاختصار. وسألتُم أن أبسط القول فيه بعض البسط، وأذكر في كل مسألة من مسائل الكتاب ما يُعتمد عليه، وبه يُستخرج الجواب عن أخواتها من المسائل، وأن ألحق في كل موضع ما يُحتاج إليه من المسائل الظاهرة التي لا يُستغنى عن معرفتها، وما يكون فيه إيضاح لغيرها، قدراً لا يطول به الكتاب، ويعتدل به أوله وآخره، وأن أقتصر من ذكر اختلاف الناس على ما جرت به العادة بذكره في وقتنا. فأجبتكم إلى ذلك، مستعيناً بالله عز وجل في جميع ما أقصده، وراغباً إليه جلت عظمته في التوفيق والعصمة في كـل مـا آتي وأذَرُ، وأن يجعل ما أتوخاه من ذلك له خالصاً، وأن ينفع الناظر فيه به ، وهو عزّ اسمه ولي الإجابة بمنه وكرمه). اهـ

ويقع هذا الشرح في مجلدين، في نحو ٣٠٠ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٣ سطراً، حسب نسخة الظاهرية بدمشق، التي تم نسخها سنة ٨٤٧هـ. وتوجد من هذا الشرح نسخ عديدة، ينظر لهـا الفهرس الشامل
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri

... and for evidence, then next in size and benefit is the commentary called 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by al-Hadadi, d. 800 AH, which he summarized in 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira'. The writing about the commentaries on al-Quduri and the works based on it prompted me to photograph as many manuscripts of these commentaries as possible and to strive to obtain them from here and there, from near and far. The number of these scholarly works, in their diversity, old and new, reached 122 works, all serving this small, blessed summary. May Allah reward their authors on behalf of knowledge and its people with the best reward. Below I mention these commentaries and works, and what needs to be said about them in detail, arranged chronologically, and at the end I mention their names summary-wise in alphabetical order:

1 - Commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta' (al-Sharh al-Kabir).

By Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad, known as Abu Nasr al-Aqta', died 474 AH, may Allah have mercy on him, and he is a student of al-Quduri (1).

This al-Sharh al-Kabir has no known name, and he has another shorter commentary known as 'al-Muqni'', which will be mentioned after this.

(1) His biography is in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya 1/311, Taj al-Tarajim p. 103, al-Wafi bi al-Wafayat 8/118, al-Fawa'id al-Bahiyya p. 40.

Below is the text of the introduction to his al-Sharh al-Kabir, where he said: ... You mentioned – may Allah guide us and you to righteousness and good judgment – your need for a commentary on the summary (Mukhtasar) written by our teacher Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Quduri, a commentary that does not go beyond the limits of conciseness, and that you saw what I had begun of my commentary for the noble, fortunate Diya' al-Sharaf, possessor of two positions, Abu al-Husayn Abdullah ibn al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn ibn Dawud, al-Nasir li-Din Allah, glory be to Him and Exalted, and you found it extremely concise. You asked me to expand the discussion somewhat, to mention in each issue of the book what is relied upon, and with which the answer to its sister issues can be derived, and to append in each place what is needed of the obvious issues whose knowledge is indispensable, and what clarifies others, to an extent that does not lengthen the book and makes its beginning and end balanced, and to limit the mention of differences among people to what is customary to mention in our time. So I responded to you, seeking help from Allah Almighty in all that I intend, and hoping to Him, whose greatness is exalted, for success and protection in all that I do and leave, and that He make what I aim for from that purely for Him, and benefit the one who looks into it. And He, exalted is His name, is the One worthy of response, with His grace and generosity. End quote.

This commentary consists of two volumes, about 300 folios, with 23 lines per page, according to the al-Zahiriyya copy in Damascus, which was copied in 847 AH. There are many copies of this commentary, see the Comprehensive Index.
Source pages p. 363

Commentary
This passage is a front-matter section from al-Lubab fi Sharh al-Quduri, where the author, al-Maydani, reaches the third chapter of his introduction: a detailed listing of the commentaries written on Imam al-Quduri's Mukhtasar. He begins by stating that after mentioning the main commentaries, he will mention the one called 'al-Siraj al-Wahhaj' by al-Hadadi (d. 800 AH), who also abridged it as 'al-Jawhara al-Nayyira'. He then explains his motivation for compiling this list: he photographed many manuscripts and accessed them from various places. The number of works devoted to this concise text, both old and new, reaches 122, all serving this small but blessed summary. He then begins the chronological list with the first commentary: that of al-Aqta' (d. 474 AH), also known as 'al-Sharh al-Kabir'. Al-Aqta' was a student of al-Quduri himself. The large commentary has no specific title; it is simply called 'al-Sharh al-Kabir' (The Great Commentary). Al-Aqta' also wrote a shorter commentary called 'al-Muqni'' which will be mentioned later. Al-Maydani then reproduces the opening of al-Aqta's introduction, which explains the circumstances of its composition: a group of students requested a commentary that is concise yet comprehensive, one that explains each issue with the relied-upon view and allows derivation of answers for similar cases. They also asked that it include necessary subsidiary issues and clarify them, while avoiding excessive length. Al-Aqta' agreed, seeking Allah's help. Finally, al-Maydani describes the physical format of the manuscript: two volumes, about 300 folios, 23 lines per page, based on a copy dated 847 AH in Damascus, and notes that multiple copies exist. This section is purely biographical and bibliographical, providing historical context about the development of Hanafi fiqh literature.

Key Terms
مختصر القدوري (Mukhtasar al-Quduri): The concise legal text by Imam Ahmad ibn Muhammad al-Quduri (d. 428 AH), a standard Hanafi primer.
الشرح الكبير (al-Sharh al-Kabir): The large commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri by al-Aqta', without a specific title, just referred to as 'the great commentary'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Who wrote the commentary known as 'al-Sharh al-Kabir' on Mukhtasar al-Quduri?
A) Al-Hadadi
B) Al-Aqta'
C) Al-Maydani
D) Al-Quduri himself

Key Takeaway
Al-Aqta's al-Sharh al-Kabir, written by a direct student of al-Quduri, is the first major commentary on Mukhtasar al-Quduri, setting the stage for the rich Hanafi sharh tradition.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
6 min
Al-Aqta'i's Commentary: Responding to a Scholarly Need
Author's introduction outlining commentary methodology

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the purpose of al-Aqta'i's expanded commentary and identify three key methodological features he promised to include.

Core Idea
A commentary must expand just enough to be useful without losing focus.

This lesson introduces the large commentary of Izz al-Din al-Aqta'i on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. The author's own preface reveals the motivation: scholars requested a commentary that goes beyond extreme conciseness but remains practical. Al-Aqta'i outlines his methodology, emphasizing reliance on the mu'tamad (relied-upon position), derivation of rulings for similar cases, and inclusion of essential issues without excessive length.

Guided Path
1
Identify the request
Read the author's introduction to see what was requested: a commentary that expands on his earlier concise version but stays within bounds.
The request came from the readers who found his earlier commentary too short.
2
List the promised features
Al-Aqta'i lists four things he agreed to do: (1) mention the mu'tamad in each issue, (2) enable derivation of answers for similar issues, (3) include necessary apparent issues, (4) limit mention of disagreements to what is customary.
These features define the standard for a good Hanafi commentary.
3
Note the balance sought
He aims for a middle path: not too long, with a balanced beginning and end.
This reflects the ideal of wasatiyya (moderation) in scholarly writing.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الفصل الثالث : شروح مختصر القدوري
وفيما يلي نص مقدمة شرحه الكبير، حيث قال: ... ذكرتُم ـ وفقنا الله وإياكم إلى الصالح والرشاد ـ حاجتكم إلى شرح المختصر الذي عَمِله شيخنا أبو الحسين أحمـد بـن محمـد بـن جعفر القدوري شرحاً لا يخرج عن حد الاختصار، وأنكم رأيـتـم مـا كنتُ ابتدأت به من شرحه للشريف السعيد ضياء الشرف ذي المنصبين أبي الحسين عبد الله بن المطهر بن الحسين بن داود، الناصر لدين الله سبحانه وتعالى، فوجدتموه في غاية الاختصار.
وسألتُم أن أبسط القول فيه بعض البسط، وأذكر في كل مسألة من مسائل الكتاب ما يُعتمد عليه، وبه يُستخرج الجواب عن أخواتها من المسائل، وأن ألحق في كل موضع ما يُحتاج إليه من المسائل الظاهرة التي لا يُستغنى عن معرفتها، وما يكون فيه إيضاح لغيرها، قدراً لا يطول به الكتاب، ويعتدل به أوله وآخره، وأن أقتصر من ذكر اختلاف الناس على ما جرت به العادة بذكره في وقتنا.
فأجبتكم إلى ذلك، مستعيناً بالله عز وجل في جميع ما أقصده، وراغباً إليه جلت عظمته في التوفيق والعصمة في كـل مـا آتي وأذَرُ، وأن يجعل ما أتوخاه من ذلك له خالصاً، وأن ينفع الناظر فيه به ، وهو عزّ اسمه ولي الإجابة بمنه وكرمه). اهـ
ويقع هذا الشرح في مجلدين، في نحو ٣٠٠ ورقة، وفي كل صفحة ٢٣ سطراً، حسب نسخة الظاهرية بدمشق، التي تم نسخها سنة ٨٤٧هـ.
وتوجد من هذا الشرح نسخ عديدة، ينظر لهـا الفهرس الشامل للتراث العربي الإسلامي المخطوط (١).
وقد سجل الكتاب لتحقيقه في رسائل جامعية في جامعة الإمام محمد بن سعود في الرياض، وتمت مناقشة الرسالة الأولى منه، بتحقيق الأخ الكريم الأستاذ إبراهيم أكبر، ونال بها درجة الماجستير بمرتبة الامتياز مع التوصية بالطبع.
وقد قال العلامة الكوثري رحمه الله عن هذا الشرح «بأنه أحسن شروح المختصر » (٢).
وقد توسع الأقطع في هذا الشرح في ذكر الأدلة، كما أكثر من التفريع على المسائل، مع ذكره لخلاف الإمام مالك والشافعي، ومناقشة الأدلة، مع الأخذ والرد.
كما اهتم المؤلف بذكر فوارق نُسَخ مختصر القدوري التي وقـف عليها، وبين الصواب منها ، كما صرح بهذا في خاتمة شرحه، فقال: «وقد وجدتُ في أكثر نسخ الأصل خللاً في بعض المسائل، وهـو من الناسخ، وقد أصلحت جميع ذلك على ما يقتضيه مذهب أصحابنا رحمهم الله تعالى». اهـ
وممن كان يحفظ شرح الأقطع هذا، مـا ذكـره القرشي في الجواهر المضية، في ترجمة محمد بن يحيى بـن مـسـلـم القاضي خيري.
Chapter Three: Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri. Below is the text of the introduction to his large commentary, where he said: ... You mentioned – may Allah guide us and you to righteousness and good conduct – your need for a commentary on the Mukhtasar compiled by our Shaykh Abu al-Husayn Ahmad ibn Muhammad ibn Ja'far al-Quduri, a commentary that does not exceed the limits of conciseness, and that you saw what I had initially begun of his commentary for the noble and happy Diya' al-Sharaf, holder of two positions, Abu al-Husayn 'Abd Allah ibn al-Mutahhar ibn al-Husayn ibn Dawud, the supporter of the religion of Allah, and you found it extremely concise. And you asked that I expand the discussion somewhat, and mention in each issue of the book's issues what is relied upon, and by which the answer to similar issues can be derived, and that I append in each place the apparent issues that are needed and whose knowledge cannot be dispensed with, and what clarifies others, to an extent that does not lengthen the book, and makes its beginning and end balanced, and that I restrict the mention of disagreement among people to what is customary to mention in our time. So I responded to you, seeking help from Allah in all that I intend, and desiring His success and protection in all that I do and leave, and that He make what I aim for sincere to Him, and benefit the reader thereby. And He is worthy of response by His favor and generosity. End quote. This commentary is in two volumes, about 300 folios, each page 23 lines, according to the Zahiriyya copy in Damascus, copied in 847 AH. There are many copies of this commentary; see the Comprehensive Index of Arabic Islamic Manuscripts (1). The book has been registered for academic theses at Imam Muhammad ibn Sa'ud University in Riyadh, and the first thesis was discussed, edited by the brother Professor Ibrahim Akbar, who obtained a master's degree with distinction and recommendation for publication. The scholar al-Kawthari said about this commentary: 'It is the best of the commentaries on the Mukhtasar.' Al-Aqta'i expanded in this commentary in citing evidences, and abundantly branched out issues, while mentioning the disagreement of Imam Malik and al-Shafi'i, and discussing evidences with give and take. The author also paid attention to mentioning the differences among copies of Mukhtasar al-Quduri that he came across, and clarified the correct among them, as he stated in the conclusion of his commentary: 'And I found in most copies of the original errors in some issues, and that is from the copyist, and I corrected all of that according to the requirements of the madhhab of our companions, may Allah have mercy on them.' End quote. Among those who memorized this commentary of al-Aqta'i, as mentioned by al-Qurashi in al-Jawahir al-Mudiyya, in the biography of Muhammad ibn Yahya ibn Muslim al-Qadi Khayri.
Source pages p. 364

Commentary
This passage is front matter from a modern study on commentaries of Mukhtasar al-Quduri, specifically introducing the large commentary by Izz al-Din al-Aqta'i. It opens with the chapter heading 'Commentaries on Mukhtasar al-Quduri' and then provides the text of the author's own introduction to his expanded commentary. In that introduction, al-Aqta'i explains that his readers requested a commentary that, while expanding on the original concise work, remains focused and practical. He commits to mentioning the relied-upon position in each issue, enabling the derivation of rulings for similar cases, and to include necessary apparent issues without making the book too long. He also limits mention of scholarly disagreement to what is customary. He then describes the physical description of the manuscript (two volumes, ~300 folios, 23 lines per page) and notes that it was copied in 847 AH. The passage goes on to quote later scholars, such as al-Kawthari, praising this commentary as the best. It highlights the commentary's features: extensive citation of evidence, branching out of issues, engagement with Maliki and Shafi'i positions, and critical correction of discrepancies in manuscript copies of the Mukhtasar. Finally, it mentions that the commentary was memorized by some, as recorded in biographical works.

Key Terms
المعتمد (al-Mu'tamad): The relied-upon position in the Hanafi school for a given issue.
التخريج (al-Takhrij): Deriving rulings for new cases from established principles or analogous issues.
الإختصار (al-Ikhtisar): Conciseness; al-Aqta'i's earlier commentary was extremely concise.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What did al-Aqta'i agree to include in his expanded commentary?
A) The relied-upon position (mu'tamad) in each issue
B) All differences of opinion among all schools
C) A complete history of Hanafi jurisprudence
D) Only the proofs without any rulings

Key Takeaway
Al-Aqta'i's commentary methodology focuses on clarity of the mu'tamad, practical derivation, and balanced length.
